Takbir al-Tashriq and Talbiyah After Salam: Order and Invalidity
Rulings on takbir al-tashriq and talbiyah after salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the correct order for performing missed takbir al-tashriq and talbiyah after salam and identify which actions invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Takbir al-tashriq and talbiyah must follow sajdah sahw; starting with talbiyah invalidates earlier obligations.

In addition to missed sajdahs, a person may have outstanding takbir al-tashriq (wajib takbirs during Tashriq days) and talbiyah (the call of Hajj/Umrah). This lesson covers how these interact with sajdah obligations when all are owed after salam. The key principle is that takbir al-tashriq takes precedence over talbiyah, and both come after sajdah sahw. If one begins with talbiyah, it invalidates the preceding sajdahs and takbir; if one begins with takbir, it is valid but the order is still recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of obligations
Determine if the obligations include sahw, takbir al-tashriq, and/or talbiyah. Each has a specific place in the order.
2
Apply the general rule of mindfulness
If the person is mindful at salam, the prayer terminates and obligations drop? Actually, for takbir and talbiyah, they do not drop regardless of mindfulness; order must still be followed.
The passage says: 'none of that drops from him, whether he is mindful of all or forgetful of all.'
3
Follow the prescribed order
The order is: first sajdah sahw (if owed), then takbir al-tashriq, then talbiyah.
If any sajdah obligations (salbiyyah, tilawah) are also present, they are made up first before sahw.
4
Assess the consequence of incorrect order
If talbiyah is said before sahw and takbir, both sahw and takbir drop (not performed). If talbiyah is said after sahw but before takbir, only takbir drops.
Beginning with talbiyah invalidates the entire sequence and the prayer.
5
Consider the comprehensive case
When all five obligations (salbiyyah, tilawah, sahw, takbir, talbiyah) are present, the order is: make up salbiyyah and tilawah with intention, tashahhud and salam, sajdah sahw, takbir, then talbiyah. Starting with talbiyah invalidates; starting with takbir is valid but not ideal.

تنبيه: لو سلم وعليه تلاوية وسهوية وهو غير ذاكر لهما، أو ذاكر للسهو فقط، لا بـ يعد سلامه قاطعاً، فيسجد للتلاوة، ثم يتشهد لرفعها القعود ويسلم، ثم يسجد للسهو ويتشهد لرفعها التشهد ويسلم، وإن سلم وكان ذاكراً لهما أو للتلاوية فقط كان قاطعاً، وسقطت عنه التلاوية والسهو، لامتناع البناء بسبب القطع، إلا إذا تذكر أنه لم يتشهد، ويسجد للتلاوة وصلاته تامة، وإن سلم وعليه صلبية وسهوية غير ذاكر لهما، أو ذاكراً للسهوية فقط، لم يكن سلامه قاطعاً، ويفعل كالأول، وإن كان ذاكراً لهما وللصلبية خاصة فهو قاطع، فتفسد صلاته، ولو سلم وعليه صلبية وتلاوية وسهوية غير ذاكــر لهنَّ، أو ذاكراً للسهوية لم يقطع ويقضي الأولين مرتباً الأول فالأول، وهـو يـفـيـد وجـوب النيـة في المقضى من السجدات، ثم يتشهد ويسلّم ثم يسجد للسهو. انتهى. قلت: نـص عـلـى لــزوم النيـة في المقضى من السجدات، في ( التجنيس قال : لو سلم في الفجر وعليه سهو فسجد له، ثم تكلم فتذكر أنه ترك صلبية من الركعة الأولى فسدت صلاته، لأنها صارت ديناً في ذمتـه وانـعـدمـت نـيـة القضـاء، وإن كانت من الركعة الثانية لا تفسد إلا في رواية عن أبي يوسف؛ لأنها لم تصـر ديناً في ذمته، فنابت سجدة السهو عن الصلبية، ولو كانت المسألة بحالها، إلا أنه لما سلم للفجر تذكر أن عليـه سجدة تلاوة فسجد لها، ثم تكلم، ثم تذكر أن عليه صلبية فصلاته فاسدة في الوجهين؛ لأن سجدة التلاوة دين عليه فانصرفت نيته إلى قضاء الدين فلا تنصرف السجدة إلى غير القضاء. انتهى. ثم قال الكمال: وإن كان ذاكراً للصلبية أو التلاوية فسدت، وكان سلامه قاطعاً، وإذا سلم وعليه السهو وتكبير التشريق والتلبية لا يسقط عنه ذلك كله، سواء كان ذاكراً للكل، أو ساهياً عن الكل، فيقدم السهو، ثم تكبير التشريق، ثم التلبية، ولو قدم التلبية قبل السهو [ سقطت ] سجدتا السهو والتكبير، ولو لبى قبل التكبير يسقط التكبير، ولو سلم وعليه صلبية وتلاوية وسهو وتكبير التشريق والتلبية، غير ذاكر لها، فعل ذلك على هذا الترتيب، ولو بدأ بالتلبية فسدت، ولو بالتكبير لا تفسد.
Warning: If he gives salam and has upon him [obligations of] tilawah and sahw, and he is not mindful of both, or he is mindful only of sahw, his salam is not considered terminating. So he performs sajdah for tilawah, then performs tashahhud for its sitting and gives salam, then performs sajdah for sahw and performs tashahhud for its tashahhud and gives salam. If he gives salam and is mindful of both or of tilawah only, his salam is terminating, and the tilawah and sahw drop from him, due to the impossibility of building because of the termination, except if he remembers that he did not perform tashahhud, and he performs sajdah for tilawah and his prayer is complete. If he gives salam and has upon him [obligations of] salbiyyah and sahw, not mindful of both, or mindful only of sahw, his salam is not terminating, and he does as the first. If he is mindful of both and especially salbiyyah, it is terminating and his prayer is invalid. If he gives salam and has upon him salbiyyah, tilawah, and sahw, not mindful of them, or mindful of sahw, he does not terminate and he makes up the first two in order, the first before the second. This indicates the obligation of intention in the made-up sajdahs. Then he performs tashahhud and gives salam, then performs sajdah for sahw. End. I say: He textually stated the necessity of intention in the made-up sajdahs in al-Tajnis. He said: If he gives salam in Fajr and has upon him sahw, and he performs sajdah for it, then speaks, then remembers that he left a salbiyyah from the first rak'ah, his prayer is invalid because it becomes a debt upon him and the intention of making up was absent. If it was from the second rak'ah, it is not invalid except in a narration from Abu Yusuf; because it did not become a debt upon him, so the sajdah al-sahw suffices for the salbiyyah. If the case is the same, but when he gave salam for Fajr he remembered that he had a tilawah sajdah, so he performed it, then spoke, then remembered that he had a salbiyyah, his prayer is invalid in both cases; because the tilawah sajdah is a debt upon him, so his intention turned to paying the debt, and the sajdah does not turn to other than the debt. End. Then al-Kamal said: If he is mindful of the salbiyyah or tilawah, it is invalid and his salam is terminating. If he gives salam and has upon him sahw and takbir al-tashriq and talbiyah, none of that drops from him, whether he is mindful of all or forgetful of all. He gives precedence to sahw, then takbir al-tashriq, then talbiyah. If he gives talbiyah before sahw, the two sajdahs of sahw and the takbir drop. If he performs talbiyah before takbir, the takbir drops. If he gives salam and has upon him salbiyyah, tilawah, sahw, takbir al-tashriq, and talbiyah, not mindful of them, he does that in this order. If he begins with talbiyah, it is invalid; if with takbir, it is not invalid.
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage is a detailed set of cases (furu') concerning a person who gives salam while various obligatory actions remain upon him. These include sajdah tilawah (prostration of recitation), sajdah sahw (prostration for forgetfulness), and missed fard prostrations (salbiyyah), as well as takbir al-tashriq and talbiyah. The key factors are whether the person was mindful (dhakir) of these obligations at the time of salam and the order of performance. The passage begins with a warning (tanbih) that if one has both tilawah and sahw and is not mindful of either, or only mindful of sahw, the salam is not terminating, meaning the prayer's sanctity remains. The person then performs the missed actions in a specific order: first sajdah tilawah with its tashahhud and salam, then sajdah sahw with its tashahhud and salam. If he is mindful of both or of tilawah only, the salam becomes terminating, and both sajdahs drop, except if he remembers not having performed tashahhud. If a fard rukn (salbiyyah) is missed along with sahw, similar distinctions apply. The passage then cites al-Tajnis with a specific example: a person who forgets a fard sajdah (salbiyyah) from the first rak'ah after having performed sajdah sahw and then speaking. The sajdah sahw cannot compensate for the fard sajdah because the fard sajdah becomes a debt requiring specific intention. If the missed fard sajdah is from the second rak'ah, according to one narration from Abu Yusuf, sajdah sahw may suffice. But if one has a tilawah sajdah after salam, then speaks, then remembers a salbiyyah, the prayer is invalid because the tilawah sajdah was a debt and the intention for the salbiyyah was not present. Finally, the passage covers cases where multiple obligations include takbir al-tashriq and talbiyah, which have their own order of precedence. The overall principle is that the order must be followed, and memory at the time of salam determines whether compensation is possible.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbīr al-tashrīq): The takbirs recited after fard prayers during the days of Tashriq (11th-13th of Dhul Hijjah).
تلبية (talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited during Hajj and Umrah. When missed after salam, it must be said in order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person gives salam and has outstanding sajdah sahw, takbir al-tashriq, and talbiyah, and is not mindful, what is the correct order?
A) Takbir, then talbiyah, then sajdah sahw.
B) Sajdah sahw, then talbiyah, then takbir.
C) Sajdah sahw, then takbir, then talbiyah.
D) Talbiyah, then sajdah sahw, then takbir.

Key Takeaway
The order for fulfilling missed obligations after salam is: first sajdah sahw, then takbir al-tashriq, then talbiyah; starting with talbiyah invalidates the prayer.

When Does Salaam Cut the Prayer? Ruling on Multiple Owed Sujud
Expansion on effects of taslim when owing multiple sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the scenarios where taslim cuts the prayer and state the correct order for performing multiple owed prostrations according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Taslim cuts prayer only if mindful of a missed fard; forgetful taslim preserves sanctity for makeup.

This lesson examines a detailed Hanafi ruling on what happens when a person says the final salaam (taslim) while still owing various types of prostrations—salibiyya, tilawa, or sahw. The key is whether the person is mindful of the debt at the time of taslim. We will walk through the scenarios and learn the specific order for performing these prostrations when the taslim is not cutting.

Guided Path
1
Find the core principle: Forgetting vs. Remembering
Examine the passage's opening: taslim does not cut if the person has not turned or spoken, and then the distinction is made between being mindful or forgetful of owed prostrations. The ruling hinges on awareness at the moment of taslim.
The intention to cut the prayer is void if the person is forgetful, as the sanctity remains.
2
Categorize the owed prostrations by type
Identify salibiyya (obligatory, missed from a rak'ah), tilawa (recitation), and sahw (forgetfulness). Note that salibiyya is a fard of the prayer, while tilawa and sahw are not part of the essence. This classification determines whether the prayer becomes invalid when mindful.
A missed salibiyya becomes a 'debt in the liability' if from the first rak'ah, requiring intention.
3
Apply the rule to the simplest combination: tilawa and sahw
Walk through the tanbih: if only tilawa and sahw are owed and the person is forgetful, taslim does not cut. He performs tilawa first, then tashahhud and taslim, then sahw, then tashahhud and taslim. If mindful of both, taslim cuts and both are dropped.
The specific order is crucial: tilawa before sahw.
4
Extend to salibiyya and sahw, noting the intra-Hanafi dispute
If salibiyya and sahw are owed and the person is forgetful of both (or only mindful of sahw), taslim does not cut. He performs salibiyya first (with intention if from first rak'ah), then sahw. The text cites al-Tajnis: if salibiyya is from the first rak'ah, it becomes a debt; if from the second, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say sahw suffices, but Abu Yusuf disagrees.
This dispute affects whether the prayer remains valid or must be repeated.
5
Analyze multiple obligations including takbir and talbiya
The passage adds takbir al-tashriq and talbiya as additional obligations. When all are owed and the person is forgetful, the order is: first the prostrations (salibiyya, tilawa, sahw) in order, then takbir, then talbiya. Starting with talbiya invalidates; starting with takbir does not.
This demonstrates the hierarchy of obligations in terms of precedence.

As long as he has not turned away from the qibla or spoken... and that is the prostration of forgetfulness, so his intention (to cut) is void. And we restricted the action to being not owed by him, to refute what is said: this is coupled with action, which is the taslim, so he prostrates for forgetfulness. (As long as he has not turned away from the qibla, or spoken) for these two invalidate the tahrima. And it is said: he is not cut by turning as long as he does not speak, or exit the mosque, as in al-Durar from al-Nihaya. Contrary to if he leaves an obligatory prostration (salibiyya) or a fard and says taslim while remembering it, then his prayer is invalid, because it is performed in the reality of prayer, and it has been invalidated by deliberate taslim. As for the prostration of forgetfulness, it is performed in the sanctity of prayer, which remains, and the intention of cutting is void due to what we mentioned. A note: If he says taslim while he owes tilawa and sahw, and he is not mindful of both, or he is mindful only of the sahw, then his taslim is not considered cutting. So he prostrates for tilawa, then recites tashahhud for its raising (the sitting) and says taslim, then prostrates for sahw and recites tashahhud for its raising (the tashahhud) and says taslim. And if he says taslim while mindful of both or only of tilawa, then he is cutting, and both the tilawa and sahw are dropped, because building is prevented due to the cut. And if he says taslim while he owes salibiyya, tilawa, and sahw, not mindful of any, or mindful only of the sahw, he does not cut, and he performs the first two in order, first then first, and that necessitates the obligation of intention in the makeup of prostrations. And if it was from the second rak'ah, it is not invalid except in a narration from Abu Yusuf, because it did not become a debt in his liability, so the sajdah of sahw served for the salibiyya. And if the case is the same, except that when he said taslim for Fajr he remembered that he owed a tilawa sajdah, so he prostrated for it, then spoke, then remembered that he owed a salibiyya – his prayer is invalid in both ways, because the tilawa sajdah is a debt on him, so his intention turned to repaying the debt, so the sajdah does not turn to other than the qada. End. Then al-Kamal said: And if he is mindful of the salibiyya or tilawa, it is invalid, and his taslim is cutting. And if he says taslim while he owes sahw and takbir al-tashriq and talbiya, none of that is dropped, whether he is mindful of all or forgetful of all. He gives priority to sahw, then takbir al-tashriq, then talbiya. And if he gives priority to talbiya before sahw, the two sajdas of sahw and takbir are dropped. And if he says talbiya before takbir, the takbir is dropped. And if he says taslim while he owes salibiyya, tilawa, sahw, takbir al-tashriq, and talbiya, not mindful of them, he does them in this order, and if he begins with talbiya it is invalid, and if with takbir it is not invalid.
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on a matn concerning the effects of saying taslim while one owes various types of prostrations (sajdah). It opens by explaining that the intention to cut prayer is voided by the act of sahw prostration as long as the person does not turn from the qibla or speak. The author then clarifies that turning and speaking invalidate the tahrima (sanctity of prayer), but some say turning alone does not cut without speaking or leaving the mosque. He distinguishes between leaving an obligatory prostration (salibiyya) or a fard rak'ah while remembering – this invalidates the prayer because the s alibiyya is part of the essence of prayer and deliberate taslim breaks it. In contrast, sahw prostration is done within the remaining sanctity of prayer. The main note (tanbih) lists scenarios when a person makes taslim while owing tilawa (prostration for recitation) and/or sahw. If forgetful, the taslim is not cutting, and the person performs the owed prostrations in a specific order: first tilawa with tashahhud and taslim, then sahw with tashahhud and taslim. If mindful, the taslim cuts and the owed prostrations are dropped. The commentary then cites al-Tajnis to emphasize the need for intention when making up prostrations, narrating a case from Abu Yusuf where there is an intra-Hanafi difference: if a missed salibiyya is from the first rak'ah, it becomes a debt requiring explicit intention; if from the second, sahw can substitute. Al-Kamal adds a ruling about combining sahw with takbir al-tashriq and talbiya, giving priority to sahw. The passage concludes with the order when all three plus takbir and talbiya are owed.

Key Terms
صلبية (salibiyya): An obligatory prostration (sajda) missed from a rak'ah, which must be made up.
تلاوية (tilaawiya): Prostration of recitation (sajda tilawa) owed due to reciting a verse of sajda.
سهوية (sahwiyya): Prostration of forgetfulness (sajda sahw) owed due to a mistake in prayer.
دين في الذمة (dayn fi al-dhimma): A debt in the liability, meaning an obligation that must be fulfilled with specific intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person says taslim while he owes a sajdah salibiyya from the first rak'ah and he is mindful of it, what is the ruling regarding his prayer?
A) His prayer is valid and he must make up the sajda with intention.
B) His prayer is invalid and he must repeat it.
C) His prayer is valid if he does sahw prostration.
D) His prayer is valid but the sajda is dropped.

Key Takeaway
Taslim cuts the prayer only when one is mindful of a missed fard; forgetfulness preserves the prayer's sanctity for making up obligations.

Forgetful Taslim Does Not Invalidate Prayer: Completion and Sujud Sahw Required
Ruling on a person who mistakenly thinks he completed prayer and makes taslim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that forgetful taslim does not invalidate prayer and state the conditions for sujud sahw when mistakenly completing early.

Core Idea
Forgetful taslim is a dhikr, not an exit—prayer continues; deliberate misbelief breaks it.

A common mistake in prayer is to believe you have finished and say taslim, only to realize you missed rak'ahs. This lesson explores the Hanafi distinction between forgetful and deliberate taslim, based on the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn. You'll learn when you can simply continue and when the prayer is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Initial Ruling
The passage begins with a person praying a 4 or 3-rak'ah prayer who has a wahm (preponderance of error) that he completed it and says taslim. The initial ruling: if he then knows he prayed only two rak'ahs, he completes the prayer and does sujud sahw.
Note the term 'wahm' – stronger belief of being wrong, not certainty.
2
Examine the Dalil and Its Wajh al-Dalalah
The author cites the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn: the Prophet ﷺ made taslim forgetfully, then completed. The wajh al-dalalah is that the action proves forgetful taslim does not invalidate; the prayer can be resumed.
The proof is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut), but it is relied upon here.
3
Distinguish Forgetful vs. Deliberate Taslim
The passage contrasts forgetful taslim with deliberate taslim under mistaken beliefs (e.g., thinking one is a traveler). The latter invalidates because the intent was to exit.
Key difference: intention at the moment of taslim. Forgetful = no intent to exit.
4
Analyze the Scenario of Long Reflection
If the person sits reflecting without taslim for as long as performing a rukn, then sujud sahw becomes wajib because a wajib (standing for next rak'ah) was delayed. Shorter reflection requires no sahw.
This is a detailed condition for sujud sahw when the delay is significant.
5
Apply the Rule to Similar Cases
The passage mentions similar scenarios: if reflection distracts from a wajib or from wudu after hadath due to doubt, sujud sahw may be owed. This reinforces that the ruling is based on the principle of forgetfulness (sahw).
The underlying principle is that forgetful acts do not break prayer unless accompanied by deliberate intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ولو توهَّم) الوهم: رجحان جهة الخطأ، والظن رجحان جهة الصواب، مُصَلِّ رُباعيَّةٌ) من الفرائض (أو ثلاثية) ولو فرضاً عملياً، وهـو الوتر ( أنَّه أتمها ) ، أي الصلاة فسلَّمَ ، ثمَّ عَلِمَ ) قبل إتيانه بمناف ( أنَّه صلَّى رَكْعَتين) فقط، أو عـلــم أنــه ترك سجدة صلبية أو تلاوية بعد سلامه ناسياً (أتمها ) أي : الصلاة، وسَجَدَ للسهو)، لما روي « أنَّه عليه الصلاة والسلام فَعَلَ كَذَلِكَ فِي حَدِيْثِ ذِي اليَدَيْنِ ) ) ولأن السلام ساهياً لا يبطل صلاته، لـكـونـه دعاء من وجه، بخلاف ما إذا [ سلم ] على ظن أنه مسافر، أو على ظن أنها الجمعة، أو كان قريب عهد بالإسلام فظن أن غير الرباعي ثنائياً أو كان في صلاة العشاء فظنها التراويح، حيث تبطل صلاته كما قدمناه لأنه [ سلام ] عمد، (وإن) توهم الإتمام وهو جالس، و (طال تفكره، ولم يُسلّمْ حَتَّى استيقن بما بقي من صلاته، وإن هذا هو الجلوس الأول، (إنْ كانَ زائداً عن التشهد ) (قَدْرَ أَداءِ رُكْنِ وَجَبَ عليه سجود السهو )، لتأخيره واجب القيام للثالثة (وإلاً) أي: إن لم يكن قدر أداء ركن (لا) يسجد للسهو، وكذا إذا شغله التفكر عن أداء واجب بقدر ركن، أو شغله عن الوضوء بعد سبق الحدث لشكه أنه صلى ثلاثاً أو أربعاً يجب السهو وإلا فلا كذا في « التجنيس والمزيد ».
And if a person praying a four-rak'ah or three-rak'ah prayer has a wahm (preponderance of error) that he completed it, and he says taslim, then knows that he prayed only two rak'ahs, he completes it and prostrates for sahw. And if his reflection becomes long and he does not say taslim until he becomes certain, then if it was the extent of performing a rukn, sujud sahw is wajib; otherwise not. And he must repeat it after doing these things, as in al-Fath. (And if he has a wahm) Wahm is preponderance of the side of error, and zann is preponderance of the side of correctness, a person praying a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer or a three-rak'ah, even if it is a practical fard, which is witr, (that he completed it) meaning the prayer, so he said taslim, then he knows (before doing anything forbidden) that he prayed only two rak'ahs, or he knows that he left a salibiyya or tilawa after his taslim forgetfully, (he completes it) meaning the prayer, and prostrates for sahw, due to the narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did so in the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn, and because taslim forgetfully does not invalidate his prayer, as it is a kind of supplication. Contrary to if he said taslim thinking he is a traveler, or thinking it is Friday, or he was a new Muslim thinking a non-four-rak'ah prayer is two, or he was in 'isha prayer thinking it is tarawih, where his prayer is invalid as we have presented, because it is a deliberate taslim. (And if) he has a wahm of completion while sitting, and his reflection becomes long, and he does not say taslim until he becomes certain of what remains of his prayer, and that this is the first sitting, (if it was more than the tashahhud) (the extent of performing a rukn, sujud sahw is wajib) because he delayed the wajib of standing for the third rak'ah, (otherwise) i.e., if it was not the extent of performing a rukn, (he does not) prostrate for sahw. Similarly, if his reflection distracts him from performing a wajib to the extent of a rukn, or distracts him from wudu after hadath due to doubt whether he prayed three or four, then sujud sahw is owed, otherwise not, as in al-Tajnis and al-Mazid.
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of a person who mistakenly believes he has completed his prayer and makes taslim, only to realize he has not. The author explains that if the taslim was done forgetfully (sahwan), it does not invalidate the prayer, and he may complete the remaining rak'ahs and perform sujud sahw. This is based on the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn, where the Prophet ﷺ made taslim during prayer due to forgetfulness and then completed. The key difference is intent: if the taslim was deliberate under a mistaken belief (like thinking one is a traveler), it cuts the prayer. The author also discusses a scenario where the person sits after taslim reflecting, without saying it, and wonders if he needs sahw. If his reflection lasts as long as performing a rukn (e.g., long time), he must do sujud sahw because he delayed the wajib of standing. If the reflection is shorter, no sahw is needed. He further mentions that if the reflection distracts from a wajib or from wudu after hadath due to doubt about rak'ahs, sujud sahw may be required. The passage emphasizes the importance of intention and the distinction between wahm (preponderance of error) and zann (preponderance of correctness).

Key Terms
وهم (wahm): Preponderance of error, i.e., a stronger belief that one is mistaken.
ظن (zann): Preponderance of correctness, stronger belief that one is correct.
سلام ساهياً (salam sahiyan): Taslim uttered forgetfully, without intent to exit prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must repeat the entire prayer.
B) He stands and completes the third rakah, then prostrates for sahw.
C) His prayer is valid as two rakahs; he does nothing.
D) He must perform sujud sahw only, without completing the rakah.

Key Takeaway
A forgetful taslim does not invalidate prayer; the person stands, completes, and performs sujud sahw.

Ruling on Wahm in Prayer: Completion and Sajdah al-Sahw
Ruling on wahm in prayer and sajdah al-sahw with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person mistakenly says taslim due to wahm and explain the proof from the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn.

Core Idea
Forgetful taslim does not invalidate the prayer; complete the missed units and perform sajdah al-sahw.

In prayer, forgetfulness can lead to errors like mistakenly ending the prayer early. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on such forgetful taslim (saying the final salutation) when it arises from wahm (preponderance of error). You will learn that the prayer remains valid, the missed rak'ahs must be completed, and sajdah al-sahw compensates for the forgetfulness. The proof is the well-known hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn, which demonstrates the Prophet's own practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is forgetfully saying taslim before completing the prayer due to wahm (thinking one has finished). The ruling is that the prayer is not invalidated; instead, the person must complete the remaining rak'ahs and then perform sajdah al-sahw.
This applies whether the prayer is fard or wajib (e.g., witr).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) mistakenly said taslim after two rak'ahs, then completed the prayer and performed sajdah al-sahw.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action shows that forgetful taslim does not exit the prayer; it remains in effect. Therefore, completion and sajdah are required.
The taslim is considered a supplication (du'a) from one perspective, which is why it does not invalidate.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that any taslim before completion invalidates the prayer entirely, regardless of forgetfulness.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between forgetful and deliberate taslim.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (relied upon for fatwa) because it directly follows the explicit sunnah and avoids hardship.
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَو توهَّمَ مُصَلِّ رُباعيَّةً أو ثلاثية أنَّه أتها، فسلَّمَ، ثمَّ عَلِمَ أنه صلى ركعتين أمها، وسَجَدَ للسَّهو وإِنْ طَالَ تفكره، ولم يُسلّم حتَّى استيقنَ إِنْ كانَ قَدْرَ أَداءِ رُكْنِ وَجَبَ عليه سجود السهو وإلا لا. (٢) ويجب عليه إعادته بعد فعل هذه الأشياء، كذا في «الفتح». (ولو توهـم) الوهـم: رجحان) جهـة الخطأ، والظن رجحان جهة الصواب، مُصَلِّ رُباعيَّةٌ) من الفرائض (أو ثلاثية) ولو فرضاً عملياً، وهـو الوتر ( أنَّه أتمها ) ، أي الصلاة فسلَّمَ ، ثمَّ عَلِمَ ) قبل إتيانه بمناف ( أنَّه صلَّى رَكْعَتين) فقط، أو عـلــم أنــه ترك سجدة صلبية أو تلاوية بعد سلامه ناسياً (أتمها ) أي : الصلاة، وسَجَدَ للسهو)، لما روي « أنَّه عليه الصلاة والسلام فَعَلَ كَذَلِكَ فِي حَدِيْثِ ذِي اليَدَيْنِ ) ) ولأن السلام ساهياً لا يبطل صلاته، لـكـونـه دعاء من وجه، بخلاف ما إذا [ سلم ] على ظن أنه مسافر، أو على ظن أنها الجمعة، أو كان قريب عهد بالإسلام فظن أن غير الرباعي ثنائياً أو كان في صلاة العشاء فظنها التراويح، حيث تبطل صلاته كما قدمناه لأنه [ سلام ] عمد، (وإن) توهم الإتمام وهو جالس، و (طال تفكره، ولم يُسلّمْ حَتَّى استيقن بما بقي من صلاته، وإن هذا هو الجلوس الأول، (إنْ كانَ زائداً عن التشهد ) (قَدْرَ أَداءِ رُكْنِ وَجَبَ عليه سجود السهو )، لتأخيره واجب القيام للثالثة (وإلاً) أي: إن لم يكن قدر أداء ركن (لا) يسجد للسهو، وكذا إذا شغله التفكر عن أداء واجب بقدر ،ركن، أو شغله عن الوضوء بعد سبق الحدث لشكه أنه صلى ثلاثاً أو أربعاً يجب السهو وإلا فلا كذا في « التجنيس والمزيد ».
And if a praying person supposes (with preponderance of error) in a four-rak'ah or three-rak'ah prayer that he completed it, and he says the taslim, then he knows that he prayed only two rak'ahs, he completes it and performs prostration of forgetfulness. And if his thought was prolonged and he did not say the taslim until he became certain, if it was the measure of performing a pillar, prostration of forgetfulness is obligatory upon him; otherwise not. (2) It is obligatory for him to repeat after doing these things, as in al-Fath. (And if he supposes) al-wahm: preponderance of error, and al-zann: preponderance of correctness, a praying person of a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer or three-rak'ah, even if practically supererogatory which is witr, that he completed it, i.e., the prayer, and he said taslim, then he knows before doing something contradictory that he prayed only two rak'ahs, or he knows that he left a prostration of the prayer or recitation after his taslim forgetfully, he completes it, i.e., the prayer, and prostrates for forgetfulness, due to the narration that the Prophet, peace be upon him, did likewise in the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn, and because taslim forgetfully does not invalidate his prayer, as it is a supplication from one perspective, contrary to if he says taslim thinking he is a traveler, or thinking it is Friday, or he is new to Islam and thinks that a non-four-rak'ah prayer is two rak'ahs, or he was in the 'isha prayer and thought it was tarawih, where his prayer is invalidated as we have presented because it is deliberate taslim. (And if) he supposes completion while sitting, and his thought is prolonged, and he does not say taslim until he is certain of what remains of his prayer, and that this is the first sitting, if it exceeds the tashahhud by the measure of performing a pillar, prostration of forgetfulness is obligatory upon him, due to delaying the obligatory standing for the third rak'ah; and if not, i.e., if it was not the measure of performing a pillar, he does not prostrate for forgetfulness. Likewise, if his thought prevented him from performing an obligatory act by the measure of a pillar, or it prevented him from performing ablution after the occurrence of an impurity due to his doubt whether he prayed three or four rak'ahs, then prostration of forgetfulness is obligatory; otherwise not, as in al-Tajnīs and al-Mazīd.
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn. The author explains the case of wahm (preponderance of error) in prayer. When a person mistakenly thinks they have completed their prayer but only prayed two rak'ahs, they must complete the remaining rak'ahs and then perform sajdah al-sahw. The key condition is that the taslim was said forgetfully, not deliberately. Deliberate taslim based on mistaken belief (e.g., thinking it was a different prayer) invalidates the prayer. The passage also discusses a scenario where the person does not say taslim but sits thinking they have finished, and their thought is prolonged. If the delay in standing for the next rak'ah equals the time of performing a pillar (like a prostration), then sajdah al-sahw is obligatory due to delaying a wajib. Otherwise, no sajdah is required. This ruling is based on the principle that forgetful taslim does not break the prayer because it contains an element of supplication. The proof is the sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn, where he mistakenly said taslim after two rak'ahs, then completed the prayer and performed sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms
وهم (wahm): Preponderance of error, where the likelihood of mistake outweighs correctness. In this text, it is defined as rujhan jihat al-khata'.
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, such as missing a wajib or adding/delaying an element forgetfully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) He only performs sajdah al-sahw without adding rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
Forgetful taslim due to wahm does not invalidate the prayer; complete the missed units and perform sajdah al-sahw.

When Doubt in Rak'ahs Invalidates Prayer
Ruling on when doubt in rak'ah count invalidates prayer and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between invalidating and non-invalidating doubt in rak'ah count by applying the Hanafi conditions of 'first doubt' and 'non-habitual doubt'.

Core Idea
Only first-time or non-habitual doubt in rak'ahs invalidates prayer; habitual doubt requires acting on certainty.

Doubt (shakk) during prayer can be unsettling, but not every doubt forces you to restart. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a person encountering doubt for the first time—or rarely—and someone who frequently forgets. Join us as we unpack the conditions and the intra-Hanafi debate about what constitutes 'first doubt' and how to handle it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and basic ruling
The passage states that prayer becomes invalid due to doubt in the number of rak'ahs before completion, but only under specific conditions. Recognize that the ruling is batil (invalid) under those conditions.
The act is the prayer; the cause is shakk (equal hesitation).
2
Locate the conditions for invalidation
Two conditions are given: (1) the doubt occurs before completing the prayer, and (2) it is either the first doubt the person has ever experienced (after maturity) OR doubt is not habitual for him. Note the 'or' linking the two sub-conditions.
Habitual doubt means the person regularly experiences doubt in prayers.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Fakhr al-Islam and Ibn al-Fadl interpret 'first doubt' as the first in this specific prayer. Imam al-Sarakhsi interprets it as doubt being non-habitual (i.e., not a regular occurrence). Identify which view is followed by the matn (it combines both with 'or').
The difference affects whether a person with a history of rare doubt must repeat.
4
Examine the dalil and its restriction
The hadith 'When any of you doubts... let him start over' is cited. Understand that it is restricted to first/non-habitual doubt based on another narration and the principle of avoiding hardship.
The imperative 'falyastaqbil' indicates obligation, but the restriction comes from combining proof texts.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a first-time doubter must repeat the entire prayer; a habitual doubter acts on what he is certain of (usually the lesser number) and continues without repeating.
This prevents unnecessary hardship for those prone to doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في الشك في الصلاة والطهارة. تَبْطُلُ الصَّلاةُ بالشَّكُ) وهو تساوي الأمرين، ( في عددِ رَكَعَاتِها) كالتردد بين ثلاث وثنتين، ( إذا كان ذلك الشك (قبل إكمالها)، وكان أيضاً (وهو) أي: الشك (أوّلُ ما عَرَضَ له منَ الشَّكُ) بعد بلوغه في صلاة ما، وهذا قول أكثر المشايخ، وقال فخر الإسلام أول ما عرض له في هذه الصلاة، واختاره ابن الفضل، وذهب الإمام السرخسي إلى أن المعنى أن السهو ليس بعادة له، لا أنه لم يسه في عمره قط، فحكمه حكم من ابتدأه الشك، فلذا قال (أو كان الشَّكُ غـيـر عادة له) فتبطل به لقوله : ( إِذَا شَكَ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي صَلاتِهِ أَنَّهُ كَمْ صَلَّى، فَلْيَسْتَقْبِل الصَّلاةَ ) وقد حمل على ما إذا كان أول شك عرض له، لما سنذكره من الرواية الأخرى، ولأنه قادر على إسقاط ما عليه من الفرض بيقين من غير مشقة، فيلزمه ذلك، كما لو شك أنه صلى أو لم يصل والوقت باق فإنه يلزمه أن يصلي، كما في «الفتح»، و«التبيين» (فلـو شـك بعد سلامه) أو بعد جلوسه قدر التشهد قبل السلام، أثلاثاً صلى أو أربعاً لا شيء عليه، و ( لا يُعتبر) شـكـه حملاً لحاله على الصلاح، كما في البحر، عن المحيط، ( إلا إن كان قد تيقّنَ بالتَّرْكِ)، فيعيد صلاته إن أتى بمناف بعد السلام، وإلا أتى بالمتروك ويسجد للسهو، وإذا تيقن ترك ركن وشك في تعيينه، قالوا: يسجد سجدة واحدة ثم يقعد، ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة بسجدتين ثم يقعد ثم يسجد للسهو، ولو أخبره عدل بعد السلام أنه نقص من صلاته ركعة، وعند المصلي أنه أتم لا يلتفت إلى إخباره، وإن شك في صدقه وكذبه فعن محمد : أنه يعيد احتياطاً، وإن أخبره عدلان لا يعتبر شكه، ويجب الأخذ بقولهما وإن لم يكن المخبر عدلاً لا يقبل قوله، ولو اختلف الإمام والمؤتمون فقالوا: ثلاثاً، وقال: أربعاً، إن كان على يقين لا يأخذ بقولهم وإلا أخذ، وإن اختلف القوم، والإمام مع فريق، أخذ بقوله،
Chapter on doubt in prayer and purification. The prayer becomes invalid due to doubt—which is equality of two matters—in the number of its rak'ahs, like hesitation between three and two, if that doubt occurs before completing it, and also if it is the first doubt that occurred to him after reaching maturity in a particular prayer. This is the saying of most mashayikh. Fakhr al-Islam said: the first doubt that occurred to him in this prayer. Ibn al-Fadl chose this. Imam al-Sarakhsi held that the meaning is that forgetfulness is not a habit for him, not that he never forgot in his entire life. So his ruling is like one who experiences doubt for the first time. Hence he said: or the doubt is not habitual for him. So it invalidates due to his saying: 'When any of you doubts in his prayer how many he has prayed, let him start the prayer anew.' This is interpreted as when it is the first doubt that occurred to him, due to the other narration we will mention. And because he is able to discharge the obligation upon him with certainty without hardship, so it is incumbent upon him, just as if he doubts whether he prayed or not while time remains, then he must pray, as in al-Fath and al-Tabyin. (If he doubts after his taslim) or after his sitting the measure of tashahhud before taslim, whether he prayed three or four, nothing is upon him. And his doubt is not considered, interpreting his state as correct, as in al-Bahr from al-Muhit. (Except if he is certain of omission), then he repeats his prayer if he did something contradictory after taslim, otherwise he performs the omitted act and prostrates for forgetfulness. If he is certain of leaving a pillar but doubts which one, they said: he prostrates one prostration then sits, then stands and prays one rak'ah with two prostrations, then sits, then prostrates for forgetfulness. If a trustworthy person informs him after taslim that he missed a rak'ah, but the worshipper thinks he completed, he does not pay attention to his information. If he doubts his truthfulness, from Muhammad: he repeats out of caution. If two trustworthy persons inform him, his doubt is not considered, and he must accept their statement. If the informant is not trustworthy, his statement is not accepted. If the imam and followers differ—they say three, he says four—if he is certain, he does not accept their statement; otherwise he accepts. If the people differ and the imam is with a group, he accepts his statement.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is a chapter on doubt (shakk) in prayer and purification. It begins with the ruling that doubt in the number of rak'ahs invalidates the prayer if it occurs before completion and if it is either the first doubt the person has ever experienced (in any prayer) or if doubt is not habitual for him. The author presents two interpretations of 'first doubt': Fakhr al-Islam and Ibn al-Fadl hold it means first doubt in this particular prayer, while Imam al-Sarakhsi holds it means that forgetfulness is not a habit, even if he has forgotten before rarely. The relied-upon position is the latter, as expressed by the phrase 'or the doubt is not habitual for him'. The proof is the hadith commanding one who doubts to start over. This is restricted to cases of first or non-habitual doubt. If doubt occurs after taslim, it is disregarded unless certainty of omission arises. The passage then gives detailed rulings for cases where a person is certain of missing a pillar but doubts which, and rules regarding reports from trustworthy persons about a deficiency in prayer. The overall principle is that the prayer is built on certainty, and doubt is only considered if it is a new experience or not habitual, otherwise one should rely on preponderance.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Doubt: equality of two possibilities (tasawi al-amrayn). In prayer context, it refers to hesitation between two numbers of rak'ahs.
أول ما عرض له من الشك (awwal ma 'arada lahu min al-shakk): The first doubt that ever occurred to him in his life, according to some scholars; or the first in this particular prayer according to others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person frequently doubts the number of rak'ahs in every prayer, what should he do?
A) He must repeat the entire prayer every time he doubts.
B) He should act on what he is certain of (e.g., the lesser number) and continue.
C) He should perform sajdah al-sahw and continue.
D) He must stop praying and consult a scholar.

Key Takeaway
Doubt in rak'ah count invalidates prayer only if it occurs before completion and is either the first time or non-habitual; otherwise, build on certainty.

When Doubt in Rak'ahs Invalidates Prayer
States ruling on doubt in rak'ah count nullifying prayer with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which doubt in rak'ahs invalidates the prayer according to the Hanafi school and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the interpretation of 'first time'.

Core Idea
Doubt in rak'ahs invalidates prayer only if it is the first occurrence or not habitual; regular doubt does not nullify.

This lesson examines a nuanced Hanafi ruling: when does doubt about the number of rak'ahs nullify the prayer? The matn states that doubt invalidates only if it occurs before completion and is either the first time or not habitual. The commentary explores the meaning of 'first time' and the hadith evidence, including a subtle intra-Hanafi difference in interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is doubt (shakk) regarding the number of rak'ahs during prayer. The ruling is that the prayer becomes invalid (batil) under specific conditions.
The ruling applies only to doubt in rak'ah count, not other types of doubt.
2
List the conditions for invalidity
Two conditions must be met: (1) The doubt occurs before completing the prayer (i.e., before salam). (2) The doubt is either the first time the person has experienced such doubt or it is not habitual for them.
The condition of 'first time' is interpreted differently by Hanafi scholars.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The proof is the hadith: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer about how many he prayed, let him start anew.' The imperative indicates obligation, but it is interpreted as restricted to first-time or non-habitual doubt based on other narrations.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so its application is subject to interpretation.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Fakhr al-Islam and Ibn al-Fadl interpret 'first time' as within this specific prayer. Imam al-Sarakhsi interprets it as 'not habitual' in general. Both agree that the prayer is invalid.
The mufta bihi position includes both phrasings: 'first time or not habitual'.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a concrete case, determine whether the conditions are met and state the ruling.
Practice with examples helps internalize the conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في الشك في الصلاة والطهارة
تَبْطُلُ الصَّلاةُ بالشَّكُ في عددِ رَكَعَاتِها، إذا كان قبل إكمالها، وهو أوّلُ ما عَرَضَ لَه مِنَ الشَّكُ أَوْ كان الشَّكُ غير عادةٍ له، فلو شك بعدَ سلامِهِ لا يُعتبرُ، إِلا إِنْ تيقّنَ بالتَّرْكِ، . وهو تساوي الأمرين، ( في عددِ رَكَعَاتِها) کـتردد بـيـن ثـلاث وثنتين، ( إذا كان ذلك الشك (قبل إكمالها)، وكان أيضاً (وهو) أي: الشك (أوّلُ ما عَرَضَ له منَ الشَّكُ) بعد بلوغه في صلاة ما، وهذا قول أكثر المشايخ، وقال فخر الإسلام أول ما عرض له في هذه الصلاة، واختاره ( ابن الفضل ، وذهب الإمام السرخسي) إلى أن المعنى أن السهو ليس بعادة له، لا أنه لم [ يسه في عمره قط ]، فحكمه حكم من ابتدأه الشك، فلذا قال (أو كان الشَّكُ غـيـر عــادة له) فتبطل به لقوله : ( إِذَا شَكَ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي صَلاتِهِ أَنَّهُ كَمْ صَلَّى، فَلْيَسْتَقْبِل الصَّلاةَ ) وقد حمل على ما إذا كان أول شك عرض له، لما سنذكره من الرواية الأخرى (۳)، ولأنه قادر على إسقاط ما عليه من الفرض بيقين من غير مشقة، فيلزمه ذلك، كما لو شك أنه صلى أو لم يصل والوقـت بـاق فإنه يلزمه أن يصلي، كما في «الفتح»، و«التبيين»
Chapter on Doubt in Prayer and Purification. Prayer is invalidated by doubt in the number of its rak'ahs, if that (doubt) occurs before completing it, and it is the first doubt that occurred to him or the doubt is not habitual for him. So if he doubts after his salam, it is not considered, unless he is certain of omission. (Commentary) And it (doubt) is the equality of the two matters, in the number of its rak'ahs, such as hesitation between three and two. (If that doubt) (before completing it) and also (it is) (the first doubt that occurred to him) after reaching adulthood in some prayer. This is the saying of most mashayikh. Fakhr al-Islam said: the first that occurred to him in this prayer, and Ibn al-Fadl chose it. Imam al-Sarakhsi went to the meaning that forgetfulness is not habitual for him, not that he never forgot in his life. So his ruling is the ruling of one whom doubt begins. Hence he said (or the doubt is not habitual for him), so it invalidates by it due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'When one of you doubts in his prayer about how many he prayed, let him start the prayer anew.' And it has been interpreted as when it was the first doubt that occurred to him, because of the other narration we will mention (3), and because he is able to remove what is upon him of the obligation with certainty without hardship, so that is incumbent upon him, just as if he doubts whether he prayed or not while time remains, then it is incumbent upon him to pray, as in al-Fath and al-Tabyin.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hadith. The matn states that doubt about the number of rak'ahs invalidates prayer under two conditions: (1) the doubt occurs before completing the prayer, (2) it is either the first time this person has experienced such doubt or it is not habitual for him. The sharh explains that 'doubt' means equal probability between two numbers, e.g., between two and three. The hadith 'When one of you doubts... let him restart' is interpreted as referring to the first occurrence to harmonize with another narration (about frequent doubt). The reasoning is that one can remove the obligation with certainty without hardship, similar to the case of doubting whether one prayed at all while time remains. The Hanafi scholars differ on the meaning of 'first doubt': Fakhr al-Islam and Ibn al-Fadl restrict it to this specific prayer, while Imam al-Sarakhsi interprets it as 'not habitual'. Both agree on the ruling.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Equality of two possibilities regarding the number of rak'ahs prayed.
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness in prayer; used here to describe a state that may become habitual.
عادة ('adah): Habit; if doubt is habitual, the ruling changes (see later lesson).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The doubt occurs after salam.
B) The doubt is the first time or not habitual for the person.
C) The prayer is a four-rak'ah prayer.
D) The doubt is about whether one has prayed at all.

Key Takeaway
Doubt in rak'ahs invalidates prayer only under specific conditions: it must occur before completion and be either the first occurrence or not habitual.

Doubt After Salam: Ignoring Uncertainty After Completion
Ruling on doubt after salam with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on doubt after salam and apply the exception for certainty of omission.

Core Idea
Doubt after salam is ignored; only certainty of omission requires action.

After completing the prayer, doubts about its validity may arise. This lesson examines the Hanafi default: assuming validity after salam, and the conditions under which a worshipper must act. The general principle is that the prayer is presumed valid unless the person is certain of an omission, even if a contradictory action occurred after salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Determine the exact element being ruled upon: doubt (shakk) occurring after the salam (or after sitting for tashahhud) regarding the number of rak’ahs.
The doubt is about the completion of the prayer, not during it.
2
State the general ruling
The text states: 'there is nothing upon him, and his doubt is not considered.' The prayer remains valid with no need for repetition or sujud al-sahw.
Basis: holding his situation to be upon correctness (حمل حاله على الصلاح).
3
Identify the exception
The single exception is when the person is certain (تيقن) that he omitted something. In that case, he must act.
Certainty means no doubt remains; it overrides the default assumption.
4
Analyze the sub-case: certain omission but munafi occurred
If he committed a contradictory act (munafi) after salam, then the prayer is invalid and he must repeat it entirely. If no munafi, he performs the omitted part and prostrates for forgetfulness.
The munafi after salam breaks the prayer if there was a real deficiency.
5
Analyze the sub-case: certain omission of a rukn but uncertain which
The procedure is: one prostration, sit, stand, pray a full rak'ah, sit again, then final sujud al-sahw. This complex sequence compensates for the uncertain rukn.
This is a special case; normal sahw rules do not apply directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلـو شـك بعد سلامه) أو بعد جلوسـه قـدر التشهد قبل السلام، أثلاثاً صلى أو أربعاً لا شيء عليه، و ( لا يُعتبر) شـكـه حـمـلاً لحالـه عـلـى الصلاح، كما في ( البحر ) ، عن ( المحيط» ، ( إلا إن كان قد ( تيقّنَ بالتَّرْكِ)، فيعيد صلاته إن أتى بمناف بعد السلام، وإلا أتى بالمتروك ويسجد للسهو، وإذا تيقن ترك ركن وشك في تعيينه، قالوا: يسجد سجدة واحدة ثم يقعد ، ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة بسجدتين ثم يقعد ثم يسجد للسهو، ولو أخبره عدل بعد السلام أنه نقص من صلاته ركعة، وعند المصلي أنه أتم لا يلتفت إلى إخباره، وإن شك في صدقه وكذبه فعن محمد : أنه يعيد احتياطاً، وإن أخبره عدلان لا يعتبر شكه، ويجب الأخذ بقولهما وإن لم يكن المخبر عدلاً لا يقبل قوله، ولو اختلف الإمام والمؤتمون فقالوا: ثلاثاً، وقال: أربعاً، إن كان على يقين لا يأخذ بقولهم وإلا أخذ، وإن اختلف القوم، والإمام مع فريق، أخذ بقوله،
So if he doubts after his salam, or after his sitting the amount of tashahhud before salam, whether he prayed three or four, nothing is upon him, and his doubt is not considered, interpreting his situation as being upon correctness, as in al-Bahr from al-Muhit. Unless he is certain of omission, then he repeats his prayer if he did something contradictory after salam, otherwise he performs the omitted part and prostrates for forgetfulness. If he is certain of omitting a rukn but doubts which one, they said: he prostrates one prostration, then sits, then stands and prays a rak'ah with two prostrations, then sits, then prostrates for forgetfulness. And if a just person informs him after salam that he omitted a rak'ah from his prayer, while the one praying believes he completed, he does not pay attention to his information. If he doubts his truthfulness or falsehood, from Muhammad: he repeats out of precaution. If two just persons inform him, his doubt is not considered, and it is obligatory to accept their statement. If the informant is not just, his statement is not accepted. And if the imam and followers differ: the followers say three, and he says four: if he is certain, he does not accept their statement; otherwise he accepts. And if the group differs and the imam is with a party, he accepts his own statement.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage deals with doubt after the prayer is concluded (after salam or after sitting for tashahhud). The default is that such doubt is ignored: one's situation is assumed valid unless one is certain of having missed something. If one is certain of having omitted a rukn but unsure which, a detailed procedure follows (one sajdah, then sit, pray a rak'ah, etc.). Regarding external reports: a single just person's report after salam is not accepted if the pray-er is certain; if uncertain, there is a report from Imam Muhammad that one should repeat out of precaution. Two just persons' testimony is binding. If the imam and congregation disagree on the number of rak'ahs and the imam is certain, he follows his certainty; if not, he follows the congregation's statement. If the congregation is divided and the imam sides with one group, he follows his own view.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Doubt or uncertainty about an action after completing prayer.
مناف (munafi): An action that contradicts the prayer, such as speaking or moving intentionally.
تيقّن (tayaqqun): Certainty of having omitted something.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must prostrate for forgetfulness.
B) He must repeat the prayer.
C) Nothing is required; his prayer is valid.
D) He must ask someone else.

Key Takeaway
Doubt after salam is ignored; only certainty of omission requires action, and if accompanied by a munafi, the prayer must be repeated.

External Reports After Prayer: Whose Testimony is Accepted?
Ruling on external reports after salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for accepting external reports about the prayer after salam, including the roles of the informant's integrity and number.

Core Idea
A single just person's report after salam is not accepted if the worshipper is certain; two just persons' report is binding.

After completing prayer, someone may inform the worshipper of a deficiency. The Hanafi school distinguishes between reports from one just person, two just persons, and a non-just person. Additionally, when the imam and congregation disagree on the number of rak'ahs, the imam's certainty prevails. This lesson clarifies these rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
We have a person who has completed prayer and someone informs him after salam that he missed a rak'ah. The focus is on the acceptance of that information.
The report comes after salam, not during prayer.
2
Determine the informant's integrity
First, check if the informant is 'adl (just). The text says: 'If the informant is not just, his statement is not accepted.'
Justice (adalah) is a prerequisite for testimony in Islamic law.
3
Apply the number rule: single just person
If a single just person informs and the worshipper is certain he completed, the report is ignored. If the worshipper doubts the informant's truthfulness, there is a report from Imam Muhammad that he should repeat out of precaution.
The general rule: the worshipper's certainty overrides the report.
4
Apply the number rule: two just persons
If two just persons inform, the worshipper's doubt is not considered, and it is obligatory to accept their statement.
Two witnesses provide certainty (shahada).
5
Handle imam vs congregation
If the imam and followers disagree on the number of rak'ahs: if the imam is certain, he follows his certainty; otherwise he accepts the followers' statement. If some followers agree with the imam, he follows his own view.
The imam's certainty is prioritized over the congregation's claim.

Commentary
This passage deals with doubt after the prayer is concluded (after salam or after sitting for tashahhud). The default is that such doubt is ignored: one's situation is assumed valid unless one is certain of having missed something. If one is certain of having omitted a rukn but unsure which, a detailed procedure follows (one sajdah, then sit, pray a rak'ah, etc.). Key Terms
عدل ('adl): A just person whose testimony is acceptable; conditions of justice ('adalah) apply.
عدلان ('adlan): Two just persons; their joint testimony is considered binding.
احتياطاً (ihtiyatan): Out of precaution; a recommended action to ensure validity.

Frequent Doubt: Acting on Predominant Opinion
Ruling on frequent doubt with two hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for frequent doubt in prayer and apply the two hadiths to determine whether to act on predominant opinion or take the least.

Core Idea
When doubt becomes chronic, seek the more likely; if no opinion prevails, fall back on the lesser number.

This lesson examines the Hanafi solution for the frequent doubter (kathīr al-shakk). Unlike the one-time doubter who must take the least, the frequent doubter is commanded to perform taḥarrī and act on his predominant opinion (ghālib al-ẓann). If no opinion predominates, he takes the lower number. This distinction comes from harmonizing two authentic hadith reports, each applied to a different scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the special status of frequent doubt
Recognize that frequent doubt (kathrat al-shakk) triggers a different ruling than first-time doubt. The first-time doubter must always take the least; the frequent doubter uses taḥarrī.
This is a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Examine the first hadith on taḥarrī
The hadith 'When one of you doubts in his prayer, let him seek the correct opinion and complete upon it' is interpreted as applying specifically to frequent doubt. The imperative 'falyataḥarrā' indicates obligation.
The same hadith is not applied to first-time doubt due to conflicting evidence.
3
Examine the second hadith on building upon the least
The hadith about building upon one, two, or three rak'ahs applies when no opinion predominates. It is the default for first-time doubt and the fallback for frequent doubt.
This harmonization avoids contradiction between the two reports.
4
Understand the harmonization methodology
The Hanafi scholars assigned each hadith to a distinct scenario: taḥarrī for when doubt is frequent and an opinion arises; building on the least for when no opinion is reached. This is a model of jamʿ (reconciliation) of apparent contradictory texts.
This method preserves the authority of both hadiths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كثر الشَّكُ عَمِلَ بِغَالِبِ ظَنُّه. فإنْ لم يَغْلِبُ له ظن أخذ بالأقل. وقَعَدَ بعدَ كلِّ رَكعَةٍ ظَنَّها آخر صلاتِهِ. ولو كان معه واحد، ولو استيقن واحد بالتمام وآخر بالنقصان، وشك الإمام والقوم إعادة على أحد إلا على متيقن النقصان؛ لأن تيقنه لا يبطل بيقين غيره، ولو كان الإمام استيقن أنه صلى ثلاثاً كان عليه أن يعيد بالقوم ولا إعادة على مستيقن التمام لما قلنا، أما لو استيقن واحد بالنقصان ولم يستيقن أحد بالتمام بل هم واقفون فإن كان ذلك في الوقت أعادوها احتياطاً لعدم المعارضة، بخلاف ما قبلها، وإن لم يعيدوا لا شيء عليهم، إلا إذا استيقن عدلان بالنقص وأخبرا بذلك، مـن «الفتح»، و « الزاد »، و « قاضي خان» . ( وإنْ كثر الشَّكُ) تحرى، والتحري: طلب الأحرى وهو : مــا يكون أكبر رأيه عليه، وعبروا عنه تارة بالظن، وتارة بغالب الظن، وإذا تحرى (عمل) أي: أخذ ( بغالب ظنه ) [ لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « إِذَا شَكَ أحَدُكُمْ فِي صَلاتِهِ فَلْيَتَحَرَّ الصَّوَابَ فَلْيُتِمَّ عَلَيْهِ » ) وحمل على ما إذا كثر الشك فإن لم يَغْلِب له ظن أخذ بالأقل) ] لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « إِذَا سَهَا أَحَدُكُمْ فِي صَلَاتِهِ فَلَمْ يَدْرِ وَاحِدَةً صَلَّى أو ثِنْتَين، فَلْيَبْن عَلَى وَاحِدَةٍ ، فإِنْ لَمْ يَدْرِ ثِنْتَيْنِ صَلَّى أَو ثَلَاثَاً، فَلْيَبْن عَلَى ثِنْتَين، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَدْرِ ثَلاثَاً صَلَّى أو أَرْبَعَاً، فَلْيَبْنِ عَلَى ثَلاثَ وَيَسْجُدْ سَجْدَتَيْنِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُسَلَّمْ (۳) فلما ثبت عندهم كل المرويات الثلاث التي رويناها في المسائل الثلاث سلكوا فيها طريق الجمع، بحمل كل منها على محمل يتجه حمله عليه، كما في «الفتح»، (وقعَدَ) وتشهد (بعـد كـلِّ ركعـةٍ ظَنَّها آخر صلاته)؛ لئلا تاركاً فرض القعدة مع تيسر طريق يوصله إلى يقين عدم تركها، وكذا كل يصير قعود ظنه واجباً، بأن وقع في رباعية أنها الأولى أو الثانية، يجعلها أولى، ثم يقعد، ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة، ثم يقعد، ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى، فيأتي بأربع قعدات ثنتان مفروضتان، الثالثة والرابعة، وقعدتان واجبتان، ولو شك أنها الثانية أو الثالثة أتمها وقعد، ثم قام فصلى أخرى وقعد، ثم صلى الرابعة، ولو شك في الفجر وهو في القيام أنها الثالثة أو الأولى لا يتم ركعة، بـل يقعد قدر التشهد ويرفض القيام، ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعتين بفاتحة الكتاب وسورة، ثم يتشهد ثم يسجد للسهو، وإن شك وهو ساجد أنها الأولى والثانية فإنه يمضي فيها، سواء كان في السجدة
And if doubt becomes frequent, he acts on his predominant opinion. If no opinion predominates, he takes the least (rak'ah count). And he sits after every rak'ah that he thinks might be his last prayer. And if there is one with him (i.e., another opinion), and if one is certain of completion and another of deficiency, and the imam and the people doubt: no repetition is required except on the one certain of deficiency, because his certainty does not invalidate the certainty of another. And if the imam is certain that he prayed three, he must repeat with the people, but no repetition on the one certain of completion, as we said. But if one is certain of deficiency and no one is certain of completion, but they are standing (in doubt): if that (doubt) is within the time, they repeat it out of precaution due to absence of contradiction, unlike before (after time). And if they do not repeat, nothing is upon them, unless two just persons are certain of deficiency and inform of that, from al-Fath, al-Zad, and Qadi Khan. (And if doubt becomes frequent) he performs taharrī (seeking the more likely). Taharrī is seeking the more appropriate, which is what his greater opinion is upon. They sometimes call it zann (opinion) and sometimes ghalib al-zann (predominant opinion). When he performs taharrī, he acts, i.e., takes his predominant opinion, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'When one of you doubts in his prayer, let him seek the correct (opinion) and complete upon it.' And this is interpreted as when doubt is frequent. If no opinion predominates, he takes the least, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'When one of you forgets in his prayer and does not know whether he prayed one or two, let him build upon one; if he does not know two or three, build upon two; if he does not know three or four, build upon three and prostrate two prostrations before salam.' (3) So when the three narrations were established with them in the three issues, they took the path of combining them, by interpreting each in a plausible manner, as in al-Fath. (And he sits) and recites tashahhud (after every rak'ah that he thinks is his last prayer), so as not to leave the obligatory sitting while there is an easy way to reach certainty of not leaving it. Similarly, any sitting that he thinks is obligatory becomes so. For example, if in a four-rak'ah prayer he thinks it is the first or second, he makes it the first, then sits, then stands and prays a rak'ah, then sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah, resulting in four sittings: two obligatory (the third and fourth) and two obligatory (due to doubt). And if he doubts whether it is the second or third, he completes it and sits, then stands and prays another and sits, then prays the fourth. And if he doubts in Fajr while standing whether it is the third or first, he does not complete the rak'ah, but rather sits the amount of tashahhud and abandons the standing, then stands and prays two rak'ahs with Fatiha and a sura, then recites tashahhud, then prostrates for forgetfulness. And if he doubts while prostrating whether it is the first or second, he continues in it, whether in the prostration.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage deals with the person who experiences doubt frequently (habitual doubter). The rule changes: he should act on his predominant opinion (ghalib al-zann) after seeking the more likely (taharrī). If no opinion is predominant, he takes the least number of rak'ahs (e.g., if unsure between three and four, he assumes three). Additionally, he must sit for tashahhud after every rak'ah that he thinks might be his last, to ensure he does not miss the obligatory sitting. The passage provides examples: in a four-rak'ah prayer, if he thinks he is in the first or second, he treats it as the first, sits, then continues, resulting in four sittings. Specific cases are given for Fajr and for doubt during prostration. The hadith about taharrī (Bukhari and Muslim) is interpreted for frequent doubt, while the hadith about building on the least is for the case where no opinion predominates. The passage also discusses scenarios where one person is certain of completion and another of deficiency: the one certain of deficiency must repeat, but the one certain of completion does not. If only one is certain of deficiency and no one else is certain, they repeat out of precaution if time remains.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Seeking the more likely correct opinion through reflection and estimation.
غالب الظن (ghalib al-zann): Predominant opinion; what one feels is more likely correct after taharrī.
الأقل (al-aqall): The lesser number of rak'ahs when no opinion predominates.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if he frequently doubts the number of rak'ahs in prayer and has no predominant opinion?
A) He must restart the prayer.
B) He acts on the lower number of rak'ahs.
C) He acts on the higher number of rak'ahs.
D) He asks someone else.

Key Takeaway
For frequent doubt, act on predominant opinion; if none, take the least — this harmonizes two hadiths.

Sitting Obligations and Scenarios for Frequent Doubt
Additional rules for sitting and multi-person scenarios in frequent doubt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling on sitting after each rak'ah that might be the last and resolve multi-person doubt scenarios.

Core Idea
The frequent doubter must sit after every rak'ah that could be his last, ensuring no obligation is missed.

This lesson continues the treatment of frequent doubt, focusing on the requirement to sit and recite tashahhud after any rak'ah that might be the final one. This prevents leaving an obligatory sitting. The passage also examines complex scenarios involving an imam and congregation where some are certain of completion and others of deficiency.

Guided Path
1
Understand the obligation to sit after potential last rak'ah
Because the frequent doubter does not know which rak'ah is truly last, he must sit after every rak'ah that could possibly be the last. This ensures he does not miss the obligatory sitting.
This is a wajib due to doubt, not a rukn.
2
Apply to a four-rak'ah prayer scenario
If he thinks he is in the first or second rak'ah, he treats it as the first, sits, then stands, and continues. The result is four sittings: two obligatory (third and fourth) and two obligatory due to doubt.
The example shows how the rule works in practice.
3
Handle special cases: Fajr and prostration
For Fajr, if he doubts while standing whether it is the third or first, he abandons the standing and sits, then prays two rak'ahs from the beginning. During prostration, if he doubts between first and second, he continues without change.
Different actions depending on the stage of prayer.
4
Analyze scenarios with multiple people (imam and followers)
If one person is certain of completion and another of deficiency, the one certain of deficiency must repeat, but the one certain of completion does not. If only one is certain of deficiency and no one else is certain, they repeat if still within time.
Certainty of one does not affect the certainty of another.

Frequent Doubt in Prayer: Taharri and Predominant Opinion
Expounding Hanafi rulings on frequent doubt in prayer with hadith proofs and scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on frequent doubt (kathrat al-shakk) in prayer by distinguishing between acting on predominant opinion and taking the least, and by identifying the required sittings.

Core Idea
Frequent doubt in prayer is resolved by predominant opinion; if none, take the least.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi methodology for handling persistent uncertainty in salah. You will learn when to rely on ghalib al-zann and when to fall back on the minimal certain number, supported by primary texts and detailed scenarios for different rak'ahs and prayer types.

Guided Path
1
Identify doubt frequency
Distinguish between frequent (kathir) and occasional (qalil) doubt. The ruling for frequent doubt is taharri; for occasional doubt, build on certainty.
Frequent means doubt occurs often, e.g., in every prayer or most prayers.
2
Apply taharri if predominant opinion exists
When doubt is frequent, the worshipper does taharri (seeks the likelier) and acts on his predominant opinion (ghalib al-zann). This is derived from the hadith commanding taharri.
Taharri is a wajib act; the imperative falyataharra indicates wujub in Hanafi usul.
3
Fall back to al-aqall if no predominant opinion
If no opinion predominates, the worshipper takes the least number he is certain of (al-aqall) and builds upon it, based on the hadith of building on the smallest certain number.
This is also wajib; the hadith offers a sequence from one to three rak'ahs.
4
Apply the sitting rule after probable last rak'ah
After each rak'ah that the worshipper thinks is the last, he must sit and recite tashahhud to avoid missing the obligatory sitting. This is wajib.
The number of sittings increases; in a four-rak'ah prayer, two become fard and two wajib.
5
Work through scenarios
Apply the rules to concrete cases: doubt in Fajr during standing or prostration, doubt in a four-rak'ah prayer between first/second or second/third. The text provides detailed procedures.
Each scenario illustrates how the general rules adapt to specific postures and counts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
