( وإنْ كثر الشَّكُ) تحرى، والتحري: طلب الأحرى وهو : مــا يكون أكبر رأيه عليه، وعبروا عنه تارة بالظن، وتارة بغالب الظن، وإذا تحرى (عمل) أي: أخذ ( بغالب ظنه ) [ لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « إِذَا شَكَ أحَدُكُمْ فِي صَلاتِهِ فَلْيَتَحَرَّ الصَّوَابَ فَلْيُتِمَّ عَلَيْهِ » ) وحمل على ما إذا كثر الشك فإن لم يَغْلِب له ظن أخذ بالأقل) ] لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « إِذَا سَهَا أَحَدُكُمْ فِي صَلَاتِهِ فَلَمْ يَدْرِ وَاحِدَةً صَلَّى أو ثِنْتَين، فَلْيَبْن عَلَى وَاحِدَةٍ ، فإِنْ لَمْ يَدْرِ ثِنْتَيْنِ صَلَّى أَو ثَلَاثَاً، فَلْيَبْن عَلَى ثِنْتَين، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَدْرِ ثَلاثَاً صَلَّى أو أَرْبَعَاً، فَلْيَبْنِ عَلَى ثَلاثَ وَيَسْجُدْ سَجْدَتَيْنِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُسَلَّمْ (۳) فلما ثبت عندهم كل المرويات الثلاث التي رويناها في المسائل الثلاث سلكوا فيها طريق الجمع، بحمل كل منها على محمل يتجه حمله عليه، كما في «الفتح»، (وقعَدَ) وتشهد (بعـد كـلِّ ركعـةٍ ظَنَّها آخر صلاته)؛ لئلا تاركاً فرض القعدة مع تيسر طريق يوصله إلى يقين عدم تركها، وكذا كل يصير قعود ظنه واجباً، بأن وقع في رباعية أنها الأولى أو الثانية، يجعلها أولى، ثم يقعد، ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة، ثم يقعد، ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى، فيأتي بأربع قعدات ثنتان مفروضتان، الثالثة والرابعة، وقعدتان واجبتان، ولو شك أنها الثانية أو الثالثة أتمها وقعد، ثم قام فصلى أخرى وقعد، ثم صلى الرابعة، ولو شك في الفجر وهو في القيام أنها الثالثة أو الأولى لا يتم ركعة، بـل يقعد قدر التشهد ويرفض القيام، ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعتين بفاتحة الكتاب وسورة، ثم يتشهد ثم يسجد للسهو، وإن شك وهو ساجد أنها الأولى والثانية فإنه يمضي فيها، سواء كان في السجدة الأولى أو الثانية، وإذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية يقعد قدر التشهد، ثم يصلي ركعة، ولو شك في صلاة الفجر في سجود الأولى، أنه صلى ركعتين أو ثلاثاً، يتم ركعته بالسجدتين، وصحت صلاته وإن كان الشك في السجدة الثانية فسدت صلاته. تتمة: شك في الحدث وتيقن الطهارة فهو متطهر، وبالقلب محدث ، شك في بعض وضوئه وهو أول ما عرض له غسل ذلك الموضع، وإن كان يعرض له الشك كثيراً لا يلتفت إليه، وكذا لـو شك أنه كبر للافتتاح، فإن كان أول ما عرض له استقبل وإن كثر يمضي، كذا في « الدراية». وفي التاتارخانية » : لو شك في صلاته أنه هل كبر للافتتاح أو أصابته النجاسة أو أحدث أو مسح رأسه أم لا ؟؟ إن كان أول مرة استقبل، وإن كان يقع له مثل ذلك كثيراً جاز له، ولا يلزمه الوضوء ولا غسل الثوب. وفي ( العتابية » : لو شك هل كبر ؟ قيل: إن كان في الركعة الأولى يعيد التكبيرات وإن كان في الثانية لا. انتهى.
And if doubt becomes frequent, he acts according to his predominant opinion. If no opinion predominates for him, he takes the least. And he sits after every rak'ah that he thinks is the last of his prayer. And if there is one with him, and if one is certain of completion and another of deficiency, and the imam and the congregation doubt, the prayer is repeated only upon the one certain of deficiency; because his certainty does not nullify the certainty of another. And if the imam is certain that he prayed three [rak'ahs], he must repeat with the congregation, and there is no repetition upon the one certain of completion, for what we said. As for if one is certain of deficiency and no one is certain of completion, rather they are [in doubt], then if that is within the time, they repeat it out of precaution due to no contradicting certainty, unlike before that. If they do not repeat, nothing is upon them, unless two upright persons are certain of deficiency and inform of that. From al-Fath, al-Zad, and Qadi Khan. (And if doubt becomes frequent) he does taharri, and taharri is: seeking the worthier, which is what is most likely in his opinion. They express it sometimes as dhan (opinion) and sometimes as predominant opinion. When he does taharri, (he acts) i.e. takes (according to his predominant opinion) [due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer, let him do taharri for what is correct and complete upon it'] and it is interpreted as when doubt is frequent. If no opinion predominates for him, he takes the least) [due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'When one of you forgets in his prayer and does not know whether he prayed one or two, let him build upon one; if he does not know whether he prayed two or three, let him build upon two; if he does not know whether he prayed three or four, let him build upon three and perform two prostrations before salutations.' Since it was established with them all the three narrated traditions that we narrated in the three issues, they followed in them the way of combining, by interpreting each upon an interpretation that is appropriate to apply to it, as in al-Fath. (And he sits) and recites tashahhud (after every rak'ah that he thinks is the last of his prayer) so that he does not abandon the obligatory sitting while a path is available that leads him to certainty of not abandoning it. Similarly, every sitting that he thinks is obligatory: if in a four-rak'ah prayer it occurs to him that it is the first or second, he makes it the first, then sits, then stands and prays a rak'ah, then sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah, so he performs four sittings: two obligatory (the third and fourth) and two obligatory? Actually the text says two are fard (the third and fourth) and two are wajib. And if he doubts whether it is the second or third, he completes it and sits, then stands and prays another and sits, then prays the fourth. And if he doubts in the Fajr prayer while standing whether it is the third or first, he does not complete the rak'ah, but rather sits for the duration of tashahhud and abandons standing, then stands and prays two rak'ahs with Surah al-Fatihah and a surah, then recites tashahhud then prostrates for forgetfulness. And if he doubts while prostrating whether it is the first or second, he continues in it, whether in the first or second prostration. And when he raises his head from the second prostration, he sits for the duration of tashahhud, then prays a rak'ah. And if he doubts in the Fajr prayer during the first prostration whether he had prayed two or three rak'ahs, he completes his rak'ah with the two prostrations, and his prayer is valid. But if the doubt was during the second prostration, his prayer is invalid. Appendix: If one doubts about hadath (ritual impurity) and is certain of taharah (purity), he is in a state of purity, but in his heart he is worried about hadath. If he doubts about some part of his ablution while it is the first time it occurs to him, he washes that part. But if such doubt occurs to him frequently, he pays no attention to it. Similarly, if he doubts whether he said the opening takbir, if it is the first time it occurs, he repeats; if frequent, he continues. This is in al-Dirayah. In al-Tatar Khaniyyah: If one doubts in his prayer whether he said the opening takbir, or was struck by impurity, or had an event, or wiped his head or not? If it is the first time, he repeats; if such occurs to him frequently, it is permissible for him, and neither wudu nor washing the garment is necessary for him. In al-Utabiyyah: If one doubts whether he said the takbir? It is said: If in the first rak'ah, he repeats the takbirs; if in the second, he does not. End.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the Hanafi rulings on frequent doubt (kathrat al-shakk) in prayer. It is an expansion of the matn of Nur al-Idah. The author first states the matn's ruling: when doubt is frequent, the worshipper acts on his predominant opinion (ghalib al-zann). If no opinion predominates, he takes the least number he is certain of (al-aqall). This is based on two hadith: the first commands taharri (seeking the likeliest) when in doubt, and the second instructs building on the smallest number when uncertain. The commentator explains taharri as seeking what is more likely in one's opinion, and the Hanafi school combined these hadith by interpreting the first for frequent doubt and the second for occasional doubt. The matn further states that the worshipper sits after every rak'ah he thinks is his last, to avoid missing the obligatory sitting. The commentary elaborates on scenarios: in a four-rak'ah prayer, if he thinks a rak'ah is the first or second, he makes it the first, sits briefly, then continues, resulting in four sittings (two obligatory, two wajib). Detailed cases cover Fajr prayer, standing, prostrating, and the appendix addresses doubt about hadath and takbir. The core principle is that frequent doubt is to be resolved by taharri, while occasional doubt follows the basic rule of building on certainty.

Key Terms
الشك (al-shakk): Uncertainty between two possibilities in prayer, e.g., number of rak'ahs performed.
التحري (al-taharri): Seeking the likelier (ahra) by reflecting and acting on what is most probably correct.
غالب الظن (ghalib al-zann): The predominant opinion or strong probability that tips the scale in the worshipper's mind.
الأقل (al-aqall): The smallest number of rak'ahs the worshipper is certain of having performed.
القعود (al-qu'ud): The act of sitting in prayer, specifically after a rak'ah for tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a worshipper do if he frequently doubts the number of rak'ahs in his prayer and has a predominant opinion?
A) He should act on his predominant opinion.
B) He should always take the least number.
C) He must repeat his prayer.
D) He should ignore the doubt and continue.

Key Takeaway
Frequent doubt in prayer is resolved by taharri (acting on predominant opinion or taking the least), with mandatory sittings after each rak'ah thought to be the last.

Doubt About Rak'ahs in Fajr Prayer
Ruling on doubt in Fajr prayer rak'ah count

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on doubt about the number of rak'ahs in Fajr prayer and distinguish when the prayer is valid versus invalid based on the timing of the doubt.

Core Idea
In Fajr prayer, doubt about rak'ahs invalidates only if it occurs after the second prostration.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Imdad al-Fattah sharh: doubt during the Fajr prayer about whether one has prayed two or three rak'ahs. The ruling hinges on when the doubt arises—during the first prostration or the second. This distinction illustrates the Hanafi principle that doubt after completing an essential act (here, the second sajdah) may invalidate the prayer, while doubt earlier allows correction by completing the current rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doubt scenario
The person is praying Fajr (two rak'ahs) but doubts whether he has performed two or three rak'ahs.
Fajr is normally two rak'ahs, so doubting three indicates uncertainty about an extra rak'ah.
2
Locate the timing of doubt
Distinguish between doubt occurring during the first prostration (sajdah) of the current rak'ah versus doubt during the second prostration.
The text specifies 'in the first prostration' and 'in the second prostration' of the rak'ah being performed.
3
Determine the ruling
If doubt occurs during the first prostration, the person completes the rak'ah (with both prostrations) and the prayer is valid. If doubt occurs during the second prostration, the prayer becomes invalid (fasid).
The second prostration completes the rak'ah; doubt after that indicates uncertainty about a completed unit.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The key is whether the rak'ah is still incomplete (doubt before finishing sajdah al-thaniyah) or complete (doubt after). Incomplete rak'ah allows correction; complete rak'ah means the prayer is built on a faulty count.
This aligns with the Hanafi rule that certainty is required for the number of rak'ahs; doubt after completion cannot be remedied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأولى أو الثانية، وإذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية يقعد قدر التشهد، ثم يصلي ركعة، ولو شك في صلاة الفجر في سجود الأولى، أنه صلى ركعتين أو ثلاثاً، يتم ركعته بالسجدتين، وصحت صلاته وإن كان الشك في السجدة الثانية فسدت صلاته. تتمة: شك في الحدث وتيقن الطهارة فهو متطهر، وبالقلب محدث ، شك في بعض وضوئه وهو أول ما عرض له غسل ذلك الموضع، وإن كان يعرض له الشك كثيراً لا يلتفت إليه، وكذا لـو شك أنه كبر للافتتاح، فإن كان أول ما عرض له استقبل وإن كثر يمضي، كذا في « الدراية». وفي التاتارخانية » : لو شك في صلاته أنه هل كبر للافتتاح أو أصابته النجاسة أو أحدث أو مسح رأسه أم لا ؟؟ إن كان أول مرة استقبل، وإن كان يقع له مثل ذلك كثيراً جاز له، ولا يلزمه الوضوء ولا غسل الثوب. وفي ( العتابية » : لو شك هل كبر ؟ قيل: إن كان في الركعة الأولى يعيد التكبيرات وإن كان في الثانية لا. انتهى.
(1) أي: إذا شك بالطهارة وتيقن بالحدث فهو محدث. (٢) أي: وهو في الوضوء. ط.
The first or second; and when he raises his head from the second prostration he sits for the amount of the tashahhud, then prays one rak'ah. If he doubts in the Fajr prayer during the first prostration whether he prayed two rak'ahs or three, he completes his rak'ah with the two prostrations, and his prayer is valid. But if the doubt was in the second prostration, his prayer is invalid. Appendix: If he doubts about an event and is certain of purity, he is pure; but with the heart he is impure. If he doubts about some part of his ablution and it is the first time it has occurred to him, he washes that spot; but if he has frequent doubt, he pays no attention to it. Similarly, if he doubts whether he said the takbir for opening, if it is the first time it has occurred to him, he starts again; but if it is frequent, he continues. Thus in al-Dirayah. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: If he doubts in his prayer whether he said the takbir for opening, or whether impurity touched him, or he had an event, or he wiped his head or not? Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings from the sharh dealing with doubt (shakk) in prayer and purification. The author presents scenarios: if someone doubts about the number of rak'ahs in Fajr and the doubt occurs during the first prostration, he completes the rak'ah and the prayer is valid; but if the doubt occurs during the second prostration, the prayer becomes invalid. The general principle is that if doubt occurs for the first time and is not habitual, one must act on it by performing the necessary action (e.g., repeating a missed step). However, if someone is prone to frequent doubt (waswasa), he should ignore it and continue. This applies to doubts about hadath (ritual impurity), wudu, and takbirat al-ihram. The source texts cited (al-Dirayah, al-Tatarkhaniyyah, al-Atabiyyah) are standard Hanafi references. The footnotes clarify that if one doubts purity but is certain of impurity, he is considered impure.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Doubt about a matter of worship, such as the number of rak'ahs.
سجدة الأولى (sajdah al-ula): The first prostration of a rak'ah.
السجدة الثانية (al-sajdah al-thaniyah): The second prostration of a rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Fajr prayer, if a person doubts whether he has prayed two or three rak'ahs and the doubt occurs during the first prostration of the current rak'ah, what should he do?
A) He should stop and repeat the prayer from the beginning.
B) He should complete the current rak'ah with its two prostrations and the prayer is valid.
C) He should perform two additional prostrations of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) and then continue.
D) He should sit and recite tashahhud, then complete the prayer as four rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
In Fajr prayer, doubt about the number of rak'ahs during the first prostration allows correction and the prayer remains valid, but doubt during the second prostration invalidates the prayer.

Doubt About Hadath and Parts of Wudu
Rulings on doubt about hadath and wudu parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule regarding doubt about hadath (ritual impurity) and about specific parts of wudu, distinguishing between first occurrence and frequent doubt.

Core Idea
First-time doubt about wudu or hadath requires action; frequent doubt is ignored.

This lesson covers two related rulings: doubt about whether one has broken his wudu (hadath) when certain of purity, and doubt about washing a specific part of wudu. The key principle is whether the doubt is a first-time occurrence or recurrent (waswasa). First-time doubt demands action (e.g., washing the part), while frequent doubt is disregarded to avoid hardship.

Guided Path
1
Interpret the hadath doubt ruling
If one doubts whether an event (hadath) occurred but is certain of being in a state of purity, he remains pure according to the apparent state. However, the footnotes clarify that if one doubts purity while certain of hadath, he is considered impure.
The text says 'he is pure but in the heart impure' which is a nuanced expression; the operative ruling is that certainty overrides doubt.
2
Identify the wudu doubt scenario
If a person is performing wudu and doubts whether a particular part has been washed, the ruling depends on whether this doubt is new or habitual.
The doubt is about a specific part, not the whole wudu.
3
Apply the first-time rule
If the doubt occurs for the first time (i.e., not a pattern), he must wash that part again to be safe.
This is based on the principle of certainty being required for each obligatory act.
4
Apply the frequent doubt rule
If the person frequently experiences such doubts (waswasa), he ignores the doubt and continues, as paying attention would lead to hardship.
This is a manifestation of the Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applied to waswasa.

This passage is a series of rulings from the sharh dealing with doubt (shakk) in prayer and purification. The author presents scenarios: if someone doubts about the number of rak'ahs in Fajr and the doubt occurs during the first prostration, he completes the rak'ah and the prayer is valid; but if the doubt occurs during the second prostration, the prayer becomes invalid. A) He should wash his face again every time he doubts.

D) He should perform tayammum instead.

Key Takeaway
For first-time doubt about a wudu part, one must wash it; for frequent doubt, one ignores it. In doubt about hadath, certainty of purity overrides doubt.

Doubt About Takbirat al-Ihram
Rulings on doubt about takbirat al-ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the Hanafi ruling when a person doubts whether he said the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram), differentiating between first-time and frequent doubt, and between doubt in the first rak'ah and later.

Core Idea
Doubt about the opening takbir requires restart if it is first-time; frequent doubt is ignored; if doubt arises in the second rak'ah, no need to repeat.

This lesson covers rulings on doubt regarding takbirat al-ihram (the opening Allahu Akbar). The passage cites multiple sources (al-Dirayah, al-Tatarkhaniyyah, al-Atabiyyah) to present the Hanafi position. The key distinction is whether the doubt is a first occurrence or habitual, and additionally, if the person has already entered the second rak'ah, the takbir is considered valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling from al-Dirayah
If someone doubts whether he said the opening takbir, and it is the first time he has such doubt, he must start the prayer again (istiqbal). If he frequently has such doubts, he continues.
This is the same principle as with wudu: first-time requires action, frequent is ignored.
2
Examine the ruling from al-Tatarkhaniyyah
This expands the doubt to include not just takbir, but also whether impurity touched him, he had an event, or he wiped his head. The ruling is the same: first-time start again, frequent continue.
It emphasizes that no wudu or washing of garment is required for frequent doubts.
3
Consider the ruling from al-Atabiyyah
If doubt about takbir occurs in the first rak'ah, he repeats the takbirs (i.e., he can say them again). If it occurs in the second rak'ah, he does not need to repeat them, because the prayer's validity has already been established.
This adds a time-based distinction: the later the doubt, the less likely it is to affect validity.

The first or second; and when he raises his head from the second prostration he sits for the amount of the tashahhud, then prays one rak'ah. If he doubts in the Fajr prayer during the first prostration whether he prayed two rak'ahs or three, he completes his rak'ah with the two prostrations, and his prayer is valid. But if the doubt was in the second prostration, his prayer is invalid. Appendix: If he doubts about an event and is certain of purity, he is pure; but with the heart he is impure. If he doubts about some part of his ablution and it is the first time it has occurred to him, he washes that spot; but if he has frequent doubt, he pays no attention to it. Similarly, if he doubts whether he said the takbir for opening, if it is the first time it has occurred to him, he starts again; but if it is frequent, he continues. Thus in al-Dirayah. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: If he doubts in his prayer whether he said the takbir for opening, or whether impurity touched him, or he had an event, or he wiped his head or not? If it is the first time, he starts again; but if such things occur to him often, it is permissible for him, and he is not required to perform ablution nor wash his garment. In al-Atabiyyah: If he doubts whether he said the takbir? It was said: If it is in the first rak'ah, he repeats the takbirs; if in the second, he does not. End.
(1) Meaning: if he doubts about purity and is certain of an event, he is impure. (2) Meaning: and it is during ablution. End.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings from the sharh dealing with doubt (shakk) in prayer and purification. The author presents scenarios: if someone doubts about the number of rak'ahs in Fajr and the doubt occurs during the first prostration, he completes the rak'ah and the prayer is valid; but if the doubt occurs during the second prostration, the prayer becomes invalid. The general principle is that if doubt occurs for the first time and is not habitual, one must act on it by performing the necessary action (e.g., repeating a missed step). However, if someone is prone to frequent doubt (waswasa), he should ignore it and continue. This applies to doubts about hadath (ritual impurity), wudu, and takbirat al-ihram. The source texts cited (al-Dirayah, al-Tatarkhaniyyah, al-Atabiyyah) are standard Hanafi references. The footnotes clarify that if one doubts purity but is certain of impurity, he is considered impure.

Key Terms
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbirat al-ihram): The opening 'Allahu Akbar' that begins the prayer.
دراية (al-Dirayah): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Karkhi or similar; likely refers to a commentary.
تاتارخانية (al-Tatarkhaniyyah): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Tatarkhani.
عتابية (al-Atabiyyah): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Atabi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For doubt about the opening takbir: first-time in first rak'ah → repeat takbir; first-time in second rak'ah or frequent doubt → continue.

Sajdah al-Tilawah: Cause, Obligation, and Timing
Opening of the chapter on prostration of recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the cause, ruling, and timing of sajdah al-tilawah according to the Hanafi school and distinguish between its conditions and pillar.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib on reciter and listener, on delay outside prayer but immediate during prayer.

This lesson opens the chapter on the prostration of recitation (sajdah al-tilawah). We will explore its cause (sabab), its ruling as wajib (not fard), and the important distinction between timing inside and outside prayer. You will also learn the conditions and the single pillar of this act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause
Recognize that the cause (sabab) is recitation (tilawah), not mere hearing. Understand that hearing is a condition for the listener, not a cause. Note the evidence from the hadith and the case of the deaf reciter.
The text reports a difference of opinion on whether hearing is a cause; the correct Hanafi view is that it is a condition.
2
Determine the hukm level
Identify that sajdah al-tilawah is wajib, not fard, because the proof is zanni. Understand the three types of prostration verses and why each yields obligation.
The Hanafi school distinguishes wajib (obligatory with speculative proof) from fard (obligatory with certain proof).
3
Analyse the timing
Outside prayer, the obligation is on delay (tarakhi) according to the preferred view; during prayer, it is immediate (faur). Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and the reasoning.
The text mentions two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one for delay (preferred) and one for immediacy. The chosen view is delay outside prayer.
4
Enumerate conditions and pillar
List the shurut: purity from hadath and khabath, facing qiblah, covering private parts, intention, and that tayammum is not allowed without excuse. The rukn is placing the forehead on the ground.
These are similar to prayer conditions but adapted for this prostration.

Source Text

من إضافة الحكم إلى سببه، وهو الأصل في الإضافة؛ لأنها للاختصاص، وأقوى وجوهه اختصاص المسبب بالسبب لأنه حادث به كذا في الدراية»، وشرطها الطهارة عن الحدث والخبث، ولا يجوز التيمم لها بلا عذر يبيحه، واستقبال القبلة، وستر العورة والنية، وركنـهـا : وضع الجبهة على الأرض، وصفتها الوجوب عندنا على الفور في الصلاة، وعلى التراخي إن كانت غـيـر صلاتية، كما سنذكره وحكمها سقوط الواجب في الدنيا ونيل الثواب في العقبي. ثم شرع في بيان السبب، فقال: ( سَبَبُهُ التّلاوةُ، على التّالي ) اتفاقاً (وَ) على (السّامع في الصحيح) لأن التلاوة سبب بالإجماع؛ لأن السجدة تضاف إليها وتكرر بتكررها، وفي السماع خلاف، قيل: إنه سبب لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : السَّجْدَةُ عَلَى مَنْ سَمِعَهَا » (١)، وفي ( التاتارخانية : قال الصحابة: السجدة على من سمعها، كما قالوا: على من تلاها، والصحيح أن السبب التلاوة في حق السامع، والسماع شرط عمل التلاوة في حقه، كما في «الفتح» عن « (الكافي ) ، وفي ( التاتارخانية» عن « المحيط » : حتى لو تلاها الأصم ولم يسمع وجب عليه السجدة (وهو) أي: السجود للتلاوة (واجب) لأن آيــات السجود على ثلاثة أقسام: قسم فيه الأمر الصریح به وقسم تضمن استنكاك الكفرة حيث أمروا به، وقسم فيه حكاية امتثال الأنبياء به، وكل من الامتثال والاقتداء ومخالفة الكفرة واجب، إلا أن يدل دليل في معين على عدم لزومه، لكن دلالتها فيه ظنية، فكان الثابت الوجوب لا الفرض، ووجوبـه ( على التراخي) عند محمد، وهو رواية عن الإمام وهو المختار عند أبي يوسف وهو روايـة عــن الإمام: يجب على الفور، وجه القول بالتراخي أن دليل الوجوب مطلق عن تعيين الوقت، ومطلق الأمر لا يقتضي الفور ، فيجب في وقت غير معين، ويتعين ذلك بتعيينـه فـعـلا وإنمـا يـتـضـيـق عـلـيـه الوجوب في آخر عمره، كما في سائر الواجبات الموسعة، ولا يجب نية تعيين السجدات، ولا يجب على المحتضر الإيصاء بها، وقيل: يجب كما في ( البحر ) ، عن ( القنية ) ، والوجوب على التراخي ( إن لم تكن) وجبت بتلاوة ( في الصَّلاة، فإنها تجب بها فيها على المصلي مضيقاً لـقـيـام دليـل التضييق، وهو أنها وجبت بما هو من أفعال الصلاة وهو القراءة، فالتحقت بأفعالها وصارت جزءاً من

Chapter of Prostration of Recitation. The cause is recitation, upon the reciter and upon the listener in the correct view, and it is obligatory on delay if not in prayer. Chapter of Prostration of Recitation: from adding the ruling to its cause, and that is the basis in addition; because it is for specification, and the strongest of its aspects is the specification of the effect by the cause because it occurs by it. Thus in al-Dirayah. Its conditions are purity from hadath and khabath, and tayammum is not permissible for it without an excuse that permits it, facing the qiblah, covering the private parts, and intention. Its pillar is placing the forehead on the ground. Its description: the obligation with us is immediate in prayer, and on delay if it is non-prayer, as we will mention. Its ruling: fulfillment of the obligation in this world and attainment of reward in the afterlife. Then he began to explain the cause, saying: Its cause is recitation, upon the reciter by agreement, and upon the listener in the correct view, because recitation is a cause by consensus; because the prostration is attributed to it and is repeated with its repetition. Regarding hearing, there is a difference of opinion: it was said it is a cause due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'The prostration is upon whoever hears it.' In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: The Companions said: The prostration is upon whoever hears it, just as they said: upon whoever recites it. And the correct view is that the cause is recitation in the case of the listener, and hearing is a condition for the application of recitation in his case, as in al-Fath from al-Kafi. And in al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Muhit: Even if a deaf person recites it and does not hear, the prostration is obligatory upon him. And it, meaning prostration for recitation, is obligatory, because the verses of prostration are of three types: a type containing explicit command for it, a type containing the refusal of the disbelievers where they were commanded to do it, and a type containing the narration of the prophets' compliance. And each of compliance, emulation, and opposition to the disbelievers is obligatory, unless a proof indicates in a specific case that it is not binding. But its indication in it is speculative, so what is established is obligation, not necessity (fard). And its obligation is on delay according to Muhammad, and it is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, and it is the chosen view according to Abu Yusuf, and it is a narration from the Imam: it is immediate. The argument for the view of delay is that the evidence of obligation is absolute regarding the designation of time, and an absolute command does not necessitate immediacy; so it is obligatory at an unspecified time, and it becomes specified by actual performance, but its obligation becomes restricted at the end of his life, as in all extended obligations. And it is not necessary to intend which specific prostration, nor is it necessary for the dying person to bequeath it. And it was said: it is necessary, as in al-Bahr from al-Qunyah. And the obligation is on delay if it is not due to recitation in prayer; because it is obligatory therein upon the worshiper immediately due to the existence of evidence for immediacy, which is that it is obligated by what is among the acts of prayer, namely recitation, so it becomes attached to its acts and becomes a part of...
(1) Reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah in his Musannaf (1/368) from Ibn Umar.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Sajdah al-Tilawah (prostration of recitation). The author begins by presenting the cause (sabab) of this prostration: recitation of the verses of sajdah, which applies to the reciter by agreement and to the listener in the correct Hanafi view. Hearing alone is disputed; some scholars consider it a cause, but the Hanafi position is that the actual cause is recitation, and hearing is merely a condition for the application of recitation to the listener. The prostration is wajib (obligatory but not fard) because the evidence is speculative (zanni). It is not fard, as the proofs are not qat'i. Regarding timing: outside prayer, the obligation is on delay (tarakhi) according to Imam Muhammad and a narration from Abu Hanifa, and this is the chosen view of Abu Yusuf. Another narration from Abu Hanifa says it is immediate (faur). The preferred view is delay, based on the principle that an absolute command does not necessitate immediate action. However, if the verse is recited during prayer, the prostration becomes immediate for the one praying because it is connected to the acts of prayer. Conditions for this prostration include ritual purity (from both hadath and khabath), facing the qiblah, covering the private parts, and intention. Tayammum is not permitted without a valid excuse. The pillar (rukn) is placing the forehead on the ground.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that contains a command for prostration.
التلاوة (al-tilawah): Recitation of a verse of prostration, which is the cause (sabab) of the obligation of sajdah.
التراخي (al-tarakhi): The ruling that sajdah al-tilawah is due on delay, meaning it may be performed at any time before death, without immediate necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing sajdah al-tilawah outside of prayer?
A) It is fard and must be done immediately.
B) It is wajib and may be delayed.
C) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-tilawah is a wajib act with a single cause (recitation), a preferred delayed timing outside prayer, and immediate timing during prayer, with specific conditions and a single pillar.

The Ruling of Sujud al-Tilawah: Wajib, Not Fard
Explains the ruling of Sujud al-Tilawah with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies Sujud al-Tilawah as wajib rather than fard, and state the evidence from the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Tilawah is wajib because the evidence is zanni; fard requires qat'i proof.

This lesson focuses on the legal classification of Sujud al-Tilawah. The commentator explains that the verses of prostration fall into three categories, each indicating obligation, but because the indication is speculative (zanni), the ruling is obligation (wajib) rather than duty (fard). We will examine the proof structure and how it determines the hukm level.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Sujud al-Tilawah. According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib (obligatory). Note that the author explicitly contrasts wajib with fard.
The text says: 'وهو واجب' (it is obligatory).
2
Locate the classification of evidence
The author classifies the verses of prostration into three types: those with an explicit command, those showing disdain of disbelievers, and those showing prophets' compliance. Each indicates obligation, but the indication is not definitive.
The phrase 'دلالتها فيه ظنية' (its indication is speculative) is key.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
In Hanafi usul, a ruling based on speculative (zanni) evidence is wajib, not fard. Fard requires qat'i (definitive) proof. This is why the hukm is wajib.
This distinction is a defining feature of the Hanafi school.
4
Note the intra-madhhab agreement
All Hanafi authorities agree on wajib. The dispute is only on timing (fawr vs tarakhi), not on the basic obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

من إضافة الحكم إلى سببه، وهو الأصل في الإضافة؛ لأنها للاختصاص، وأقوى وجوهه اختصاص المسبب بالسبب لأنه حادث به كذا في الدراية»، وشرطها الطهارة عن الحدث والخبث، ولا يجوز التيمم لها بلا عذر يبيحه، واستقبال القبلة، وستر العورة والنية، وركنـهـا : وضع الجبهة على الأرض، وصفتها الوجوب عندنا على الفور في الصلاة، وعلى التراخي إن كانت غـيـر صلاتية، كما سنذكره وحكمها سقوط الواجب في الدنيا ونيل الثواب في العقبي. ثم شرع في بيان السبب، فقال: ( سَبَبُهُ التّلاوةُ، على التّالي ) اتفاقاً (وَ) على (السّامع في الصحيح) لأن التلاوة سبب بالإجماع؛ لأن السجدة تضاف إليها وتكرر بتكررها، وفي السماع خلاف، قيل: إنه سبب لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : السَّجْدَةُ عَلَى مَنْ سَمِعَهَا » (١)، وفي ( التاتارخانية : قال الصحابة: السجدة على من سمعها، كما قالوا: على من تلاها، والصحيح أن السبب التلاوة في حق السامع، والسماع شرط عمل التلاوة في حقه، كما في «الفتح» عن « (الكافي ) ، وفي ( التاتارخانية» عن « المحيط » : حتى لو تلاها الأصم ولم يسمع وجب عليه السجدة (وهو) أي: السجود للتلاوة (واجب) لأن آيــات السجود على ثلاثة أقسام: قسم فيه الأمر الصریح به وقسم تضمن استنکاف الكفرة حيث أمروا به، وقسم فيه حكاية امتثال الأنبياء به، وكل من الامتثال والاقتداء ومخالفة الكفرة واجب، إلا أن يدل دليل في معين على عدم لزومه، لكن دلالتها فيه ظنية، فكان الثابت الوجوب لا الفرض، ووجوبـه ( على التراخي) عند محمد، وهو رواية عن الإمام وهو المختار عند أبي يوسف وهو روايـة عــن الإمام: يجب على الفور، وجه القول بالتراخي أن دليل الوجوب مطلق عن تعيين الوقت، ومطلق الأمر لا يقتضي الفور ، فيجب في وقت غير معين، ويتعين ذلك بتعيينـه فـعـلا وإنمـا يـتـضيـق عـلـيـه الوجوب في آخر عمره، كما في سائر الواجبات الموسعة، ولا يجب نية تعيين السجدات، ولا يجب على المحتضر الإيصاء بها، وقيل: يجب كما في ( البحر ) ، عن ( القنية ) ، والوجوب على التراخي ( إن لم تكن) وجبت بتلاوة ( في الصَّلاة، فإنها تجب بها فيها على المصلي مضيقـاً لـقـيـام دليـل التضييق، وهو أنها وجبت بما هو من أفعال الصلاة وهو القراءة، فالتحقت بأفعالها وصارت جزءاً من
أجزائها، وإذا أخرها حتى طالت التلاوة تصير قضاء ويأثم؛ لأنها صارت ملحقة بنفس التـلاوة، بخلاف غير الصلوية فإنها تجب على التراخي على مـا هـو المختار، كما في «الفتح»، عــن البدائع ». (و) لكن (كُرة تأخيره) أي: السجود عن وقت التلاوة في الأصح، لا أن يكون الوقت مكروهاً كوقت طلوع الشمس، ذكر في بعض المواضع أنه إذا قرأها في الصلاة فتأخيرهـا مكـروه، وإن قرأها خارج الصلاة لا يكره تأخيره. وذكر الطحاوي أن تأخيرها مطلقاً مكروه وهو الأصح، ذا في « التجنيس»، ولكن تأخير غير الصلوية مكروه (تَنْزيهاً)؛ لأنه بطول الزمان قد ينساها، ولـو كانت الكراهة تحريمية لوجبت على الفور وليس كذلك، ولذا كره تحريماً تأخير الصلوية عن وقت القراءة. ( ويجب) السجود على مَنْ تلا آية وكان مسلماً مكلفاً طاهراً عن حيض ونفاس، ولـيـس نائماً ولا مقتدياً، ولم يتلها في ركوع ولا سجود ولا تشهد؛ لأن المؤتم محجـور عـلـيـه، والحجر في الركوع والسجود والتشهد عام يشمل المؤتم ،وغيره كما في ( التبيين ) ، وقال « المرغيناني» عليه السجود ويتأدى بالركوع والسجود الذي هو فيه كذا في شرح الديري»، فعليه يسجد لو كان تالياً في التشهد ، انتهى (وَلَو) تلاها (بالفارسية) اتفاقاً فهم أو لم يفهم؛ لأنه وإن كان لا تجوز بها الصلاة لغير العاجز عن العربية، على الصحيح فهو قرآن من وجه، وقد تلاها فتجب احتياطاً، كما في «البرهان»، و«البحر » ، ( وقراءة حرفِ السّجدة مع كلمةٍ قبلَهُ، أو بعدَهُ، منْ آيتـهـا ) توجب السجود على قول « أبي جعفر ، كما في الفتاوى الصغرى فيكون قراءة الحرف (كالآية) المقروءة بتمامها (في الصحيح)، وقيل: لا تجب إلا أن يقرأ أكثر آية السجدة مع كلمة مـــع حـرف السجدة، كما في حاشية ( الدرر والغرر » ، وفي المحيط : إذا قرأ حرف السجدة ومعها غيرها قبلها أو بعدها ما فيه أمر بالسجود سجد، وإن كانت دون ذلك لا يسجد. وفي «مختصر البحر » : لو قرأ وَاسْجُدْ العلق : ۱۹] وسكت ولم يقل واقترب ﴾ [الحاق : ١٩] يلزمه السجدة، وعن الشيخ الإمام أبـي عـلـي الدقاق رحمه الله فيمن سمع سجدة من قوم قرأ كل واحد منهم حرفاً ليـس عـلـيـه أن يسجد؛ لأنه لم يسمعها من تال، كما في ( الدراية » . وإذا قرأ آية السجدة بالهجاء لا يجب السجدة، لأنه لا يقال: قرأ القرآن، وإنما قرأ الهجاء ولو فعل ذلك في الصلاة لم يقطع، لأنها الحروف التي في القرآن، ولا تنوب عن القراءة؛ لأنه لم يقرأ القرآن كذا في ( التجنيس والمزيد » ، و فتاوی قاضي خان» (وآياتها أربع عشرة آيةً)، فتجب السجدة ( في الأَعْرَافِ عند قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ عِندَ رَبِّكَ لَا يَسْتَكْبِرُونَ عَنْ
Chapter of Sujud al-Tilawah. Its explanation: The recitation, upon the reciter, and upon the listener in the correct view, and it is obligatory with delay if it is not in prayer. Chapter of Sujud al-Tilawah. From attaching the ruling to its cause, and that is the principle in attribution; because it is for specialization, and the strongest of its aspects is the specialization of the effect by the cause because it occurs through it, as in al-Diraya. Its conditions are purity from hadath and khabath, and tayammum is not permissible for it without a permissible excuse, and facing the qibla, covering the private parts, and intention. Its pillar is placing the forehead on the ground. Its description: it is obligatory with us immediately in prayer, and with delay if it is non-prayer, as we will mention. Its ruling is the discharge of the obligation in this world and attainment of reward in the hereafter. Then he began to explain the cause, saying: Its cause is recitation, upon the reciter by agreement, and upon the listener in the correct view. Because recitation is a cause by consensus; for the prostration is attributed to it and repeated with its repetition. And concerning hearing there is disagreement. It is said that it is a cause due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'The prostration is upon the one who hears it.' And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: The Companions said: 'The prostration is upon the one who hears it,' as they said: 'upon the one who recites it.' And the correct view is that the cause is recitation with respect to the listener, and hearing is a condition for the operation of recitation with respect to him, as in al-Fath from al-Kafi. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Muhit: Even if a deaf person recited it and did not hear, prostration is obligatory upon him. And it, that is, the prostration for recitation, is obligatory. Because the verses of prostration are of three types: a type containing an explicit command for it, a type containing the disdain of the disbelievers where they were commanded with it, and a type containing the narration of the prophets' compliance with it. And each of compliance, following, and opposing the disbelievers is obligatory, unless a specific evidence indicates its non-necessity. But its indication thereof is speculative, so what is established is obligation, not duty. And its obligation is with delay according to Muhammad, and it is a narration from the Imam, and it is the chosen view according to Abu Yusuf, and it is a narration from the Imam: it is obligatory immediately. The reasoning for the view of delay is that the evidence of obligation is absolute without specification of time, and an absolute command does not require immediacy, so it is obligatory at an unspecified time, and it becomes specified by actual performance. And it only becomes restricted upon him in the last part of his life, as in all other extended obligations. And it is not obligatory to intend the specific prostrations, nor is it obligatory for a dying person to make a bequest for it, though it is said to be obligatory as in al-Bahr from al-Qunya. And the obligation with delay (if it was not) required by recitation (in prayer), for then it is obligatory upon the praying person immediately due to the presence of evidence requiring immediacy, which is that it became obligatory due to that which is among the acts of prayer, namely recitation, so it attaches to its acts and becomes a part of its parts. And if he delays it until the recitation lengthens, it becomes make-up and he sins, because it becomes annexed to the recitation itself, unlike non-prayer acts, for which it is obligatory with delay as is the chosen view, as in al-Fath from al-Bada'i. (And) but (its delay is disliked) i.e., the prostration after the time of recitation, as the most correct view, not that the time itself is disliked like the time of sunrise. It is mentioned in some places that if he recites it in prayer, delaying it is disliked, and if he recites it outside prayer, its delay is not disliked. And al-Tahawi mentioned that its delay is disliked absolutely, which is the most correct view, as in al-Tajnis. However, delaying non-prayer prostrations is disliked as a matter of tanzih, because over a long time he may forget it. If the dislike were prohibitive, it would require immediate performance, which is not the case. Hence, delaying prayer prostrations after the time of recitation is prohibitively disliked. (And it is obligatory) prostration upon one who recites a verse, being Muslim, accountable, pure from menstruation and postnatal bleeding, not sleeping, not following an imam, and not having recited it in bowing, prostration, or tashahhud. Because the follower is restricted, and the restriction in bowing, prostration, and tashahhud is general, including the follower and others, as in al-Tabyin. And al-Marghinani said: He must prostrate and it is fulfilled by the bowing and prostration he is in, as in Sharh al-Dayrī. So he should prostrate if he was reciting in tashahhud. End. (Even if) he recites it (in Persian) by agreement, whether he understands or not. Because even though prayer is not valid with it for one unable to speak Arabic, according to the correct view, it is still Quran in one respect, and he has recited it, so it becomes obligatory as a precaution, as in al-Burhan and al-Bahr. (And reciting) the letter of prostration with a word before or after it from its verse (makes prostration obligatory according to the view of Abu Ja'far, as in al-Fatawa al-Sughra. So reciting the letter is like the entire verse recited, as the correct view. And it is said: It is not obligatory unless he recites most of the prostration verse with a word along with the prostration letter, as in the gloss of al-Durar wa al-Ghurr. And in al-Muhit: If he recites the prostration letter and with it something else before or after it that contains a command to prostrate, he prostrates; if it is less than that, he does not prostrate. And in Mukhtasar al-Bahr: If he recites 'wasjud' [Surah al-‘Alaq: 19] and stops and does not say 'waqtarib' [Surah al-‘Alaq: 19], prostration is required of him. And from the shaykh al-imam Abu ‘Ali al-Daqqaq, may Allah have mercy on him, regarding one who hears a prostration from a group each of whom read a letter: he is not required to prostrate, because he did not hear it from a reciter, as in al-Diraya. And if he recites a prostration verse by spelling it, prostration is not required, because it is not said that he recited the Quran; rather he recited the spelling. And if he does that in prayer, it does not break the prayer, because these are letters that are in the Quran, but they do not substitute for recitation, because he did not recite the Quran, as in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid and Fatawa Qadi Khan. (And its verses are fourteen verses), so prostration is required (in al-A‘raf at His statement, exalted: 'Indeed, those who are with your Lord are not arrogant...')
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of Sujud al-Tilawah (prostration of recitation) from the matn. The commentator begins by stating the cause of the prostration: recitation (tilawah) is the cause for both the reciter and the listener, with a note that there is a difference of opinion on whether hearing is a cause. The preferred view (sahih) is that recitation is the cause for the listener, and hearing is a condition for the operation of the cause. The ruling is that Sujud al-Tilawah is wajib (obligatory), not fard, because the evidence from the verses is speculative (zanni), not definitive. It is obligatory upon the reciter and the listener who hears the recitation. The obligation is on delay (tarakhi) outside prayer, but immediate (fawr) within prayer. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad and a narration from Abu Hanifa say delay; Abu Yusuf and another narration from Abu Hanifa say immediate. The chosen view (mukhtar) is delay. However, if the prostration becomes due during prayer, it must be performed immediately because it attaches to the acts of prayer. Delaying the prostration after recitation is disliked (makruh tanzihan) outside prayer, but makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked) within prayer. The conditions for the obligation include: being Muslim, accountable (mukallaf), pure (not menstruating or postnatal), not sleeping, not following an imam, and not having recited the verse in ruku‘, sujud, or tashahhud. Reciting in Persian also necessitates prostration, even if the reader does not understand. Reciting only the word of prostration with a word before or after may also require prostration according to some scholars. The verses of prostration are fourteen in number, and the first one mentioned is in Surah al-A‘raf. The passage ends mid-verse.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Quran.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation; a ruling that carries reward for performance and sin for omission, but based on speculative evidence.
الفرض (al-fard): Duty; a ruling proven by qat'i evidence, e.g., five daily prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is Sujud al-Tilawah classified as wajib rather than fard?
A) Because the evidence from the Quran and hadith is speculative (zanni).
B) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran.
C) Because the Prophet never performed it.
D) Because it is only recommended by the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules Sujud al-Tilawah as wajib because the evidence, while sufficient for obligation, does not reach the level of certainty required for fard.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Fifteen Verses of Sajdah Tilawah in the Hanafi School
Listing surahs and verses where sajdah tilawah is wajib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the fifteen sajdah tilawah verses as recognized by the Hanafi school and explain the Hanafi position on the location of sajdah in Surah Fussilat, including the principle of ihtiyat used for tarjih.

Core Idea
There are fifteen wajib sajdah verses in the Qur'an according to the Hanafi school; the location in Surah Fussilat is disputed with the Shafi'i school.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text enumerates the specific verses where prostration becomes wajib upon recitation or hearing. It not only lists the verses but also addresses two important ikhtilafat: the reading of Surah an-Naml and, more significantly, the location of the sajdah in Surah Fussilat. The author uses the principle of ihtiyat (precaution) to argue for the Hanafi position, showcasing a key feature of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fifteen verses
Carefully read through the Arabic passage and compile a list of the fifteen surahs and the specific ayah where the sajdah occurs according to the Hanafi school.
The list includes: al-A'raf (206), ar-Ra'd (15), an-Nahl (48?), al-Isra' (107?), Maryam (58), al-Hajj (18), al-Furqan (60), an-Naml (verse after 25?), as-Sajdah (15), Sad (24 or 25), Fussilat (38), an-Najm (62), al-Inshiqaq (21), al-'Alaq (19). Verify with a reliable source.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on Surah an-Naml
The passage mentions that some scholars, like al-Farra', considered the sajdah in Surah an-Naml only wajib on the reading of al-Kisa'i with takhfif ('alla yasjudu'). Understand why the preferred view is that it is wajib on both readings (heavy and light).
The decisive factor is that both readings were written in the 'Uthmanic mushaf, so the obligation is established for both.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute on Surah Fussilat
Identify the two positions: Hanafi places the sajdah at verse 38, Shafi'i at verse 37. Examine the reasoning each school uses, especially the Hanafi argument from ihtiyat (precaution).
The Hanafi argument: if the sajdah were at 37, delaying to 38 is harmless; if at 38, prostrating before that is a deficiency. Hence precaution favors the later verse.
4
Apply the Hanafi tarjih mechanism
Understand why the Hanafi position is preferred (mufta bihi). The author cites the principle of ihtiyat when the companions differ, a common Hanafi methodology.
The ruling is not absolute but based on a weighted preference.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequence of the dispute: If one follows the Shafi'i position and prostrates at verse 37, is it valid according to the Hanafi school? According to the author, it would be a deficiency if done in prayer, but if outside prayer, it may be acceptable with different conditions.
The thamarah al-khilaf affects the validity of prayer if the sajdah is performed incorrectly.

عثمان لهلهلهله، كذا في « الدراية»، (و) في (السجدة) عند قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّمَا يُؤْمِنُ بِنَايَتِنَا الَّذِينَ إِذَا ذُكِرُوا بِهَا خَرُّوا سُجَّدًا وَسَبِّحُوا بِحَمْدِ رَبِّهِمْ وَهُمْ لَا وَحُسْنَ مَشَابِ ﴾ [جن]، وهذا هو الأولى مما قاله الزيلعي: تجب عند قوله تعالى: ﴿وَخَرَّ رَاكِعًا وَأَنَاب [ ج : ٢٤] ، وعند بعضهم عند قوله تعالى: ﴿وَحُسْنَ مشاب) [ق: ٢٥] لما نذكره (و) في (حم السَّجْدَةِ) عند قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنِ اسْتَكْبَرُوا فَالَّذِينَ عِندَ رَبِّكَ يُسَبِّحُونَ لَمُ بِاللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَهُمْ لَا يَسْتَمُونَ ﴾ [فصلت: ۳۸] من قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمِنْ ءَايَتِهِ الَّيْلُ، وَالنَّهَارُ وَالشَّمْسُ وَالْقَمَرُ لَا تَسْجُدُوا لِلشَّمْسِ وَلَا لِلْقَمَرِ وَاسْجُدُوا لِلَّهِ الَّذِي خَلَقَهُنَّ إِن كُنتُمْ إِيَّاهُ تَعْبُدُونَ فَإِنِ اسْتَكْبَرُوا فَالَّذِينَ عِندَ رَبِّكَ يُسَبِّحُونَ لَهُ بِالَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَهُمْ لَا يَسْتَمُونَ ) [فصلت، وهذا على مذهبنا، وهو المروي عن ابن عباس ووائل بن حجر، وعند الشافعي رحمه الله عـنـد قوله تعالى: (إن كُنتُمْ إِيَّاهُ تَعْبُدُونَ ﴾ [فصلت : ٣٧] وهو مذهب علي، ومروي عن ابن مسعود وابــن عمر، ورجح أئمتنا الأول أخذاً بالاحتياط عند اختلاف مذاهب الصحابة ، فإن السجدة لو وجبت عنـد قوله تعالى: تَعْبُدُونَ ﴾ [فصلت : ٣٧] فالتأخير إلى قوله تعالى: لَا يَسْتَمُونَ ﴾ [فصلت : ۳۸] لا يضر، ويخرج عن الواجب، ولو وجبت عند قوله تعالى: لَا يَسْتَمُونَ ﴾ [فصلت : ٣٨] لكانت السجدة المؤداة قبله حاصلة قبل وجوبها ووجود سبب وجوبها، فيوجب نقصاناً في الصلاة لـو كـانـت صلاتية، ولا نقص فيما قلناه أصلاً، وهذا هو إمارة التبحر في الفقه (۱) كذا في ( البحر )، عن « البدائع». انتهى. ففيما قلته قبله كذلك في (ص)، وإلا يلزمنا التناقض، وهذا هو الوجه الذي وعدنا به)، (و) في (النَّجْمِ) عند قوله تعالى: ﴿ أَفَمَنْ هَذَا الْحَدِيثِ تَعْجَبُونَ ) وَتَضْحَكُونَ وَلَا تَكُونَ وَأَنتُمْ سَمِدُونَ فَاسْجُدُوا لِلَّهِ واعْبُدُوا الي )، (و) في (إذا السماء انْشَقَّتْ) عند قوله تعالى: (فَمَا لَهُمْ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ ) وَإِذَا قُرِئَ عَلَيْهِمُ الْقُرْمَانُ لَا يَسْجُدُونَ ) الات: ٢١)، (و) في ) [ الانشقق : ۲۱]، (و) في (اقرأ) باسم ربك عند قوله تعالى: كَلَّا لَا تُطِعْهُ وَاسْجُدْ وَاقْتَرِب [العلق : ۱۹].
And in ar-Ra'd, an-Nahl, al-Isra', Maryam, the first of al-Hajj, al-Furqan, an-Naml, as-Sajdah, Sad, and Ha-Mim as-Sajdah. ... (listing each verse with the specific ayah where sajdah is performed). And in an-Najm at His saying: 'Then are you amazed at this discourse? And you laugh and do not weep, while you are heedless? So prostrate to Allah and worship [Him].' And in [Surah] 'When the sky splits asunder' at His saying: 'So what is [the matter] with them that they do not believe? And when the Quran is recited to them, they do not prostrate?' and in [Surah] 'Iqra' bismi rabbika' at His saying: 'No! Do not obey him. But prostrate and draw near [to Allah].'
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage is a detailed listing of the fifteen verses of sajdah tilawah in the Qur'an according to the Hanafi school. The author specifies the exact surah and ayat where prostration is wajib. He includes a discussion of the ikhtilaf regarding Surah an-Naml (the recitation of al-Kisa'i) and a more extensive dispute about Surah Fussilat (Ha-Mim as-Sajdah). In the latter, the Hanafi position places the sajdah at the verse 'فَإِنِ اسْتَكْبَرُوا...' (41:38), while Imam al-Shafi'i places it at 'إِن كُنتُمْ إِيَّاهُ تَعْبُدُونَ' (41:37). The author argues that the Hanafi position is preferable because it avoids a potential deficiency if one were to prostrate before the obligation arises. The listing also includes Surah Sad, where the sajdah is at the verse mentioning Dawud's prostration, not at the earlier 'رَاكِعًا'. The passage concludes with the last three surahs: an-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and al-'Alaq.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): The prostration that is wajib upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Qur'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, at which verse does the sajdah tilawah occur in Surah Fussilat (Ha-Mim as-Sajdah)?
A) At verse 37: 'إِن كُنتُمْ إِيَّاهُ تَعْبُدُونَ'
B) At verse 38: 'فَإِنِ اسْتَكْبَرُوا فَالَّذِينَ عِندَ رَبِّكَ يُسَبِّحُونَ لَهُ بِاللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَهُمْ لَا يَسْأَمُونَ'
C) At verse 36: 'وَإِمَّا يَنزَغَنَّكَ مِنَ الشَّيْطَانِ نَزْغٌ فَاسْتَعِذْ بِاللَّهِ'
D) At verse 39: 'وَمِنْ ءَايَاتِهِ أَنْ تَقُومَ السَّمَاءُ وَالْأَرْضُ بِأَمْرِهِ'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes 15 verses of sajdah tilawah, and for Surah Fussilat, the sajdah is at verse 38 based on the principle of ihtiyat.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Obligation of Sajdah upon the Listener and Exceptions
Stating the obligation of sajdah on the listener and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general ruling of sajdah tilawah for the listener and identify the exceptions along with their legal reasons.

Core Idea
Hearing a sajdah verse obligates prostration even without intention, except for women in menses/postpartum and the imam/follower from a follower's recitation.

This passage from Nur al-Idah establishes the rule that anyone who hears an ayah sajdah must prostrate, whether they intended to listen or not. The author then carves out specific exceptions. Understanding these exceptions helps clarify the boundaries of the obligation and the conditions for its performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hearing an ayah sajdah. The ruling is that sajdah becomes wajib on the hearer.
This is the default rule.
2
Note the scope of the ruling
The obligation applies even if the listener did not intend to hear. Intent is not a condition.
Based on the practice of the Companions.
3
List the exceptions
Three exceptions: menstruating woman, woman in postpartum bleeding, and the imam and follower when hearing from another follower.
4
Understand the rationale for each exception
For ha'idh/nufasa': lack of ritual purity. For imam/muqtadi: the imam's recitation takes precedence; a follower's recitation does not obligate the imam or other followers.
The exception is due to the structure of congregational prayer.
5
Apply the ruling
Consider scenarios: a woman in haidh hears the verse; a follower in prayer hears another follower recite a sajdah verse. Determine obligation based on the exceptions.
Practice with examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب السجود على مَنْ سمعَ، وإنْ لم يَقْصِدِ السَّمَاعَ، إلا الحائض، والنَّفَسَاءَ، والإمام والمقتدِيَ به بالسَّماعِ مِنْ مُقْتَدِ.
And prostration is obligatory upon whoever hears, even if he did not intend to hear, except the menstruating woman, the woman in postpartum bleeding, and the imam and the one following him (muqtadi) by hearing from a follower (muqtadi).
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (hukm) stating the general obligation of sajdah tilawah upon anyone who hears the recitation of a sajdah verse, whether they intended to listen or not. This is based on the practice of the Companions (Uthman, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas) who made it obligatory on the reciter and listener without distinction, and on the verse 'فَمَا لَهُمْ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ...' which rebukes those who do not prostrate when the Quran is recited to them. The author then lists three exceptions: (1) a menstruating woman, (2) a woman in postpartum bleeding (nifas), and (3) the imam and the muqtadi (follower in prayer) when the recitation is heard from another muqtadi (i.e., not directly from the imam). The reason for the first two exceptions is that they are not in a state of ritual purity required for prayer, and sajdah tilawah is like a prayer. The third exception is because the imam's recitation is more authoritative; he is not obligated to prostrate for a follower's recitation. The text also notes that the sajdah is obligatory on a person in janabah (major impurity) because they are prohibited from reciting but not entirely barred from worship; they can still prostrate.

Key Terms
مُقْتَدٍ (muqtadin): A follower in congregational prayer who recites behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is excepted from the obligation of sajdah tilawah upon hearing a sajdah verse?
A) A person in a state of major impurity (junub)
B) A menstruating woman
C) A child who has not reached puberty
D) A person performing the ritual bath (ghusl)

Key Takeaway
Hearing a sajdah verse obligates sajdah tilawah, even without intention, except for those in menstruation/postpartum bleeding and the imam/follower when the recitation comes from another follower.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Obligation of Sajdah al-Tilawah on the Hearer and Exceptions
Explains obligation of prostration of recitation on hearer and who is exempt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-tilawah for the hearer, identify the exceptions, and explain the dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding the verse location.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib upon anyone who hears the verses in Arabic, even unintentionally, except for specific exemptions.

This lesson clarifies the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) upon the hearer. The Hanafi school holds that merely hearing the sajdah verses in Arabic triggers the wajib, regardless of intent or understanding. However, certain individuals are exempt due to their state. The passage also addresses a well-known ikhtilaf with the Shafi'i school concerning the exact verse of prostration in Surah Fussilat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm and its basis
Note that the text declares sajdah al-tilawah 'wajib' on the hearer. This is not fard but a confirmed obligation (wajib) derived from the practice of the Companions and the Quranic verse blaming those who do not prostrate.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, due to the zanni nature of the evidence.
2
Recognize the generalization
The obligation applies to 'whoever hears the Arabic recitation, even if he did not intend to listen'. This includes understanding or not, Muslim or disbeliever (as hearer), but the performer must be Muslim.
3
Note the exceptions
The text exempts the menstruating woman (ha'id), the postpartum woman (nafasaa'), and the imam and follower when hearing from a follower. Understand the rationale: lack of ritual purity for the women, and the follower's recitation being legally ineffective for the imam/follower.
Hearing from a disbeliever or a discerning child still obligates the sajdah.
4
Understand the dispute on Surah Fussilat
The Hanafi school places the sajdah at verse 38 ('and they never tire'), while the Shafi'i school places it at verse 37 ('if you worship Him'). The Hanafis follow narrations from Ibn Abbas and Wail ibn Hujr and apply the principle of caution (ihtiyat).
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: Hanafis prostrate after verse 38, Shafi'is after verse 37.
5
Apply the Hanafi position with caution
The Hanafi reasoning: if the sajdah were at verse 37, delaying to verse 38 does not harm; if it were at verse 38, performing earlier would be invalid. Thus caution dictates placing it at verse 38.
This reasoning is called 'ihitiyat' and reflects mastery in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنَّجْمِ، وَانْشَقَّتْ واقْرَأْ. ويجب السجود على مَنْ سمعَ، وإنْ لم يَقْصِدِ السَّماعَ، إلا الحائض، والنَّفَسَاءَ، والإمام والمقتدِيَ به بالسَّماعِ مِنْ مُقْتَدِ.. وَالنَّهَارُ وَالشَّمْسُ وَالْقَمَرُ لَا تَسْجُدُوا لِلشَّمْسِ وَلَا لِلْقَمَرِ وَاسْجُدُوا لِلَّهِ الَّذِي خَلَقَهُنَّ إِن كُنتُمْ إِيَّاهُ تعبدُونَ فَإِنِ اسْتَكْبَرُوا فَالَّذِينَ عِندَ رَبِّكَ يُسَبِّحُونَ لَهُ بِالَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَهُمْ لَا يَسْتَمُونَ ) [فصلت، وهذا على مذهبنا، وهو المروي عن ابن عباس ووائل بن حجر، وعند الشافعي رحمه الله عـنـد قوله تعالى: (إن كُنتُمْ إِيَّاهُ تَعْبُدُونَ ﴾ [فَضَلَ : ٣٧] وهو مذهب علي، ومروي عن ابن مسعود وابــن عمر، ورجح أئمتنا الأول أخذاً بالاحتياط عند اختلاف مذاهب الصحابة ، فإن السجدة لو وجبت عنــد قوله تعالى: تَعْبُدُونَ ﴾ [فصلت : ٣٧] فالتأخير إلى قوله تعالى: لَا يَسْتَمُونَ ﴾ [فَضَلَتْ : ۳۸] لا يضر، ويخرج عن الواجب، ولو وجبت عند قوله تعالى: لَا يَسْتَمُونَ ﴾ [فصلت : ٣٨] لكانت السجدة المؤداة قبله حاصلة قبل وجوبها ووجود سبب وجوبها، فيوجب نقصاناً في الصلاة لـو كـانـت صلاتية، ولا نقص فيما قلناه أصلاً، وهذا هو إمارة التبحر في الفقه (۱) كذا في ( البحر ) ، عن « البدائع». انتهى. ففيما قلته قبله كذلك في (ص)، وإلا يلزمنا التناقض، وهذا هو الوجه الذي وعدنا به) ، (و) في (النَّجْمِ) عند قوله تعالى: ﴿ أَفَمَنْ هَذَا الْحَدِيثِ تَعْجَبُونَ ) وَتَضْحَكُونَ وَلَا تَكُونَ وَأَنتُمْ سَمِدُونَ فَاسْجُدُوا لِلَّهِ واعْبُدُوا الي )، (و) في (إذا السماء انْشَقَّتْ) عند قوله تعالى: (فَمَا لَهُمْ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ ) وَإِذَا قُرِئَ عَلَيْهِمُ الْقُرْمَانُ لَا يَسْجُدُونَ ) الات: ٢١)، (و) في ) [ الانشقق : ۲۱]، (و) في (اقرأ) باسم ربك عند قوله تعالى: كَلَّا لَا تُطِعْهُ وَاسْجُدْ وَاقْتَرِب [العلق : ۱۹]. ويجب السجود على مَنْ سمع) التلاوة العربية (وإن لم يَقْصِدِ السَّماعَ)، فهم أو لم يفهم لما روي عن عثمان وعلي وابن مسعود وابن عباس، أنهم أوجبوا على التالي والسامع من غير فصل، وكفى بهم قدوة، وقد قال تعالى: ﴿فَمَا لَهُمْ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ وَإِذَا قُرِئَ عَلَيْهِمُ الْقُرْءَانُ لَا يَسْجُدُونَ ) [ الانشقاقل ] ، ذم السامعين على ترك السجود مـن غـيـر فصل، (إلا) أنـه استثنى (الحائض، والنُّفَسَاءَ) فلا يجب عليهما بسماعهما ، كما لا يجب عليهما بتلاوتهما؛ لأن السجدة ركن الصلاة وليستا بأهل لها، وتجب بالسماع منهما ومن الجنب، كمـا تجـب عـلـى الجنـب لأنهم منهيون عن القراءة لا محجورون، كذا في « التبيين » ، وفي «مجمع الـروايــات » : والقـدر الـذي تجب به السجدة مباح لهما على الصحيح دون المقتدي. انتهى. وكذا تجب بسماعه من كافر وصغير مميز. (وَ) إلا (الإمام، والمقتدِي  ِبهِ) فلا تجب عليهما ( بالسَّماعِ مِنْ مُقْتَد) بالإمام السامع، أو بإمام (۱) أي: علامة على اتساع علم قائله وكثرته. ط.
(۲) لما ذكره قبل قليل من قوله لما نذكره.
And [the prostration of] An-Najm, and Inshiqaq, and Iqra'. And prostration is obligatory upon whoever hears, even if he did not intend to listen, except the menstruating woman, the postpartum woman, and the imam and the one following him due to hearing from a follower. And the day and the sun and the moon: do not prostrate to the sun nor to the moon, but prostrate to Allah who created them, if you worship Him. But if they are arrogant, then those who are with your Lord glorify Him by night and day, and they never tire. [Fussilat: 37-38] This is our madhhab, and it is narrated from Ibn Abbas and Wail ibn Hujr. According to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, it is at His statement: 'If you worship Him' [Fussilat: 37] and it is the madhhab of Ali, and narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar. Our imams preferred the first opinion out of caution when the opinions of the Companions differed. For if the prostration were obligatory at His statement: 'you worship Him', then delaying it to His statement: 'they never tire' does no harm, and the obligation is fulfilled. But if it were obligatory at His statement: 'they never tire', then the prostration performed before it would have occurred before its obligation and before the existence of its cause, which would cause a deficiency in prayer if it were a prayer prostration, whereas there is no deficiency in what we say at all. This is a sign of mastery in fiqh. It is in 'al-Bahr' from 'al-Bada'i'. End. So in what I said before, similarly in (S), otherwise contradiction would be necessary. This is the aspect we promised. And in An-Najm at His statement: 'Do you then wonder at this statement? And you laugh and do not weep, while you are heedless? So prostrate to Allah and worship' [Najm: 59-62]. And in Idha al-sama' unshaqqat at His statement: 'Then what is the matter with them that they believe not? And when the Quran is recited to them, they prostrate not?' [Inshiqaq: 20-21]. And in Iqra' at His statement: 'Nay! Do not obey him. But prostrate and draw near' [Alaq: 19]. And prostration is obligatory upon whoever hears the Arabic recitation, even if he did not intend to listen, whether he understood or not, because it is narrated from Uthman, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Abbas that they obligated it upon the reciter and the hearer without delay, and they are sufficient as leaders. And Allah said: 'Then what is the matter with them that they believe not? And when the Quran is recited to them, they prostrate not?' [Inshiqaq: 20-21], blaming the hearers for leaving prostration without delay. Except that he exempted the menstruating woman and the postpartum woman; prostration is not obligatory upon them by hearing, just as it is not obligatory upon them by recitation, because prostration is a pillar of prayer and they are not fit for it. And it is obligatory by hearing from them and from the junub, just as it is obligatory upon the junub, because they are prohibited from recitation but not restricted. This is in 'al-Tabyin'. In 'Majma' al-Riwayat': the amount which necessitates prostration is permissible for them according to the correct view, except for the follower. End. And likewise it is obligatory by hearing from a disbeliever and a discerning child. And except the imam and the one following him: it is not obligatory upon them due to hearing from a follower of the imam who heard it or from an imam.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh of Nur al-Idah discusses the rulings of sajdah al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). The author first mentions the surahs that contain verses of prostration: Surah al-Najm (53), Surah al-Inshiqaq (84), and Surah al-Alaq (96). He then adds the verse in Surah Fussilat (41:37-38) and explains the Hanafi position regarding which part of the verse triggers the obligation. According to the Hanafi school, the sajdah is at the statement 'وَهُمْ لَا يَسْتَمُونَ' (and they never tire), while Imam al-Shafi'i holds it to be at 'إِن كُنتُمْ إِيَّاهُ تَعْبُدُونَ' (if you worship Him). The Hanafis prefer their view based on the practice of Companions and out of caution (ihtiyat). The passage then establishes that sajdah al-tilawah is wajib upon anyone who hears the recitation of these verses in Arabic, even if they did not intend to listen. This obligation is proven by the practice of the Companions (Uthman, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas) who obligated it without delay, and by the Quranic verse blaming those who do not prostrate when the Quran is recited. Exceptions are made for menstruating and postpartum women, for whom the sajdah is not required because they are not in a state of ritual purity and sajdah is akin to a prayer act. The imam and the follower are also excepted when they hear it from a follower, as the follower's recitation has no legal effect in prayer. The passage also notes that hearing from a disbeliever or a discerning child still obligates the sajdah.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdah al-tilawah): Prostration required upon reciting or hearing specific verses of the Quran.
الحائض (al-ha'id): Menstruating woman; exempt from the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah.
النفساء (al-nafasaa'): Postpartum woman; exempt for the same reason as menstruating woman.
مقتد (muqtadi): Follower in prayer; his recitation does not obligate sajdah upon the imam or other followers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A menstruating woman
B) A postpartum woman
C) A disbeliever
D) The imam when hearing from his follower

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib upon hearing the verses in Arabic, with specific exemptions; the Hanafi position on the Fussilat sajdah is adopted out of caution.

Sajdah al-Tilawah: Imam/Follower, Persian Recitation, and Hearing from Sleeping Person
Continues rulings on sajdah for imam/follower, Persian recitation, and hearing from asleep or insane

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for sajdah al-tilawah in three scenarios: imam/follower hearing from a non-participant, hearing in Persian, and hearing from a sleeping or insane person, and identify the relied-upon positions and underlying reasoning.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilawah obligates after prayer when hearing from an outsider; Persian requires understanding; sleeping person's recitation triggers obligation.

This passage delves into nuanced cases of sajdah al-tilawah, clarifying when and how the prostration is performed. It addresses the scenario where the imam and followers hear a sajdah verse from someone not in their congregation, the effect of hearing the verse recited in Persian translation, and the status of hearing from a person who is asleep, insane, or even a bird. Understanding these rulings requires careful attention to the conditions of the reciter and hearer, as well as the school's reliance on the dominant transmission (zahir al-riwayah) and the adopted opinion (mu'tamad).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling for Each Scenario
For each of the three cases (imam/follower hearing from outsider, Persian recitation, hearing from sleeper/insane), state the hukm: is sajdah wajib? If wajib, when is it performed (during or after prayer)?
Use the text to extract the specific ruling per scenario.
2
Locate the Dalil (Reasoning)
Identify the legal reasoning (ta'lil) provided for each ruling. Look for phrases like 'li-tahaqquqi al-sabab' (because the cause is realized) or 'li-anna' (because).
The text uses cause (sabab) and prevention (mani') reasoning.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the reasoning proves the ruling. For example, why does hearing from a non-participant obligate after prayer but not during? Why does Persian require understanding? Why does a sleeping person's recitation count?
The underlying principle is that the sajdah is a prayer-related act that cannot be done during fard prayer if it disrupts the sequence.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Identify the disagreements: between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on Persian, and between the two (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) and Muhammad on the follower's recitation effect, and the differing verifications on sleeping/insane.
The text mentions 'wa ikhtalafa al-tashih' and names specific imams.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih (Mufta Bihi)
Determine which position is relied upon (mu'tamad) or correct (sahih) according to the text and later authorities like al-Khulasah and Qadi Khan.
The text explicitly uses 'ala al-mu'tamad' for Persian and 'as-sahih' for sleeping person.

And if they (the imam and followers) hear it from someone else, they prostrate after the prayer. And if they prostrate during it, it does not suffice them, and their prayer is not invalidated according to the apparent narration. And it is obligatory by hearing the Persian recitation if he understands it, according to the relied-upon opinion. And the verification differed regarding its obligation by hearing from a sleeping person or an insane person. And this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, said: It is obligatory upon them, and they prostrate it after finishing the prayer, because the cause (recitation and hearing) is realized, and there is no prevention after finishing it, unlike the state of prayer because it leads to reversing the place of leadership or recitation. And thus it is obligatory upon one who hears it while not in their prayer. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), there is no legal effect for the follower's recitation just as his forgetfulness is prevented from recitation, and there is no effect for the action of one under restriction. The restriction is established for those in prayer, so it does not extend beyond them. So if he hears while not in prayer, he prostrates according to the most correct view, as in 'Majma' al-Riwayat'. And there is no basis for prostrating after finishing, because it is a prayer-related act and is not made up outside of it, just as if the imam recited it and did not prostrate until after finishing. And if they hear it from someone else, i.e., other than the follower, they prostrate after the prayer, because the cause is realized and the prevention from doing it in prayer is removed, since it is not a prayer act. And if they prostrate during it, it does not suffice them because it is deficient due to the prohibition; they must repeat it to perform it completely, and their prayer is not invalidated by prostrating in it according to the apparent narration. This is correct because adding one prostration does not nullify the sacredness, as seen in one who catches up with the imam in prostration: he prostrates with him, not counted, and his sacredness is not nullified. In the narration of al-Nawadir, it nullifies the prayer, but it is not correct. It is said that it is Muhammad's opinion, but according to the two, he does not repeat. And it is obligatory by hearing the recitation in Persian if he understands it according to the relied-upon opinion. This is according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And according to Abu Hanifa, it is obligatory upon him even if he does not understand its meaning if he is informed that it is a verse of prostration. The difference in this matter is based on whether the Quran in Persian is considered Quran in every respect or in some respect. According to the opinion that permits prayer with it, it is Quran in every respect. According to the opinion he retracted, it is Quran in some respect, so that it is not permissible for one who knows Arabic. So accordingly, he is not a hearer of the Quran in every respect if he does not understand, and if he understands, he is a hearer in some respect, so it becomes obligatory as a precaution. Thus in al-Burhan. And verification differed regarding its obligation upon the hearer by hearing from a sleeping person or an insane person. Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that prostration is not due by hearing from an insane person, sleeping person, or bird, because the cause is hearing a valid recitation, and valid recitation requires discernment, which is lacking. In al-Khulasah: if he hears it from a bird, it is not obligatory, that is the chosen view. From a sleeping person, the correct view is that it is obligatory. Kamal said that. Qadi Khan said: It is obligatory upon one upon whom prayer is obligatory, if he recites a verse of prostration or hears it from someone upon whom prayer is obligatory or not obligatory due to menstruation, postpartum, disbelief, minority, or insanity. And it is not obligatory by hearing it from a bird. If he hears from a sleeping person, they differed, and the correct view is obligation. End.
