Sajda al-Tilawa After Hearing from an Imam
Explaining when to perform sajda outside prayer after hearing from imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for sajda al-tilawa when hearing from an imam in various scenarios and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding following in a different rak'ah.

Core Idea
Sajda al-tilawa is wajib, but following the imam in the same rak'ah changes the obligation.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the nuanced rulings for sajda al-tilawa when hearing the verse from an imam outside or inside prayer. The key distinction hinges on whether you follow the imam in the same rak'ah. If you do not, the sajda is wajib outside; if you do, it drops or is performed with the imam. The text also explores an intra-Hanafi difference about whether following in a different rak'ah still obligates sajda.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
List the possible cases of hearing a sajda verse from an imam: not following at all, following in a different rak'ah, following before the imam's sajda in the same rak'ah, and following after the imam's sajda in the same rak'ah.
The text divides these explicitly.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
According to the most apparent opinion (al-azhar), if you do not follow or follow in a different rak'ah, you perform sajda outside the prayer. If you follow before the imam's sajda, you perform it with him. If you follow after his sajda in the same rak'ah, no sajda is required.
The ruling for following in a different rak'ah is the contested point.
3
Locate the dispute
Al-Atabi holds that following in a different rak'ah drops the sajda entirely because the hearing becomes prayer-related (salawiyya). The author presents this as a weaker view.
This is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the reasoning
The dispute centers on the cause (sabab) of sajda: is it recitation or hearing? The author maintains recitation is the cause, so the sajda remains wajib outside. Al-Atabi focuses on hearing, which is based on the prayer recitation, making it salawiyya.
Understanding the cause is key to resolving the dispute.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author favors performing sajda outside (al-azhar) as a precaution, citing al-Burhan. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Precaution (ihtiyat) supports the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولَوْ سَمِعَ من إمام، فلم يأتم به، أو انتم في ركعة أخرى، سجد خارج الصَّلاةِ، فِي الأَظْهَرِ. وَإِنِ اثْتَمَّ قبلَ سجود إمامه لها سَجَدَ معه . ، وَإِنِ اقْتَدَى به بعد سجودِها في ركعتها، صار مُدْرِكاً لها حُكْمَا، فلا يسجدُها أصلاً. ولم تُقضَ الصَّلاتيّةُ خارجها.
القياس، فإنه لا تـ ترجيح للخفي لخفائه ولا للظاهر لظهوره، بل يرجع في الترجيح إلى ما اقترن بهما من المعاني. فمتى قوي الخفي أخذوا به أو الظاهر أخذوا به، غير أن استقرارهم أوجب قلــة الظاهر المتبادل بالنسبة إلى الخفي المعارض، فلذا حصروا مواضع تقديم القياس على الاستحسان في بضعة عشر موضعاً، تعرف في الأصول، هذا أحدها ولا حصر لمقابله. انتهى. ولو سمع آية السجدة من إمـام فلم يأتم به أصلاً، أو انتم به في ركعة أخرى، غير التي تلى الآية فيها وسجد لها الإمام، سجد السامع سجوداً خارج الصَّلاةِ؛ لتحقق السبب، وهو التلاوة ممن ليس بمحجـور عـلـيـه، أو السماع مـن تلاوة صحيحة، على اختلاف المشايخ في السبب وقوله في الأَظْهَر متعلق بالمسألة الأخيرة، وقال العتابي: أشار في بعض النسخ إلى أنها تسقط عنه بالاقتداء في غير ركعتها؛ لأن السماع بناء على التلاوة، وقد وجبت في الصلاة، فكانت السجدة صلوية فلم تؤد خارجها، ووجه ما قلنا: أنهم لما اختلفوا في السبب، هل هو السماع أو التلاوة؟ نظرنا إلى أنه التلاوة وهو الصحيح، كما قدمناه لم تؤد خارجها، ولو نظرنا إلى السماع تؤدى خارجها، فالاحتياط أن تؤدى خارجها لا فيها صوناً لها وللصلاة عن الزائد، كما في البرهان. وإنِ اثْتَمَّ السامع قبل سجود إمامه لها سَجَدَ معه لوجود السبب في حقـه وعــدم المانع، قاله الزيلعي ولأنه لو لم يسمعها بأن أخفاها الإمام سجدها معه فهنا أولى، كما في العناية. وإنِ اقْتَدَى السامع به أي : بالإمام بعد سجودِها وكان اقتداؤه في ركعتها، صار السامع مُدْرِكـاً لها أي: للسجدة حُكْماً، بإدراكه ركعتها فيصير مؤدياً لها حكماً، فلا يسجدها أصلاً باتفاق الروايات؛ لأنه لا يمكنه أن يسجدها في الصلاة لما فيه من مخالفة الإمام ولا بعد فراغه منها لأنها صلوية، ولم تُقضَ الصَّلاتيّة خارجها؛ لأن لها مزية لتأديها في حرمة الصلاة فلا تتأدى بالناقص، وهذا إذا لم تفسد الصلاة بغير الحيض فيها، أما لو فسدت فعليه السجدة خارجها، لأنها لما فسدت بقي مجرد التلاوة، فلم تكن صلوية، ولو أداها فيها ثم فسدت لا يعيد السجدة؛ لأنه بالمفسد لا يفسد جميع أجزاء الصلاة، وإنما يفسد الجزء المقارن فيمنع البناء عليه، والحائض تسقط عنها السجدة بالحيض في الصلاة، كذا في البحر. قلت: ومثلها النفساء، لأن حكمها في الصلاة واحد. انتهى.
And if he heard from an imam and did not follow him, or he followed him in another rak'ah, he performs sajda outside the prayer, according to the most apparent opinion. And if he followed him before his imam's sajda, he performs sajda with him. And if he followed him after his sajda in its rak'ah, he becomes a perceiver of it [the sajda] legally, so he does not perform it at all. And the prayer-related sajda is not made up outside it.
Analogy: for there is no preference for the hidden due to its hiddenness nor for the apparent due to its obviousness; rather preference is given to what is accompanied by meanings. So when the hidden is stronger, they adopt it, or the apparent, they adopt it, except that their establishment necessitated the scarcity of the apparent in exchange relative to the opposing hidden. Thus they restricted the places where analogy is preferred over istihsan to about a dozen places, known in usul. This is one of them, and there is no limit to its counterpart. End. And if he heard the verse of sajda from an imam and did not follow him at all, or he followed him in another rak'ah, other than the one in which he recited the verse and performed sajda, the hearer performs sajda outside the prayer due to the realization of the cause, which is the recitation from one not under restriction, or the hearing from a valid recitation, according to the difference among the mashayikh regarding the cause. And his saying 'in the most apparent' relates to the last issue. Al-Atabi said: some copies indicate that it drops from him by following in other than its rak'ah; because the hearing is based on the recitation, and it had become obligatory in the prayer, so the sajda is prayer-related and thus not performed outside it. The basis of what we say: when they differed over the cause—is it hearing or recitation? We look to the fact that it is recitation, which is correct, as we have established; it is not performed outside it. If we look to hearing, it would be performed outside it. So the precaution is to perform it outside it, not inside, to preserve it and the prayer from excess, as in al-Burhan. And if the hearer followed before his imam's sajda for it, he performs sajda with him due to the presence of the cause in his case and the absence of prevention, as al-Zayla'i said, and because if he had not heard it—the imam having concealed it—he would perform sajda with him; even more so here, as in al-Inayah. And if the hearer followed him after his sajda, and his following was in its rak'ah, the hearer becomes a perceiver of it legally, by perceiving its rak'ah, thus becomes a performer of it legally, so he does not perform it at all by consensus of the narrations; because he cannot perform it in the prayer due to opposing the imam, nor after finishing from it because it is prayer-related. And the prayer-related sajda is not made up outside it because it has an advantage of being performed within the sanctity of the prayer, so it cannot be performed by a deficient act. This is when the prayer is not invalidated by something other than menstruation. If it is invalidated, then he must perform the sajda outside it, because when it was invalidated, only the mere recitation remains, so it was not prayer-related. If he performed it inside and then it was invalidated, he does not repeat the sajda; because the invalidator does not invalidate all parts of the prayer, only the part that coincides, preventing building upon it. The menstruating woman has the sajda dropped by menstruation in the prayer, as in al-Bahr. I say: and similarly the woman in post-partum bleeding, because her ruling regarding prayer is one. End.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding sajda al-tilawa upon hearing from an imam. The author explains several scenarios. First, if one hears the verse of sajda from an imam but does not follow him at all, or follows him in a different rak'ah than the one in which the imam recited and performed sajda, then the hearer must perform sajda outside the prayer according to the most apparent opinion (al-azhar). The reason is that the cause (sabab) for sajda is the recitation itself, not just hearing, and the recitation is valid. However, there is a difference among the mashayikh whether the cause is recitation or hearing. The correct view is that it is recitation, so if one hears a valid recitation, sajda is wajib. If the hearer follows the imam in the same rak'ah but before the imam performs sajda, then he performs sajda with the imam. If he follows after the imam's sajda but still in that same rak'ah, he becomes a 'mudrik' of the sajda legally, meaning he is considered to have performed it by virtue of catching the rak'ah, so he does not perform it at all. This is consistent across narrations. The prayer-related sajda (salatiyya) is not made up outside the prayer because it has a special merit of being performed in the prayer. If the prayer is invalidated (e.g., due to a major impurity), then the sajda must be performed outside because the recitation remains. If a menstruating woman hears the verse during her period, the sajda falls from her, as does the ruling for a woman in post-partum bleeding. The passage also includes a discussion on qiyas and istihsan, noting that this case is one of the few where qiyas is preferred over istihsan, but the details are in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration.
صلوية (salawiyya): An act that is connected to the prayer, thus cannot be performed outside it.
مدرك (mudrik): A latecomer who catches the imam in a rak'ah and is considered to have performed that rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hears a verse of sajda from an imam but does not follow him at all, what must he do according to the most apparent opinion?
A) He must perform sajda in the same prayer if he joins later.
B) He must perform sajda outside the prayer.
C) He does not need to perform sajda at all.
D) He should repeat the prayer with sajda.

Key Takeaway
Whether you perform sajda al-tilawa after hearing from an imam depends on whether you followed him in the same rak'ah; if not, the sajda is wajib outside the prayer.

Ruling on Reciting Sajda Verse Outside then Inside Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sajda repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajda al-tilawa when a verse is recited both outside and inside prayer, and distinguish between the apparent narration and the narration from al-Nawadir.

Core Idea
One sajda suffices for two recitations only if the first was not performed and the sitting is continuous.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses a common scenario: a person recites a sajda verse outside prayer, prostrates, then recites the same verse inside prayer. Does the outside sajda count? The Hanafi school has two narrations. We will explore the ruling and the reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that reciting a verse of sajda (tilawa) makes sajda al-tilawa wajib. The ruling level is wajib.
Sajda al-tilawa is wajib upon recitation or hearing.
2
State the scenario and possibilities
The scenario: recitation occurs outside prayer then inside prayer. Two possibilities: (a) he prostrated outside, (b) he did not prostrate outside.
The ruling differs based on this.
3
Apply the principle of stronger act subsuming weaker
The prayer-related sajda (salawiyya) is stronger. If he did not prostrate outside, one sajda in prayer suffices for both recitations because the sitting is unified. If he prostrated outside, that outside sajda is weaker and cannot substitute for the stronger prayer-related one, so a second sajda inside is required.
This is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Contrast with the narration from al-Nawadir
In al-Nawadir, the earlier recitation is not subordinate to the later, and entering prayer changes the 'place', so he must prostrate for the first after prayer. The apparent narration considers entering prayer a small action that does not break the sitting.
The reconciliation depends on whether the sitting is broken.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and reconciliation
The relied-upon position is Zahir al-Riwayah. If after prayer he recites again, another sajda is needed unless the sitting is maintained (no speech after salam). The reconciliation between narrations hinges on whether a break occurs.
Speech after salam breaks the sitting; mere salam does not.

Source Text

ولو تلا خارج الصَّلاةِ، فسجد ، ثمَّ أَعادَ فيها ، سجدَ أخرى. وإن لم يسجد أولاً كَفَتْهُ واحدةً، في ظاهر الرواية. وإذا لم يسجد حتى فرغ من الصلاة سقطت، وأثم والمخرج له التوبة كسائر الذنوب، وإياك أن تفهم من قولهم بسقوطها عدم الإثم فإنه خطأ فاحش صرح به في البدائع، قاله صاحب البحر، وتعبيرنا بالصلاتية متناً تبعاً للهداية، والكنز، وهو مستعمل عند الفقهاء كثيراً، فهو خير من صواب نادر. قال الكمال وصواب النسبة فيه صلوية، كما عبرنا به شرحاً برد ألفه واواً وحذف التاء، وإذا كانوا حذفوها في نسبة المذكر إلى المؤنث كنسبة الرجل إلى بصرة مثلاً، فقالوا: بصري لا بصرتي، كي لا تجمع تاءان في نسبة المؤنث فيقولون: بصرتية فكيف نسبة المؤنث إلى المؤنث. ولو تلا آية خارج الصَّلاةِ، فَسَجَدَ لها، ثُمَّ دخل في الصلاة و أعاد تلاوتها فيها في ذلك المجلس) سَجَدَ سجدة أخرى؛ لأن الصلوية أقوى، فلا تكون تبعاً للأضعف فلا تنوب عنها، وإن لم يسجد أولاً حين تلا خارج الصلاة، ثم تلاها في الصلاة بذلك المجلس كَفَتْهُ سجدة واحدة، وهي الصلاتية عن التلاوتين؛ لأنَّ المجلس متحد، والصلوية أقوى فصارت الأولى تبعاً لها في ظاهر الرواية، وفي رواية النوادر يسجد للأول إذا فرغ من الصلاة، لأن السابق لا يكون تبعاً للاحق، ولأن المكان قد تبدل بالاشتغال بالصلاة، فصار كمـا لـو تبـدل بعمل آخر، وجه الظاهر أن الدخول في الصلاة عمل قليل وبمثله لا يختلف المجلس، كذا في التبيين فإن وجد بين التلاوتين وبين الدخول في الصلاة ما يقطع حكم المجلس، يلزم لكل تلاوة سجدة، كذا في مجمع الروايات، وإذا تلاها في الصلاة وسجد، ثم تلاها في مجلسه بعد السلام يسجد أخــرى، في ظاهر الرواية، قيل: هذا إذا سلم وتكلم ثـم قــرأ، كذا في الخلاصة، والتبيين، لأن المتلوة في الصلاة لا وجود لها، لا حقيقة ولا حكماً، والموجود هو الذي يستتبع دون المعدوم، بخلاف ما إذا كانت الأولى خارجية، فإنها باقية بعد التلاوة حكماً، وذكـــر في النوادر: أنه لا يلزمه سجدة أخرى بإعادتها بعد السلام، ووفق بينهما بحمل الأول عـلـى مـا إذا أعادها بعد الكلام، والثاني على ما قبله، وبه يختلف الحكم، وهو الصحيح، أي: في التوفيق لا في نفس الحكم. انتهى. لأنه متى سلم ولم يتكلم لم ينقطع به المجلس؛ لأنه كــلام يـسـيـر وبـه لا يتبـدل المجلس، خصوصاً بالسلام، فإنه لا ينقطع به مجلس الصلاة إذا نسي واجباً، وإذا تكلم فقد انقطع المجلس، كذا في مجمع الروايات وغيره، ولكن قد علمت أن ظاهر الرواية وجوب السجود.
And if he recited outside the prayer and prostrated, then repeated it inside, he prostrates another. And if he did not prostrate at first, one prostration suffices, according to the apparent narration. And if he did not prostrate until he finished the prayer, it drops, and he sins, and his outlet is repentance like other sins. Beware of understanding from their statement 'it drops' that there is no sin, for that is a gross error made clear in al-Bada'i'. Said the author of al-Bahr: Our expression 'salatiyya' in the matn following al-Hidayah and al-Kanz is commonly used by jurists, so it is better than correct rare usage. Al-Kamal said: the correct attribution is 'salawiyya', as we expressed in the sharh by changing the alif to waw and dropping the ta'. And when they drop the ta' in attributing masculine to feminine, like attributing a man to Basra, they say 'Basri' not 'Basrati', so that two ta's are not gathered in attributing feminine, so they would say 'Basratiyya'; how then with attributing feminine to feminine? And if he recited the verse outside the prayer, and prostrated for it, then entered the prayer and repeated its recitation in that sitting, he prostrates another prostration; because the prayer-related (salawiyya) is stronger, so it is not subordinate to the weaker, nor does it substitute for it. And if he did not prostrate at first when he recited outside the prayer, then recited it in the prayer in that same sitting, one prostration suffices, which is the prayer-related one for the two recitations, because the sitting is unified, and the prayer-related is stronger, so the first becomes subordinate to it, according to the apparent narration. In a narration from al-Nawadir, he prostrates for the first when he finishes the prayer, because the earlier is not subordinate to the later, and because the place has changed by engaging in the prayer, so it becomes as if it changed by another action. The basis of the apparent view is that entering the prayer is a small action, and the sitting does not change by like it, as in al-Tabyin. If between the two recitations and entering the prayer there is something that breaks the ruling of the sitting, then a prostration is required for each recitation, as in Majma' al-Riwayat. And if he recites it in the prayer and prostrates, then recites it in his sitting after the salutation, he prostrates another, according to the apparent narration. It is said: this is when he says the salutation and speaks, then recites, as in al-Khulasa and al-Tabyin, because the recitation in the prayer has no existence, neither in reality nor legally; what exists is what is followed, not the non-existent. Unlike when the first was external, for it remains after recitation legally. And it is mentioned in al-Nawadir that he is not required to prostrate another by repeating it after the salutation. And they reconciled between them by interpreting the first as when he repeated it after speaking, and the second as before it, and with this the ruling differs, and it is correct, i.e., in the reconciliation not in the ruling itself. End. Because when he says the salutation and does not speak, the sitting is not broken by it; because it is light speech and the sitting does not change by it, especially with the salutation, for the prayer sitting is not broken by it if he forgot an obligatory act. And if he speaks, the sitting is broken, as in Majma' al-Riwayat and others. But you have known that the apparent narration is the obligation of prostration.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario where a person recites a verse of sajda outside the prayer and prostrates, then later recites the same verse inside the prayer. According to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), he must prostrate again for the inside recitation because the prayer-related prostration (salawiyya) is stronger and cannot be substituted by the outside one. However, if he did not prostrate at all for the outside recitation, then one prostration during the prayer suffices for both, because the sitting is unified and the stronger (prayer) subsumes the weaker (outside). There is a narration from al-Nawadir that he must prostrate for the first after the prayer, arguing that the earlier cannot be subordinate. The author reconciles by considering whether the sitting is broken by entering the prayer or by speech after the prayer. If he recites outside, enters the prayer without speaking or other interruption, the sitting is considered continuous, so one sajda suffices. But if there is a break (e.g., speaking), each requires its own sajda. After finishing the prayer, if he recites the verse again, he must prostrate again per Zahir al-Riwayah, unless the sitting is maintained by not speaking after salam. The author emphasizes that dropping the prostration due to completing the prayer without performing it does not mean there is no sin; one must repent. The discussion also includes a philological note on the word 'salawiyya' versus 'salatiyya'.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad in his six books, which are the authoritative basis of the school.
النوادر (al-nawadir): Rare narrations transmitted from Hanafi imams that are not part of the six books of zahir al-riwayah.
صلوية (salawiyya): An act that is associated with the prayer, such as the sajda performed within the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration, if a person recites a verse of sajda outside the prayer and prostrates, then recites the same verse inside the prayer in the same sitting, what must he do?
A) He must perform another prostration inside the prayer.
B) The outside prostration suffices; no need to prostrate again.
C) He must perform two prostrations inside the prayer.
D) He must repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
When a sajda verse is recited both outside and inside prayer, the inside recitation requires its own prostration if the outside one was performed; otherwise one prostration in prayer suffices, provided the sitting remains unbroken.

One or Two Prostrations: Sajdat al-Tilawah Recited Outside Then Inside Prayer
Ruling on sajdat al-tilawah when verse recited outside then inside same sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for sajdat al-tilawah when recited outside then inside prayer in the same sitting, explain the basis of the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
If you recite a sajdah verse outside without prostrating, one prayer prostration suffices for both recitations in the same sitting.

This lesson examines a practical scenario: you recite a sajdah verse outside prayer, then later recite the same verse during prayer in the same sitting. Does one prostration cover both recitations, or must you prostrate twice? The Hanafi school has a clear position in the Ẓāhir al-Riwāya, but a weaker view (Nawādir) differs. We will work through the ruling, the proofs, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the two scenarios: (a) one prostrated outside then recited inside; (b) did not prostrate outside then recited inside. Also consider the case where prostration is delayed until after prayer.
The key variable is whether the first recitation was accompanied by prostration.
2
Identify the Hanafi position (Ẓāhir al-Riwāya)
State the ruling: if no prior prostration outside, one prostration inside suffices for both; if prior prostration outside, a new prostration is required inside. Explain the reasoning: prayer prostration is stronger, the sitting is unified, entering prayer is a minor action.
This is the muftā bihī position.
3
Identify the Nawādir view
State the minority view: a separate prostration for the outside recitation is required after prayer, because the earlier action cannot be subordinate and entering prayer changes the place.
This view is weak in authority (Nawādir).
4
Analyse the proofs (dalīl)
For Ẓāhir al-Riwāya: the prayer prostration is aqwā (stronger), so the outside recitation is subordinate; also, the sitting (majlis) is unbroken because entering prayer is a qalīl (minor) action. For Nawādir: the earlier cannot be tabi‘; change of place (makan) disrupts unity.
The dispute hinges on how we define the continuity of the majlis.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilāf and muftā bihī
The practical consequence: if one delays until after prayer, according to Ẓāhir al-Riwāya the prostration is dropped but he sins; according to Nawādir, he must prostrate after prayer. The relied-upon position is Ẓāhir al-Riwāya.
The text warns against thinking that 'dropped' means no sin.

ولو تلا خارج الصَّلاةِ، فسجد ، ثمَّ أَعادَ فيها ، سجدَ أخرى. وإن لم يسجد أولاً كَفَتْهُ واحدةً، في ظاهر الرواية. وإذا لم يسجد حتى فرغ من الصلاة سقطت، وأثم والمخرج له التوبة كسائر الذنوب، وإياك أن تفهم من قولهم بسقوطها عدم الإثم فإنه خطأ فاحش صرح به في ( البدائع » ، قالــه صـاحب « البحر »، وتعبيرنا بالصلاتية متناً تبعاً « للهداية »، و «الكنز»، وهو مستعمل عند الفقهاء كثيراً، فهو خير من صواب نادر. قال الكمال وصواب النسبة فيه صلوية، كما عبرنا به شرحاً برد ألفه واواً وحذف التاء، وإذا كانوا حذفوها في نسبة المذكر إلى المؤنث كنسبة الرجل إلى بصرة مثلاً، فقالوا: بصري لا بصرتي، كي لا تجمع تاءان في نسبة المؤنث فيقولون: بصرتية فكيف نسبة المؤنث إلى المؤنث. (ولو تلا) آية (خارج الصَّلاةِ، فَسَجَدَ لها، (ثُمَّ) دخل في الصلاة و(أعاد) تلاوتها (فيها) أي: في الصلاة في ذلك [ المجلس ]) (سَجَدَ ) سجدة ( أخرى)؛ لأن الصلوية أقوى، فلا تكون تبعاً للأضعف فلا تنوب عنها، ( وإن لم يسجد (أولاً) حين تلا خارج الصلاة، ثم تلاها في الصلاة بذلك المجلس (كَفَتْهُ) سجدة (واحدة)، وهي الصلاتية عن التلاوتين؛ لأنَّ المجلس متحد، والصلوية أقوى فصارت الأولى تبعاً لها (في ظاهر الرواية)، وفي رواية ( النوادر » يسجد للأول إذا فرغ من الصلاة، لأن السابق لا يكون تبعاً للاحق، ولأن المكان قد تبدل بالاشتغال بالصلاة، فصار كمـا لـو تبـدل بعمل آخر، وجه الظاهر أن الدخول في الصلاة عمل قليل وبمثله لا يختلف المجلس، كذا في التبيين» فإن وجد بين التلاوتين وبين الدخول في الصلاة ما يقطع حكم المجلس، يلزم لكل تلاوة سجدة، كذا في مجمع «الروايات»،
If one recited (a sajdah verse) outside prayer, and prostrated, then recited it again in prayer, he should prostrate another prostration. And if he did not prostrate initially, one prostration suffices him, in the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah). If he did not prostrate until he finished the prayer, it is dropped, and he sins; his way out is repentance like other sins. Beware of understanding from their statement 'it is dropped' that there is no sin, for that is a grave mistake, as stated in al-Bada'i, said by the author of al-Bahr. Our expression using 'salatiyah' in the matn following al-Hidayah and al-Kanz is common among jurists, so it is better than a rare correct form. Al-Kamal said: The correct relative adjective is 'salawiyah', as we expressed in the sharh by converting its alif to waw and dropping the ta. If they dropped the ta in the masculine relative to feminine, like the man relative to Basra, they say 'Basri' not 'Basriy', so that two tas are not combined in the feminine relative, they say 'Basriyyah' – so how about the feminine relative to feminine? (And if one recites) a verse (outside prayer and prostrates for it, (then) enters prayer and (repeats) its recitation (in it) i.e., in prayer in that [sitting], (he should prostrate) (another) prostration; because the prayer-prostration is stronger, so it cannot be subordinate to the weaker, so it does not substitute for it. (And if he did not prostrate (first) when he recited outside prayer, then he recites it in prayer in that sitting, (one) prostration (suffices) him, and it is the prayer-prostration for the two recitations; because the sitting is one, and the prayer-prostration is stronger, so the first becomes subordinate to it (in the apparent transmission). And in the narration of al-Nawadir, he prostrates for the first when he finishes prayer, because the earlier does not become subordinate to the later, and because the place has changed by engaging in prayer, so it is as if it changed by another action. The reasoning of the apparent (transmission) is that entering prayer is a small action, and the sitting does not change by its like, as in al-Tabyin. If there occurs between the two recitations and entering prayer something that cuts the ruling of the sitting, then each recitation requires a prostration, as in Majma' al-Riwayat.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding sajdat al-tilawah when a verse is recited outside prayer and then again inside prayer in the same sitting. The author (Imdad al-Fattah sharh) first states the ruling: if one prostrated for the first recitation outside, then recites again inside, a new prostration is required. If he did not prostrate outside, one prostration (the one for the prayer recitation) suffices for both, according to Zahir al-Riwayah. This is because the prostration during prayer (salatiyah) is considered stronger (aqwa), so it cannot be subordinate to the weaker one outside; the weaker becomes subordinate to the stronger. The author then warns against misunderstanding: if he delays prostration until after prayer, it is dropped but he sins—repentance is required. A textual note discusses the preferred terminology: 'salatiyah' (from salat) is more common, though 'salawiyah' is linguistically correct. The dispute: In Zahir al-Riwayah, one prostration suffices; in al-Nawadir, he must prostrate for the first after prayer because the change of place (from outside to inside prayer) breaks the unity of the sitting. The author explains that according to the apparent view, entering prayer is a minor action that does not break the sitting (majlis). However, if a significant action occurs between the recitations that cuts the ruling of the sitting, then each recitation requires a separate prostration.

Key Terms
صلاتية (ṣalātiyya): A prostration performed during prayer (sajdat al-tilawah inside salat).
مجلس (majlis): A single sitting or session during which multiple recitations occur that are considered to be in the same place for the purpose of merging obligations.
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāya): The well-known transmitted corpus of Imam Muhammad's six books representing the authoritative Hanafi position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ẓāhir al-Riwāya, if a person recites a sajdah verse outside prayer without prostrating, then recites it again inside prayer in the same sitting, what must he do?
A) Prostrate once after prayer for the first recitation.
B) Prostrate twice: once outside and once inside.
C) One prostration during prayer suffices for both recitations.
D) He must prostrate outside and then again inside.

Key Takeaway
One prostration during prayer suffices for a sajdah verse recited outside then inside the same sitting, per the authoritative Hanafi position.

Sajdat al-Tilawah Repeated After Salam: Zahir al-Riwayah vs. Nawadir
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the repetition of sajdat al-tilawah after salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir positions on sajdat al-tilawah after salam, explain the effect of salam on the unity of the sitting, and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Salam alone breaks the sitting according to Zahir al-Riwayah but not according to Nawadir, leading to different obligations when the sajdah verse is repeated after salam.

This passage delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute on the obligation of sajdat al-tilawah. If you recite a sajdah verse in prayer, prostrate, then after salam recite the same verse again, does a second prostration become wajib? The answer depends on whether salam breaks the unity of the sitting. Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir differ, and a proposed reconciliation is subjected to critical scrutiny. By understanding this debate, you will appreciate how the Hanafi school treats the continuity of acts within a single sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
The passage discusses a specific case: a person recites a sajdah verse in prayer, performs the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) during the prayer, then after giving salam, recites the same verse again in the same sitting without any speech in between. The question is whether a second prostration is required.
The scenario assumes no speech after salam before the second recitation.
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position and its rationale
According to the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), a second prostration is wajib. The reason given is that the recitation inside prayer has no legal existence after salam, either in reality (ḥaqīqa) or legally (ḥukman). Since it is nonexistent, it cannot fulfill the obligation of the subsequent recitation, which is a new trigger for sajdat al-tilawah.
The key concept is al-ʿadam al-ḥukmī (legal nonexistence) of the prayer recitation after salam.
3
State the Nawadir position and its rationale
According to the rare transmissions (Nawadir), no second prostration is required. The reasoning is that salam, being a minor form of speech, does not break the sitting (majlis). Therefore, the entire sitting remains one continuous unit, and the first prostration suffices for both recitations.
Nawadir considers the sitting unified unless explicit speech intervenes.
4
Examine the proposed reconciliation and its critique
Some scholars reconciled the two positions by interpreting that Zahir al-Riwayah refers to cases where the person speaks after salam before reciting again, while Nawadir refers to cases without speech. The text criticizes this reconciliation because it assumes that mere salam does not break the sitting (in Nawadir) but does in Zahir al-Riwayah. The resolution is not about speech but about the nature of salam itself.
The author (probably Ibn Abidin or a later commentator) states that the reconciliation is correct in method but not in the ruling itself.
5
Extract the final investigation (taḥqīq)
The author's investigation clarifies: according to Nawadir, mere salam does not prevent legal unity, so the prayer prostration covers the post-prayer recitation. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, mere salam does prevent unity, requiring a second prostration. If speech occurs after salam, all agree that a new prostration is wajib. The author also refutes a misunderstanding that the prayer prostration can be 'transferred' outside prayer; citing Qadi Khan's ruling that if one recites in prayer but prostrates after salam, only one prostration is needed—showing that the prayer obligation is dropped, not transferred.
The taḥqīq affirms that the difference is real and rooted in whether salam alone breaks the sitting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا تلاها في الصلاة وسجد، ثم تلاها في مجلسه بعد السلام يسجد أخرى، في « ظـاهـر الـروايـة»، قيل: هذا إذا سلم وتكلـم ثـم قــرأ، كذا في « الخلاصة»، و« التبيين»، لأن المتلوة في الصلاة لا وجود لها، لا حقيقة ولا حكماً، والموجود هو الذي يستتبع دون المعدوم، بخلاف ما إذا كانت الأولى خارجية، فإنها باقية بعد التلاوة حكماً، وذكـــر في النوادر » : أنه لا يلزمه سجدة أخرى بإعادتها بعد السلام، ووفق بينهما بحمل الأول عـلـى مـا إذا أعادها بعد الكلام، والثاني على ما قبله، وبه يختلف الحكم، وهو الصحيح، أي: في التوفيق لا في نفس الحكم. انتهى. لأنه متى سلم ولم يتكلم لم ينقطع به المجلس؛ لأنه كــلام يـسـيـر وبـه لا يتبـدل المجلس، خصوصاً بالسلام، فإنه لا ينقطع به مجلس الصلاة إذا نسي واجباً، وإذا تكلم فقد انقطع المجلس، كذا في مجمع الروايات وغيره، ولكن قد علمت أن «ظاهر الرواية» وجوب السجود، 
 وإن لم يتكلم بتلاوتها ثانياً بعد السلام فيتحد حكم «ظاهر الرواية » و « النوادر» مـع كـونـه مختلفـاً ولذا قيد «ظاهر الرواية بما إذا تلكم بعد السلام، ثم قرأ على ما قيل، فالحمل المذكور غير مسلم، والتحقيق أن مجرد السلام لا يمنع الاتحاد الحكمي على رواية « النوادر »، فتكفيـه الصـلويـة عـن التي بعدها خارج الصلاة، ويمنع مجرد السلام على ظاهر الرواية»، وأما إذا فصـل بـعـد الســلام بكلام فيتكرر الوجوب اتفاقاً، وما فهمه بعض المتأخرين من هذا المحل أن الصلوية تقضى خارجها فغير مستقيم، لما تقدَّم ولنص قاضي خان على أنه لو قرأها في الصلاة فلم يسجد حتـى سـلـم، فقرأها يسجد،واحدة وسقطت عنه الأولى، فلو كانت قائمة مقامها لقال وأجزأته واحدة عنهما
And if he recites it in prayer and prostrates, then recites it in his sitting after salam, he prostrates another (prostration) in the apparent transmission. It was said: This is if he gave salam and spoke then recited, as in al-Khulasa and al-Tabyin, because that which is recited in prayer has no existence, neither in reality nor legally, and that which exists is what is followed, not the nonexistent, contrary to when the first is outside, for it remains legally after recitation. And it is mentioned in al-Nawadir: that another prostration is not required upon repeating it after salam. They reconciled between them by interpreting the first as when he repeats after speaking, and the second as before that, and by this the ruling differs, and that is correct, i.e., in the reconciliation, not in the ruling itself. End. Because whenever he gives salam and does not speak, the sitting is not broken by it; because it is little speech and the sitting does not change by it, especially salam, for the prayer sitting is not broken by it if he forgets an obligatory act. And if he speaks, the sitting is broken, as in Majma' al-Riwayat and others. But you have known that the apparent transmission (requires) the obligation of prostration. [page 508] And if he does not speak reciting it a second time after salam, then the ruling of the apparent transmission and al-Nawadir unite despite being different, and therefore the apparent transmission was restricted to when he spoke after salam, then recited, as was said. So that reconciliation is not conceded. The investigation is that mere salam does not prevent legal unity according to the narration of al-Nawadir, so the prayer prostration suffices for that which follows it outside prayer, while mere salam prevents it according to the apparent transmission. And if he separates after salam by speech, the obligation is repeated by agreement. And what some later scholars understood from this that the prayer prostration is performed outside it is incorrect, due to what preceded and the text of Qadi Khan that if he recited it in prayer and did not prostrate until he gave salam, then recited it, he prostrates once and the first is dropped for him. For if it (the prayer prostration) were to take its place, he would have said 'and one suffices him for both'.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage continues the intra-Hanafi dispute on sajdat al-tilawah, now addressing the scenario where one recites the verse in prayer, prostrates, then after salam recites the same verse again. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, a second prostration is required because the recitation inside prayer is considered 'nonexistent' after salam, whereas the outside recitation is 'existent'. However, al-Nawadir says no second prostration is needed. A reconciliation is proposed: if he spoke after salam before reciting again, the sitting is broken and a new prostration is required (Zahir al-Riwayah's condition); if he did not speak, the sitting remains unified and one prostration suffices (Nawadir's view). The text critiques this reconciliation, stating that mere salam does not break the sitting according to Nawadir (so unity is preserved), while it does according to Zahir al-Riwayah. The investigation (tahqiq) clarifies: in Nawadir, salam does not prevent union, so the prayer prostration covers the post-prayer recitation; in Zahir al-Riwayah, salam does prevent union, so a second prostration is required. If he speaks after salam, all agree a new prostration is needed. The author then refutes a misunderstanding: some later scholars thought the prayer prostration can be performed outside prayer, but Qadi Khan's text shows that if one recites in prayer, does not prostrate until after salam, then recites again, only one prostration is needed (the post-prayer one) and the prayer obligation drops—this indicates the prayer prostration is not transferred outside.

Key Terms
حُكْماً (ḥukman): Legally considered existence; a ruling that something is treated as existing for legal purposes.
سلام (salām): The concluding taslim of prayer; the text discusses its effect on the unity of the sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the investigation (tahqiq) in the text, what is the effect of mere salam (without speech) on the unity of the sitting for sajdat al-tilawah?
A) It always breaks the sitting, so a second prostration is required.
B) It never breaks the sitting, so one prostration suffices.
C) It breaks the sitting according to Zahir al-Riwayah but not according to Nawadir.
D) It breaks the sitting only if one intends to end the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two transmissions on sajdat al-tilawah after salam: Zahir al-Riwayah requires a second prostration; Nawadir does not, with the difference hinging on whether salam breaks the sitting.

Tadakhul in Sajdat al-Tilawah: Merging Prostrations in One Sitting
Explains tadakhul (merging) of multiple sajdah prostrations in one sitting and its absence in two sittings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of tadakhul (merging) for sajdat al-tilawah and apply it to determine when one prostration suffices for multiple recitations.

Core Idea
One prostration suffices for multiple sajdah recitations in one sitting; separate sittings require separate prostrations.

When a person recites the same ayah of sajdah multiple times, does he need to prostrate each time? The Hanafi school answers with the principle of tadakhul (merging): if the recitations occur in a single sitting, one prostration is enough. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the conditions, and the exact scope of this principle, including a key intra-madhhab difference about the unity of the reciter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine the hukm for repeating a sajdah verse in one sitting: one prostration suffices for multiple recitations.
The ruling applies whether the recitation is at the beginning, middle, or end of the sitting.
2
Examine the dalil
Review the hadith of Jibril and the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrating once after multiple recitations. This is the primary evidence for tadakhul.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but it is relied upon in matters of worship.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi difference: some scholars require the reciter to be the same person for tadakhul when hearing and reciting. The text prefers the view that unity of reciter is not required.
The preferred view is based on the same hadith.
4
Distinguish tadakhul types
Understand the two types of tadakhul: tadakhul fi al-sabab (merging of causes) applies to worship, while tadakhul fi al-hukm (merging of rulings) applies to punishments.
Sajdat al-tilawah falls under tadakhul fi al-sabab, where multiple causes are merged into one obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كَمَنْ كرّرها أي الآية الواحدة (في مجلس واحد حيث تكفيه سجدة واحدة سواء كان في ابتداء التلاوة أو أثنائها أو بعدها للتداخل ، قال في ( الزاهدي » : لما روي « أنَّ جبريل عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يقرأها على النبي ثم هو على أصحابه ويسجد مرة واحدة، وكذا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم « كان يقرأها علـى أصحابه مراراً ويسجد مرة » (١) ، قال في « الفوائد : ولأن سببي الوجوب اجتمعا في مجلس لسجدة واحدة كالتالي السامع، وفي ( التبيين»: لو تلاها في الصلاة بعدما سمعها مـن غـيـره يكفيــه سـجدة واحدة انتهى. ولو تلاها أولاً ثم سمعها، ليه سجدة واحدة باتفاق الروايات، كما في «مجمع الروايات». وفي «الوبري : لو سمع المصلي آية السجدة من رجل، ثم من آخر، ثم تلاها، أجزأته واحدة عن الكل، وإن لم يسجدها سقط الكل، ولو لم يقرأ التي سمعها يجب عـلـيـه سـجـدتـان خــارج الصلاة، كما في « التبيين وهذا على غير الصحيح الشارط اتحاد التالي، والصحيح خـلافـه لـمـا رويناه، كما في « مجمع الروايات (لا) أي: لا يكفيه سجدة واحدة بتكريره في (مجلسين)، لعدم التداخل، وهذا لأن مبنى السجود على التداخل ما أمكن، وإمكانه عند اتحاد المجلس؛ لكونـه جامعاً للمتفرقات فيما يتكرر للحاجة، كما في الإيجاب والقبول وغيره، والقارئ محتاج إلى التكرار للحفظ والتعليم والاعتبار، وهو تداخل في السبب دون الحكم، ومعناه: أن تجعــل التـلاوة كلها كتلاوة واحدة تكون الواحدة منها سبباً والباقي تبعاً لها، وهو أليق بالعبادات، والتداخل في الحكم أليق في العقوبات، لأنها شرعت للزجر فهو ينزجر بواحدة فيحصل المقصود، فلا حاجة إلى العقوبة الثانية، قال الزيلعي والفرق بينهما أي بين التداخلين أن التداخل في السبب تنوب فيـه
Like one who repeats it, i.e., the same verse (in one sitting, where one prostration suffices him, whether at the beginning of recitation or in the middle or after it, due to tadakhul. He said in al-Zahidi: Because it is narrated that Jibril (peace be upon him) used to recite it to the Prophet, then he (the Prophet) to his companions, and he prostrated once. And likewise the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to recite it to his companions repeatedly and prostrate once. He said in al-Fawa'id: And because the two causes of obligation meet in one sitting for one prostration, like the reciter and the listener. And in al-Tabyin: If he recites it in prayer after hearing it from someone else, one prostration suffices him. End. And if he recites first then hears it, he has one prostration by agreement of the narrations, as in Majma' al-Riwayat. And in al-Webrawi: If the one praying hears a sajdah verse from a man, then from another, then recites it, one suffices him for all; if he does not prostrate for it, all fall off. And if he does not recite that which he heard, he must make two prostrations outside the prayer, as in al-Tabyin. And this is not the correct (view) which requires unity of the reciter; the correct is contrary to it due to what we narrated, as in Majma' al-Riwayat. (Not) i.e., one prostration does not suffice him if he repeats it in (two sittings), due to lack of tadakhul. This is because the basis of prostration is tadakhul as much as possible, and its possibility occurs when the sitting is one; because the sitting gathers the separate matters that are repeated due to need, as in offer and acceptance and other things. The reciter needs repetition for memorization, teaching, and contemplation. And it is tadakhul in the cause, not in the ruling. Its meaning is to make the whole recitation like one recitation, with one of them being the cause and the rest being subordinate to it. And it is more suitable for acts of worship. And tadakhul in the ruling is more suitable for penalties (punishments), because they are legislated for deterrence; so one deters and the purpose is achieved, so there is no need for a second punishment. Al-Zayla'i said: The difference between them (i.e., between the two types of tadakhul) is that tadakhul in the cause means that one (prostration) substitutes...
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage establishes the general principle of tadakhul (merging/overlap) for sajdat al-tilawah when the same verse is recited multiple times in one sitting (majlis). One prostration suffices for all recitations in the same sitting, whether at the beginning, middle, or end. The evidence is a hadith about Jibril and the Prophet reciting and prostrating once, and the Prophet doing the same with his companions. The reason (illa) is that the causes (recitations) are multiple but the obligation (prostration) is one; since the sitting is unified, they merge. The text further discusses that if one hears a sajdah verse and then recites it, or hears from multiple people, one prostration suffices. If he does not recite the heard verse, he must prostrate separately for hearing and reciting? The text notes two opinions: the correct one does not require unity of the reciter. The principle applies only within one sitting; if the repetitions occur in two different sittings, no tadakhul occurs and separate prostrations are required. The wisdom: prostration is an act of worship, so merging is appropriate to avoid hardship; repetition is needed for learning and teaching. The text distinguishes two types of tadakhul: (a) tadakhul in the cause (sabab) – where multiple causes (recitations) are treated as one, and the subsequent ones are subordinate; (b) tadakhul in the ruling (hukm) – where the same ruling is applied without merging the causes, more suitable for punishments (e.g., multiple crimes require multiple punishments but one may suffice for deterrence). Al-Zayla'i further explains that in tadakhul in the cause, one prostration substitutes for all. The passage ends abruptly, likely continuing this explanation.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadākhul): The merging of multiple causes (recitations) into one obligation (prostration) due to unity of time/place.
تداخل في السبب (tadākhul fī al-sabab): Multiple causes (e.g., recitations) are combined and treated as one, with one cause being primary and the rest subordinate.
تداخل في الحكم (tadākhul fī al-ḥukm): Merging of multiple judgments into one, e.g., multiple crimes receive one punishment if one suffices for deterrence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for tadakhul (merging) of multiple sajdat al-tilawah in one sitting?
A) Qiyas on zakat
B) The practice of Jibril and the Prophet reciting and prostrating once
C) Ijma of the Companions
D) Necessity due to forgetfulness

Key Takeaway
One prostration suffices for multiple sajdah recitations in a single sitting; separate sittings require separate prostrations.

Tadaakhul in Sujood al-Tilawah: One Sujood for Repeated Recitations in One Sitting
Explains the ruling of sujood al-tilawah when the verse is repeated in one sitting, and the principle of tadaakhul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that one sujood al-tilawah suffices for multiple recitations of the same verse in one sitting and distinguish between tadaakhul in cause and tadaakhul in ruling.

Core Idea
In one sitting, repeated sajdah verses require only one sujood due to tadaakhul in the cause.

This passage from Nur al-Idah and its commentary addresses a common scenario: what if you recite the same verse of prostration multiple times in one sitting? The Hanafi school answers with one sujood, based on the principle of tadaakhul (legal overlap). The text provides evidence from prophetic practice and distinguishes between tadaakhul in acts of worship (cause) versus punishments (ruling). It also discusses an intra-Hanafi difference regarding the effect of salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sujood al-tilawah, which is wajib. When the same verse is repeated in one sitting, only one sujood is required due to tadaakhul.
The ruling applies whether the verse is recited at the beginning, middle, or end of the sitting.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The primary evidence is the practice of Jibril and the Prophet (peace be upon him): they would recite the verse repeatedly but prostrate only once. This is a mursal hadith cited by al-Zahidi.
The hadith is considered zanni in transmission but sufficient for istihsan.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The repeated recitation with only one sujood indicates that multiple causes (recitations) in one sitting yield a single obligation. This is the essence of tadaakhul.
The principle is istihsan; qiyas would require a sujood for each recitation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Zahir al-Riwaya holds that salam breaks the unity of the sitting, so reciting after salam (without speech) creates a new obligation. Nawadir holds that mere salam does not break unity. The text prefers Nawadir as the tahqiq (investigated view).
Both views are valid; the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is the Nawadir position.
5
Understand the theoretical basis: tadaakhul in cause vs. ruling
For acts of worship, tadaakhul is in the cause (sabab): multiple recitations are treated as one cause. For punishments, tadaakhul is in the ruling: one punishment suffices for multiple offenses in one sitting. This distinction is based on the nature of worship (multiplicity) vs. punishment (deterrence).
This explains why repeating salawat is recommended (not covered by tadaakhul) while repeating sujood is merged.

Like one who repeats it in one sitting, not in two sittings. And if he does not speak after the second recitation after the salam, then the ruling of Zahir al-Riwaya and Nawadir becomes unified despite being different. Therefore, Zahir al-Riwaya is restricted to the case where he spoke after salam, then recited as is said, so that interpretation is not accepted. The investigation is that mere salam does not prevent legal unity according to Nawadir, so the one [sajdah] suffices for the subsequent one outside the prayer, while mere salam prevents it according to Zahir al-Riwaya. But if he separates after salam with speech, the obligation is repeated by agreement. What some later scholars understood from this place, that the prayer-sajdah is performed outside it, is incorrect due to what preceded and due to the text of Qadi Khan that if one recited it in prayer and did not prostrate until he said salam, then recited it, he prostrates once and the first is waived. If it were standing in its place, he would have said one suffices for both. (Like one who repeats it, i.e., the same verse, in one sitting) where one sajdah suffices, whether at the beginning of recitation, during it, or after it, due to tadaakhul. Al-Zahidi said: Because it was narrated that Jibril (alayhi al-salam) used to recite it to the Prophet and then he to his companions and prostrated once. Similarly, the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) would recite it to his companions repeatedly and prostrate once. In al-Fawa'id: Because the two causes of obligation come together in one sitting for one sajdah, like the listener in succession. In al-Tabyin: If he recited it in prayer after hearing it from someone else, one sajdah suffices him. If he recited it first then heard it, he has one sajdah by agreement of the narrations, as in Majma' al-Riwayat. In al-Wabri: If the praying person hears the verse of sajdah from a man, then from another, then recites it, one suffices for all. If he does not prostrate, all are waived. If he did not recite the one he heard, two sajdahs are obligatory upon him outside the prayer, as in al-Tabyin. This is contrary to the correct view conditioned on the unity of the reciter; the correct view is opposite due to what we narrated, as in Majma' al-Riwayat. (No) meaning: one sajdah does not suffice him by repeating in two sittings, due to lack of tadaakhul. This is because the basis of sujood is tadaakhul as much as possible, and its possibility is when the sitting is unified, because it gathers the scattered matters in what is repeated for need, like offer and acceptance and others. The reciter needs repetition for memorization, teaching, and contemplation. It is tadaakhul in the cause, not in the ruling. Its meaning: to make all the recitations like one recitation, where one is the cause and the rest are dependent on it. This is more appropriate for acts of worship. Tadaakhul in the ruling is more appropriate for punishments, because they are legislated for deterrence, so one deters and the purpose is achieved, hence no need for a second punishment. Al-Zayla'i said: The difference between them, i.e., the two types of tadaakhul, is that tadaakhul in the cause causes one to substitute for what is before and after it. Tadaakhul in the ruling only substitutes for what is before it, such that if one fornicates and is punished, then fornicates in the same sitting, he is punished a second time. It is said: if he prostrated for the first then recited it, another becomes obligatory, like the hadd of drinking. This is based on the view that tadaakhul for recitation is in the ruling, and it is weak. Rather, it is in the cause. This is because acts of worship are treated with caution in establishing them. If we established tadaakhul in rulings here, i.e., in worship, it would lead to nullifying tadaakhul, because in terms of causes it repeats, and in terms of rulings it does not repeat, so it repeats out of caution, because when it oscillates between establishment and fall, it is established, as their basis is multiplicity, as we are created for them. As for punishments, their basis is warding off and pardon, and it does not lead to the nullification of tadaakhul we mentioned, so when it oscillates, it falls. And because the effect of the sitting is verified on all causes, not on rulings, as in sale and other matters. This tadaakhul is restricted by the sitting, so it is known that it is in the cause. (Mustasfa, Fath al-Qadir). Note: Tadaakhul is istihsan, while qiyas requires a sajdah for every recitation, as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. Al-Diraya said: Based on this, they said: If one sneezes and praises Allah repeatedly in a sitting, it is appropriate for the listener to respond (yashmittuh) because it is the right of the servant. Similarly, sending blessings on the Prophet; it is said to respond once, and it is said up to ten. The most correct is that if he exceeds three, do not respond. As in al-Mabsut, because it is narrated that Umar said to the sneezer after three in his sitting: 'Stand and blow your nose, for you have a cold.' As in al-Bahr. Fakhr al-Islam mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir a difference between sajdah and salawat on the Prophet, saying: Repeating salawat is recommended, unlike sujood, because the servant, however great his rank, cannot match the right of Allah Almighty in lifting hardship, so they differ. The preponderant view is to send blessings on the Prophet whenever his name is mentioned. In Yatimat al-Dahr: Umar al-Hafiz was asked about one who recites the verse of sajdah repeatedly in one sitting: is it better for him to prostrate for each recitation or better to do one? He said: This is like one who mentions the Prophet repeatedly; he is not obliged to send blessings except once, except that repeating his name is obligatory? He prostrates as wajib? [To preserve his Sunnah by which the laws are established, and to oblige blessings at every mention would be hardship, so it is waived] when the sitting is unified. So this is similar, except there is a difference: repeating salawat is recommended. That is, not obligatory.
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the issue of sujood al-tilawah when the same verse of prostration is recited multiple times in one sitting. The primary ruling is that only one sujood is required, based on the principle of tadaakhul (legal overlap). The text distinguishes between Zahir al-Riwaya (which requires the reciter to speak after salam to separate sittings) and Nawadir (where mere salam does not separate). The core evidence is the practice of Jibril and the Prophet (peace be upon him) reciting and prostrating once despite repeating the verse. The passage also explains that tadaakhul operates on the level of the cause (sabab) not the ruling (hukm) for acts of worship, while for punishments tadaakhul is in the ruling. This is istihsan (juristic preference), as qiyas would require a sajdah for each recitation. The text then analogizes to sneezing (tasmit) and sending blessings on the Prophet, clarifying that repeating tasmit is not required after three, while repeating salawat is recommended. The overall message is that in one sitting, the obligation merges, and one sujood removes the duty for all recitations.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadaakhul): Legal overlap where multiple causes (asbab) merge to produce a single ruling due to unity of time/place (majlis).
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwaya): The well-known (mashhur) transmission from the founding imams via Imam Muhammad's six books, which holds that salam breaks the sitting for sujood.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare transmissions, including those of Hasan ibn Ziyad, which here hold that salam does not break the unity of the sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Tadakhul in Sujud al-Tilawah: One Sujud for Multiple Recitations
Ruling and proof for tadakhul in sujud al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tadakhul in sujud al-tilawah and distinguish it from the qiyas, and apply the principle to related acts like tashmit and salawat.

Core Idea
One sujud suffices for multiple recitations in one gathering by istihsan, not by strict qiyas.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on overlapping sujud al-tilawah when multiple verses of prostration are recited in one gathering. The text explains why one sajdah suffices by way of istihsan (juristic preference), contrasting this with the qiyas that would require a separate sujud for each verse. It also compares this ruling to those for tashmit (responding to a sneeze) and sending blessings upon the Prophet, highlighting how the Hanafi school balances textual proofs and practical ease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration. The question is: if multiple verses are recited in one gathering, how many sujud are required?
2
Understand the principle of tadakhul
The Hanafi view (istihsan) is that one sujud covers all recitations in one gathering. The strict qiyas would require a separate sujud for each recitation.
The text explicitly states: 'التداخل استحسان، والقياس أن يجب لكل تلاوة سجدة'.
3
Examine the rationale and proof
The text provides reasoning: acts of worship are based on caution and multiplicity, while punishments are based on leniency and dropping. The gathering is the effective cause for overlap. It also uses the hadith of Umar about sneezing to illustrate that after three times, tashmit is not required, analogous to sujud.
The proof is the hadith 'قُمْ فَاسْتَنْثِرْ فَإِنَّكَ مَزْكُومٌ' (Get up and blow your nose, for you have a cold).
4
Compare with tashmit and salawat
For tashmit, the majority view is that it is not required after three sneezes. For sending blessings on the Prophet, it is recommended to repeat each time his name is mentioned, unlike sujud. The reason is that the Prophet's right is not equal to Allah's right in removing hardship.
The text contrasts the rights of Allah and the rights of servants.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The authoritative position (mufta bihi) is that one sujud suffices for multiple recitations in one gathering. This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
The text says: 'بل في السبب' emphasizing the overlap is in the cause, not the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الواحدة عما قبلها وعما بعدها. وفي التداخل في الحكم لا تنوب إلا عما قبلها حتى لـو زنــي فـحـد، ثم زنى في المجلس يُحد ثانياً. انتهى. وقيل: إذا سجد للأولى ثم تلاها لزمته أخـــرى، كحد الشرب، وهذا على ما قيل أن التداخل للتلاوة في الحكم وهو ضعيف. انتهى. بل في السبب، وهذا لأن العبادات يحتاط في إثباتها، فلو أثبتنا التداخل في الأحكام هنا أي في العبادات يؤدي إلى إبطال التداخل، لأنه بالنظر إلى الأسباب يتكرر، وبالنظر إلى الأحكام لا يتكرر، فيتكرر احتياطاً لأنها متی دارت بين الثبوت والسقوط ثبتت لأن مبناها على التكثر لأنا خلقنـا لهـا، وأما العقوبات فمبناها على الدرء والعفو، ولا يؤدي إلى ما ذكرناه من إبطال التداخل حتى إذا دارت كذلك سقطت، ولأن المتحقق تأثير المجلس في جميع الأسباب لا الأحكام على ما في البيع وغيره، وهذا التداخل تقيد بالمجلس، فعلم أنه في السبب انتهى . ( مستصفى»، «بفتح القدير». تنبيه: التداخل استحسان، والقياس أن يجب لكل تلاوة سجدة، كما في « التاتارخانية». قال في الدراية » : وعلى هذا قالوا: لو عطس وحمد الله في مجلس مراراً ينبغي للسامع أن يشمته، لأنه حق العبد، وكذا الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قيل : يشمته مرة وقيل : إلى العشرة، والأصــح: أنه إذا زاد علـى الثلاث لا يشمته (۳) كذا في ( المبسوط » ، لما روي أن عمر ه ه ه ه قال للعاطس في مجلسه بعد الثلاث: قم فاستنثر فإنك مزكوم » (۳)، كذا في ( البحر » ، وذكر فخر الإسلام في « الجامع الكبير » فرقـاً بـيـن السجدة والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال : يستحب تكرار الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بخلاف السجود، لأن العبد وإن عظمت منزلته لا يوازي حقه حق الله تعالى في وضع الحرج فلذا افترقا انتهى. والراجح الصلاة على النبي كلما ذكر اسمه. انتهى. وفي ( يتيمة الدهر » سئل عمر الحافظ، عمن قرأ آية السجدة مراراً في مجلس واحد، الأفضل في حقه أن يسجد لكل تلاوة، أم الأفضل أن بـ مرة واحدة، قال: هذا كمن ذكر النبي و مراراً لا يلزمه الصلاة إلا مرة واحدة، إلا أن تكرار اسمه وجوب يسجد واجب [ لحفظ سنته التي بها قوام الشرائع وفي إيجاب الصلاة في كل ذكر حرج فوجب وضعـــه ] إذا اتحد المجلس، فكذلك هذا إلا أن بينهما فرقاً، وهو أنه يستحب تكرار الصلاة انتهى، أي: لا
The one [sajdah] suffices for what came before and after it. As for overlapping in the ruling, it does not substitute except for what came before, such that if someone committed zina and was punished with hadd, then committed zina again in the same gathering, he is punished a second time. End. And it was said: If he prostrated for the first [recitation] then recited another, another [prostration] becomes obligatory upon him, like the hadd of drinking, and this is based on the opinion that overlapping is for the recitation in the ruling, and it is weak. End. Rather, it is in the cause. This is because acts of worship are to be applied with caution in establishing them. If we established overlapping in rulings here, i.e., in acts of worship, it would lead to invalidating overlapping, because with regard to causes it repeats, and with regard to rulings it does not repeat, so it repeats out of caution, because when they fluctuate between being established and dropped, they are established because their basis is multiplicity, for we are created for them. As for punishments, their basis is on warding off and pardoning, and it does not lead to what we mentioned of invalidating overlapping, such that if they fluctuate likewise, they drop. And because the effect of the gathering is established on all causes, not the rulings, as in sale and other matters, and this overlapping is tied to the gathering, so it is known that it is in the cause. End. (Mustasfa, Fath al-Qadir). Note: Overlapping is istihsan, and the qiyas is that for every recitation a prostration is obligatory, as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. He said in al-Dirayah: On this basis they said: If someone sneezes and praises Allah repeatedly in a gathering, it is proper for the listener to respond to him with tashmit, because it is a right of the servant. Likewise, sending blessings upon the Prophet, peace be upon him. It was said: Respond once; and it was said: up to ten times. And the most correct is that if he exceeds three, do not respond to him (3). As in al-Mabsut, because it is narrated that Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said to a sneezer in his gathering after three: Get up and blow your nose, for you have a cold (3). As in al-Bahr. Fakhr al-Islam mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir a difference between prostration and sending blessings upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, saying: It is recommended to repeat blessings upon the Prophet, unlike prostration, because the servant, though his status is great, his right does not equal the right of Allah Almighty in removing difficulty, so they differ. End. And the preponderant is to send blessings upon the Prophet whenever his name is mentioned. End. In Yatimah al-Dahr: Umar al-Hafiz was asked about someone who recited a verse of prostration repeatedly in one gathering: Is it better for him to prostrate for each recitation, or is it better to do it once? He said: This is like someone who mentions the Prophet repeatedly; it is not obligatory upon him to send blessings except once, except that repeating his name is obligatory. For the preservation of his Sunnah, by which the laws are established, and in making blessings obligatory in every mention there is difficulty, so it is dropped. End. That is: no.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage discusses the principle of tadakhul (overlap) for sujud al-tilawah when multiple verses are recited in one gathering. The preferred view (istihsan) is that one prostration suffices for all recitations, unlike the qiyas which would require a separate sajdah for each verse. The text contrasts this with hudud punishments where overlapping does not occur. It then compares sujud al-tilawah with tashmit (responding to a sneeze) and sending blessings upon the Prophet. The Hanafi position is that for sneezing, tashmit is recommended but not required after three times. For blessings upon the Prophet, it is recommended to repeat them each time his name is mentioned. However, for sujud al-tilawah, one sujud suffices in one gathering due to istihsan, as established by the masters of the school.

Key Terms
التداخل (al-tadakhul): Legal overlap where one act suffices for multiple causes in one gathering.
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran.
تشميت العاطس (tashmit al-’atis): Responding to a sneezer who praises Allah by saying 'yarhamukallah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if someone recites multiple verses of prostration in one gathering without changing location, how many sujud al-tilawah are required?
A) One sujud suffices for all recitations.
B) A separate sujud for each recitation.
C) No sujud is required if more than one verse is recited.
D) Two sujud, one after the first and one after the last.

Key Takeaway
One sujud al-tilawah suffices for multiple recitations in one gathering by Hanafi istihsan, due to the unity of the gathering and the caution in worship.

Change of Majlis for Sujud al-Tilawah
Rulings on what constitutes a change of gathering for multiple sujud al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between situations that require repeated sujud al-tilawah due to change of gathering and those that do not, and apply the Hanafi rules to open spaces, enclosed spaces, and special cases like weaving and tree climbing.

Core Idea
Change of gathering for sujud al-tilawah requires physical movement in open spaces but not within small enclosed areas.

The obligation of sujud al-tilawah is wajib every time one recites or hears an ayah of sajdah. However, if one recites multiple times within the same gathering (majlis), a single sujud suffices. The key question is: what constitutes a change of gathering? This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the Hanafi position, distinguishing between open spaces like deserts and roads, enclosed spaces like houses and mosques, and special cases like weaving and swimming.

Guided Path
1
Identify the environment
Determine if the person is in an open space (desert, road, river) or an enclosed space (house, mosque, small basin).
Open spaces change gathering easily; enclosed spaces generally do not.
2
Apply the three-step rule for open spaces
If the person moves three steps or more in an open space, the gathering changes; otherwise it does not.
Three steps is the threshold in deserts and roads.
3
Check special cases: weaver, tree, swimmer
For a weaver, distinguish active movement (change) from sitting in one place (no change). For tree branches, if descent/ascent is needed, change occurs; otherwise one sujud suffices. For swimming, a river or large basin changes gathering; a small basin may not.
These cases have detailed rulings based on physical displacement.
4
Apply the rule for enclosed spaces
Moving within corners of a small house or mosque does not change the gathering. In a large dwelling like a sultan's palace, moving between separate houses does change.
The principle: places where iqtida is valid are considered one gathering.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتبدل المجلس بالانتقال منه، ولو كان مُسَدِّياً وبالانتقال من غُصْنٍ إلى غصن، وعَوْمٍ في نهرٍ، أَوْ حَوْضِ كبير، في الأصح. ولا يتبدل بزوايا البيتِ، والمسجدِ، . سجود التلاوة وفي «» المجتبى»: لا خلاف في وجوب تعظيم اسمه تعالى عند ذكــره فـي كـل مـرة. ( ويتبدل المجلس بالانتقال منه بخطوات ثلاث في الصحراء والطريق، (ولو كان مُسَدِّياً) في الأصح، بأن يذهب وبيده السدى ويلقيه على أعواد مضروبة في الحائط أو الأرض، لا الـذي يـكـون جالساً على شيء ويدير دوارة يلقي عليها السدى، لأنه جالس في مكان واحد فلا يتكرر الوجوب، كما في «الفتح»، وإنما قيدنا بكونه في الصحراء لما سنذكر، أن البيت الصغير لا يتبدل المجلس بالانتقال فيه إلى زاوية أخرى منه بغير تسدية، فمنعها بالأولى، خصوصاً عـلـى الـفـور بـأنـهـا تمـنــع اختلاف المكان، ولم يقيد ذلك القول بكونها في بيت لما هو الشأن فيها على عادتهم التسدية بـغـيـر دواره يدار عليها وهو جالس والضابط أن كل مكان يصح فيه الاقتداء لا يتبدل بالانتقال فيه إلى ناحيته منه، كما سنذكره عن قاضي خان» (وَ) يتبدل المجلس ( بالانتقال من غُصْن) شجرة (إلى غصن) منها في «ظاهر الرواية» وهو الصحيح، كذا في ( التاتارخانية»، وكذا يعتبر الـغـصـن مختلفـاً عن الآخر في الحل والحرم، حتى أن الحلال لو رمى صيداً على شجرة أصلها في الحــل والـغـصـن في الحرم يجب الجزاء، كذا في «الفتح» ، وفي ( التاتارخانية ) عن ( الحجة ) : إن كان لا يمكنه التحول من غصن إلى غصن إلا بالنزول والصعود يسجد ثانية، وإلا تكفيه واحدة للتلاوتين، (و) يتبدل المجلس في (عوم) أي: سباحة في نهر، أو ) سباحة في حوض (كبير)، لاختلاف المجلس، وقولـه ( في الأصح) يرجع إلى المسائل كلها، وعن محمد: إذا كان طول الحوض وعـرضـه مثـل طـول المسجد وعرضه، يكفيه سجدة واحدة، وفي ( الخانية » : الصحيح أنه يتكرر انتهى. وكذا في الدياسة والدور حول الرحى في الأصح، كما في «الفتح». (ولا يتبــدلُ) مجلس السماع والتلاوة (بزوايـا البيت الصغير، كذا في « البرهان» وكذا لو تلاها في كرم في أماكن مختلفة، كما في « الدراية»، وفي التاتارخانية»، (و) لو قرأها في زوايا (المسجد الجامع، يكفيه سجدة واحدة، وكذا حكـم البيـت والدار، وقيل: وفي الدار إذا كانت الدار كبيرة، كدار السلطان، فتلا في دار منها ثم في دار أخرى يلزمه سجدة أخرى انتهى. وقد جزم قاضي خان حيث قال : ولا يتكرر الوجـوب لـو انـتـقـل مـن زاوية البيت، أو المسجد، إلى زاوية، إلا إذا كانت الدار كبيرة كدار السلطان، وإن انتقل في المسجد الجامع من زاوية إلى زاوية، لا يتكرر الوجوب، وإن انتقل فيه من دار إلى دار، ففي كل موضع يصح يصير كمكان واحد، ولا يتكرر الوجوب انتهى.
الاقتداء
And the gathering changes by moving from it, even if one is a weaver, and by moving from a branch to a branch, and swimming in a river or a large basin, in the more correct view. And it does not change by [moving within] corners of the house and the mosque. Sujud al-tilawah: And in al-Mujtaba: There is no disagreement about the obligation of glorifying His name, the Exalted, when it is mentioned every time. (And the gathering changes by moving from it by three steps in the desert and the road, (even if one is a weaver) in the more correct view, meaning he goes with the warp in his hand and throws it onto sticks set up in the wall or ground, not one who sits on something and turns a spool to which he throws the warp, because he is sitting in one place so the obligation is not repeated, as in al-Fath. And we only restricted it to the desert because we will mention that the small house does not have the gathering change by moving to another corner of it without weaving, so preventing it is a fortiori, especially immediately, because they prevent difference of place. And that statement was not restricted to being in a house because the matter in their custom is weaving without a spool that is turned while sitting. And the rule is that every place where following [the imam] is valid does not change by moving to its side, as we will mention from Qadikhan. (And) the gathering changes (by moving from a branch) of a tree (to a branch) of it in al-Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is the correct view, as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. And likewise, the branch is considered different from another in the halal and haram [area], such that if a halal person shoots game on a tree whose trunk is in the halal and branch in the haram, compensation is wajib, as in al-Fath. And in al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Hujjah: If he cannot move from branch to branch except by descending and ascending, he prostrates a second time; otherwise one suffices for the two recitations. (And) the gathering changes in (swimming) i.e., in a river, or swimming in a (large) basin, due to the change of gathering. And his statement (in the more correct view) applies to all the issues. And from Muhammad: If the length and width of the basin are like the length and width of the mosque, one prostration suffices. And in al-Khaniyyah: The correct view is that it is repeated. End. Likewise, in treading and going around the mill, in the more correct view, as in al-Fath. (And it does not change) the gathering of hearing and recitation (by the corners of the small house), as in al-Burhan, and likewise if he recites in a vineyard in different places, as in al-Dirayah, and in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. (And) if he recites in the corners of the congregational mosque, one prostration suffices him, and likewise the ruling of the house and the dwelling. And it was said: And in the dwelling, if it is large like the sultan's dwelling, and he recites in one house then in another, another prostration is obligatory. End. Qadikhan has affirmed: The obligation does not repeat if he moves from a corner of the house or the mosque to a corner, except if the dwelling is large like the sultan's dwelling. And if he moves in the congregational mosque from corner to corner, the obligation does not repeat. And if he moves in it from house to house, then in every place where following is valid, it is as one place, and the obligation does not repeat. End. Following.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage details the conditions under which the gathering (majlis) changes for the purpose of sujud al-tilawah. It distinguishes between different environments: in the desert or road, moving three steps changes the gathering; similarly, a weaver moving actively (but not if sitting in one place) changes the gathering. Moving from one branch of a tree to another also changes the gathering, especially if the branches are in different zones (halal/haram). Swimming in a river or large basin changes the gathering, but a small basin may not. However, moving within corners of a small house or a mosque does not change the gathering; one sujud suffices. For a large dwelling like a sultan's palace, moving from one house to another may require a separate sujud. The key principle is that any place where it is valid to follow an imam in prayer is considered one gathering for this ruling.

Key Terms
المجلس (al-majlis): The gathering or place where one is present for recitation; its change may require a separate sujud.
تسدية (tasdiyah): Weaving activity; moving while weaving may change the gathering if the weaver moves actively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, what action changes the gathering for sujud al-tilawah in the desert?
A) Moving three steps.
B) Turning around in place.
C) Changing intention.
D) Remaining stationary.

Key Takeaway
The gathering changes only with significant physical movement in open spaces or special cases, but not within small enclosed areas like a mosque or small house.
