Change of Assembly (Majlis) for Sajdah Tilawah
Ruling with proof: expansions on change of majlis for sajdah tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific movements that change the majlis for sajdah tilawah according to the Hanafi school and distinguish them from movements that do not.

Core Idea
The obligation of sajdah tilawah repeats whenever you physically move to a new place.

When you recite or hear a verse of prostration, a sajdah tilawah becomes wajib. But what if you encounter multiple verses? Does one sajdah suffice? The Hanafi school teaches that the answer depends on whether your 'majlis' (assembly) has changed. This passage from Nur al-Idah and its commentary explains exactly what counts as changing the majlis, with vivid examples from daily life.

Guided Path
1
Recognise the general principle
The passage opens by stating that the majlis changes by moving from it. This is the baseline rule: any physical departure from the original location creates a new majlis, requiring a new sajdah for each verse heard or recited in that new place.
Contrast with staying in the same spot: multiple verses in one majlis require only one sajdah.
2
Apply to specific scenarios
Work through the examples: walking three steps in the desert, weaving while walking, moving from one tree branch to another, and swimming in a river or large basin. In each case, the movement is sufficient to change the majlis, so the sajdah is repeated.
The condition of 'three steps' is a guideline in open areas; in confined spaces, any movement may suffice if it is substantial.
3
Identify the exceptions
Movement within a small house or a mosque does not change the majlis. Similarly, sitting while turning a weaving wheel is considered one place because the person does not relocate. These exceptions are based on the idea that the entire enclosed space is considered a single majlis.
A large basin or river is not considered a single majlis because water allows easy travel and the place is not enclosed.
4
Resolve the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad held that a large basin the size of a mosque suffices for one sajdah. The text declares the soundest opinion (al-ashah) to be that the sajdah is repeated. This is the mufta bihi position.
This dispute shows the active ijtihad within the Hanafi school; the later tarjih favours repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتبدل المجلس بالانتقال منه، ولو كان مُسَدِّياً وبالانتقال من غُصْنٍ إلى غصن، وعَوْمٍ في نهرٍ، أَوْ حَوْضِ كبير، في الأصح. ولا يتبدل بزوايا البيتِ، والمسجدِ، . سجود التلاوة وفي [؟] المجتبى: لا خلاف في وجوب تعظيم اسمه تعالى عند ذكره في كل مرة. ( ويتبدل المجلس بالانتقال منه بخطوات ثلاث في الصحراء والطريق، (ولو كان مُسَدِّياً) في الأصح، بأن يذهب وبيده السدى ويلقيه على أعواد مضروبة في الحائط أو الأرض، لا الذي يكون جالساً على شيء ويدير دوارة يلقي عليها السدى، لأنه جالس في مكان واحد فلا يتكرر الوجوب، كما في «الفتح»، وإنما قيدنا بكونه في الصحراء لما سنذكر، أن البيت الصغير لا يتبدل المجلس بالانتقال فيه إلى زاوية أخرى منه بغير تسدية، فمنعها بالأولى، خصوصاً على الفور بأنها تمنع اختلاف المكان، ولم يقيد ذلك القول بكونها في بيت لما هو الشأن فيها على عادتهم التسدية بغير دواره يدار عليها وهو جالس والضابط أن كل مكان يصح فيه الاقتداء لا يتبدل بالانتقال فيه إلى ناحيته منه، كما سنذكره عن قاضي خان» (وَ) يتبدل المجلس ( بالانتقال من غُصْن) شجرة (إلى غصن) منها في «ظاهر الرواية» وهو الصحيح، كذا في ( التاتارخانية»، وكذا يعتبر الغصن مختلفاً عن الآخر في الحل والحرم، حتى أن الحلال لو رمى صيداً على شجرة أصلها في الحل والغصن في الحرم يجب الجزاء، كذا في «الفتح» ، وفي ( التاتارخانية ) عن ( الحجة ) : إن كان لا يمكنه التحول من غصن إلى غصن إلا بالنزول والصعود يسجد ثانية، وإلا تكفيه واحدة للتلاوتين، (و) يتبدل المجلس في (عوم) أي: سباحة في نهر، أو ) سباحة في حوض (كبير)، لاختلاف المجلس، وقوله ( في الأصح) يرجع إلى المسائل كلها، وعن محمد: إذا كان طول الحوض وعرضه مثل طول المسجد وعرضه، يكفيه سجدة واحدة، وفي ( الخانية ) : الصحيح أنه يتكرر انتهى. وكذا في الدياسة والدور حول الرحى في الأصح، كما في «الفتح».
And the assembly changes by moving from it, even if one is weaving, and by moving from one branch to another, and by swimming in a river or a large basin, according to the soundest opinion. And it does not change by moving within corners of a house or a mosque. ... He said: and the assembly changes by moving from it with three steps in the desert and the road, and if one is weaving, in the soundest view, by going with the warp in his hand and throwing it onto rods fixed in the wall or ground, not one who sits on something and turns a wheel throwing warp onto it, because he is sitting in one place so the obligation is not repeated. ... And the assembly changes by moving from a tree branch to another branch from it according to the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), and it is correct. ... And the assembly changes by swimming in a river or a large basin, due to the difference of place. And his statement 'in the soundest opinion' refers to all the issues. And from Muhammad: if the length and width of the basin are like the length and width of a mosque, one prostration suffices. And in al-Khaniyyah: the correct view is that it is repeated. And likewise in treading and turning around a mill, according to the soundest opinion.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the rulings of sajdah tilawah regarding the change of the 'majlis' (the place where one hears or recites the verse of prostration). It begins by stating the general rule: the majlis changes when one physically moves from it, even if engaged in weaving. The exception is moving within a small house or mosque, which does not change the majlis. The commentary then details three specific cases: (1) Moving three steps in the desert or road changes the majlis, but if weaving while sitting and turning a wheel, the place is considered one, so no repetition. (2) Moving from one tree branch to another changes the majlis, with a condition if climbing is required. (3) Swimming in a river or large basin changes the majlis; a large basin is like a mosque in size, and there is a difference of opinion on repetition. The Hanafi position is that the majlis changes in these cases, and the obligation of sajdah is repeated.

Key Terms
المجلس (al-majlis): The place where one recites or hears a verse of prostration; a change of majlis requires a new sajdah.
تسدية (tasdiyah): The act of weaving warp threads while moving, which changes the majlis if one walks, but not if sitting and turning a wheel.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six core books, considered authoritative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Moving from one corner to another in a small house
B) Moving three steps in the desert
C) Sitting and turning a weaving wheel
D) Reciting two verses while riding a donkey without moving

Key Takeaway
The obligation of sajdah tilawah repeats whenever you physically move to a new place, as defined by the Hanafi school's specific criteria.

One Sajdah Tilawah Suffices: The Hanafi Rule on Majlis Continuity
Lists cases preserving the unity of majlis for sajdah tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the obligation of sajdah tilawah does not repeat within the same majlis and identify which movements do not break continuity.

Core Idea
Frequent movement within a small space does not reset the obligation of sajdah tilawah; only a clear change of location does.

You have recited or heard multiple ayahs of sajdah, and you are moving around — maybe in a small house, a mosque, or a ship. Do you need multiple prostrations? The Hanafi school answers with a clear distinction: as long as you remain within the same 'majlis' (assembly place), one sajdah suffices. This lesson unpacks the rulings and exceptions from the text of Nur al-Idah and its commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
The text states that the 'majlis' does not change by moving through corners of a small house or a congregational mosque. This means the obligation to perform sajdah tilawah applies only once per majlis, regardless of how many sajdah ayahs are recited or heard.
The principle is based on considering the entire area as one place unless it is exceptionally large like a sultan's palace.
2
Recognize the exceptions
Large houses (e.g., a sultan's palace) are not considered one place; moving from one house to another within such a compound requires a new sajdah. This is stated by Qadi Khan as the relied-upon position.
Size matters: a 'small house' is treated as one unit; a large compound is not.
3
List the actions that do NOT change the majlis
The text enumerates many actions: sailing on a ship, performing one or two rak'ahs, taking a sip, eating two morsels, walking two steps, reclining, returning, standing, riding, dismounting, or riding an animal while praying — all within the same place. These do not break the continuity of the majlis.
These are examples of minor movements or actions that do not constitute leaving the original place.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Suppose you recite a sajdah ayah in the corner of a small house, then move to another corner and recite again. According to the Hanafi ruling, one sajdah suffices for both recitations because the majlis has not changed.
If the house were as large as a palace, moving from one building to another would require a separate sajdah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ولا يتبدل) مجلس السماع والتلاوة (بزوايا البيت الصغير، كذا في « البرهان» وكذا لو تلاها في كرم في أماكن مختلفة، كما في « الدراية»، وفي التاتارخانية»، (و) لو قرأها في زوايا (المسجد الجامع، يكفيه سجدة واحدة، وكذا حكم البيت والدار، وقيل: وفي الدار إذا كانت الدار كبيرة، كدار السلطان، فتلا في دار منها ثم في دار أخرى يلزمه سجدة أخرى انتهى. وقد جزم قاضي خان حيث قال : ولا يتكرر الوجوب لو انتقل من زاوية البيت، أو المسجد، إلى زاوية، إلا إذا كانت الدار كبيرة كدار السلطان، وإن انتقل في المسجد الجامع من زاوية إلى زاوية، لا يتكرر الوجوب، وإن انتقل فيه من دار إلى دار، ففي كل موضع يصح يصير كمكان واحد، ولا يتكرر الوجوب انتهى. الاقتداء ولو كبيراً، ولا بسير سفينة، ولا بركعة، وبركعتين وشربةٍ وأكل لقمتين، ومشي خطوتين، ولا باتكاء، وتعود، وقيام، وركوب ونزول في محل تلاوته، ولا بسير دابته مصلياً
And the assembly of hearing and recitation does not change by the corners of a small house, likewise if one recites in a vineyard in different places, as in al-Dirayah and al-TatarKhaniyyah. And if one recites in the corners of a congregational mosque, one prostration suffices, and likewise the ruling of a house and a courtyard. It is said: if the courtyard is large, like the Sultan's palace, and one recites in one house then in another, another prostration is required. Qadi Khan definitively stated: the obligation is not repeated if one moves from a corner of a house or mosque to another corner, unless the house is large like the Sultan's palace; and if one moves in a congregational mosque from corner to corner, the obligation is not repeated, and if one moves from one house to another, each place becomes like one place, and the obligation is not repeated. Iqtida: and even if it is large, nor by sailing of a ship, nor by one rak'ah, nor by two rak'ahs, nor by a sip, nor by eating two morsels, nor by walking two steps, nor by reclining, nor by returning, nor by standing, nor by riding, nor by dismounting in his place of recitation, nor by the walking of his animal while he is praying.

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on when the majlis does not change, meaning one prostration suffices even if multiple verses are recited or heard. It specifies that moving within corners of a small house or a congregational mosque does not change the majlis, because the area is considered one place. The exception is a very large house like a sultan's palace, where moving from one house to another does change it. Then it lists actions that also do not change the majlis: sailing in a ship, performing one or two rak'ahs with multiple recitations, drinking a sip, eating two morsels, walking two steps, reclining, returning, standing, riding, or dismounting, as long as it is in the same place. Similarly, riding an animal while praying does not change the majlis because the prayer necessitates continuity. These rulings are based on the principle that the place is considered one unless there is a clear separation.

Key Terms
زوايا البيت الصغير (zawaya al-bayt al-saghir): Corners of a small house; moving between them does not change the majlis.
المسجد الجامع (al-masjid al-jami'): The congregational mosque; moving within its corners does not change the majlis.
سير سفينة (sayr safinah): The movement of a ship; sailing does not change the majlis.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of sajdah tilawah does not repeat unless the reciter or hearer moves to a clearly separate place, defined by size and customary separation.

The Listener's Sajdah Tilawah When Assembly Changes
Clarifies obligation for listener when his assembly changes while the reciter's remains same

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the listener's obligation in sajdah tilawah when he changes his assembly, and explain the difference in reasoning between those who hold the cause is hearing vs. recitation.

Core Idea
The listener's sajdah obligation repeats when he changes his assembly, even if the reciter remains in one place.

You know that hearing a verse of prostration makes sajdah tilawah wajib. But what if you step out and come back while the reciter is still in the same spot? Does the obligation repeat? This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies that the listener is judged by his own assembly, regardless of the reciter's unity of place. We will explore the legal reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
The passage describes a listener who hears a sajdah verse from a reciter, then leaves the place (changes his assembly), returns, and hears the same verse again. Determine the applied ruling.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi position is that the listener must perform sajdah again for the second hearing. This is stated as a consensus (ijma'an).
Consensus here refers to the Hanafi school agreement on this point.
3
Contrast the two views on the cause (sabab)
Some scholars say the cause is hearing, so each new hearing is a separate cause. The majority (Hanafis) say the cause is recitation, yet the listener's repetition is still required.
The majority's reasoning: unity of place only nullifies repetition for the reciter, not for others.
4
Analyze the majority's talil (reasoning)
Since the reciter's assembly remains one, his obligation does not repeat. However, the listener's assembly is independent; when he changes it, he triggers a new obligation. The text says 'that does not appear in the right of others'.
This shows the listener's obligation is tied to his own assembly, not the reciter's.
5
Note the incomplete example
The passage ends with a hypothetical: 'if he walks behind his master...' – likely illustrating another scenario. Though cut off, the core ruling is clear.
The missing part does not affect the established ruling.

Source Text

And the obligation is repeated upon the listener by his changing of his assembly, while the assembly of the reciter is one. Such that if he heard a reciter in a place, then the listener went outside, then returned and heard him repeating it, the prostration is repeated for the listener by consensus. As for the opinion of some that the cause is hearing, the assembly of hearing is multiple. As for the opinion of the majority that the cause is recitation, the unity of the assembly nullifies multiplicity in the right of the reciter, so that does not appear in the right of others. They said: if he walks behind his master...

Commentary
This passage addresses the obligation of sajdah tilawah for the listener (sami') when he changes his assembly while the reciter remains in one place. The ruling is that the listener must repeat the sajdah if he leaves and returns, even if the reciter's majlis is considered one. The reasoning differs: some say the cause (sabab) is hearing, so each hearing is separate; the majority say the cause is recitation, but since the unity of the reciter's place only applies to him, the listener is judged by his own place. The text mentions an example of walking behind his master, but it is cut off. This shows the Hanafi position that the listener's obligation is independent of the reciter's context.

Key Terms
السامع (al-sami'): The person who hears the verse of prostration; his obligation depends on his own assembly change.
السبب (al-sabab): The cause of obligation for sajdah; disputed whether it is hearing or recitation.
اتحاد المجلس (ittihad al-majlis): The unity of the sitting place that nullifies repetition for the reciter but not for the listener.

When the Reciter's Session Remains Unified for Sajdah Tilawah
Explaining which actions do not break the reciter's session for sajdah tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which actions do not break the reciter's session for sajdah tilawah and explain the relied-upon view regarding repetition in two rak'ahs.

Core Idea
The reciter's session stays unified unless he physically leaves; even prayer actions like rak'ahs do not break it.

This lesson explores the Hanafi concept of 'majlis al-tilāwah' (session of recitation) for the reciter of Qur'anic verses of prostration. The key ruling is that if a reciter repeats a prostration verse multiple times within a single session, only one sajdah is required. The passage lists numerous actions that do not constitute a change of session, including performing multiple rak'ahs, walking a few steps, riding an animal, or being in a large mosque. An important intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding repetition in two rak'ahs illustrates the application of qiyas (analogy) versus istihsan (juristic preference).

Guided Path
1
List the actions that do not change the session
Identify all the actions mentioned (e.g., large mosque, ship, one rak'ah, two rak'ahs, drinking, eating two morsels, walking two steps, reclining, sitting, standing, riding, descending, movement of animal while praying). Note that these keep the session unified.
The list includes both common prayer-related actions and mundane actions like eating or drinking.
2
Understand the dispute on two rak'ahs
Abu Yusuf holds that the session does not change with two rak'ahs, so only one sajdah is needed. Muhammad holds that it changes, requiring a second sajdah by istihsan. Note that Abu Yusuf later retracted to qiyas.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the relied-upon view is that of Abu Yusuf.
3
Analyze the rider case
When two riders recite different verses in prayer and hear each other, each must perform sajdah in prayer for his own recitation. Outside prayer, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, only one sajdah is needed for hearing the other, because the reciter's session is considered unified for necessity.
This case shows the principle that unification of session is extended only for the reciter's own obligation, not for others.
4
Identify the relied-upon position
The text states that in Zahir al-Riwayah, the ruling is that the listener does not repeat sajdah for the recitation of his companion in the same session, and upon this is reliance.
This reinforces the primacy of the unified session for the reciter.

Source Text

ومسجد،
(و) لا يتبدل مجلس التلاوة بزوايا المسجد، (لو) كان ( كبيراً ) ، ولذا لا يضر اتساع الفضاء في صحة الاقتداء فيه، وقيل خلافه: (ولا) يتبدل مجلس التلاوة والسماع (بسير سفينة)، كما لو كانت واقفة، (ولا) يتبدل (بـركـعـة) تكررت فيها التلاوة اتفاقاً قياساً واستحساناً، وكذا في « الـــدرر والغرر»، (و) لا يتبدل ( بركعتين) كررت فيهما على قول أبي يوسف، وعنــد محمـد يـسـجـد ثانياً استحساناً، وهذه [ من ] المسائل التي رجع فيها أبو يوسف عن الاستحسان إلى القياس، انتهى. وإذا كررها في الشفع الثاني من النفل، أو سنة الظهر، يسجد أيضاً، وفي الفـــرض اختلاف بـيـن أبـي يوسف ومحمد، كذا في «القنية » ، فجعل الخلاف في الشفعين، مع أن المذكور [ في ( المجمع » ] وغيره في الركعتين، كذا في شرح « المقدسي» (وَ) لا يتبدل بحصول (شُرْبَةٍ، وَأَكْلِ لُقمتينِ، ومَشي خطوتين) في الصحراء، بخلاف الأكثر، ولا باتكاء، وقُعود، وقيام) بدون مشـي فـي غـيـر بـيـت ( وركوب، ونزول) كائن ذلك ( في محل تلاوتِهِ)، كما في ( الخانية». (ولا) يتبدل المجلس (بسير دابته) إذا كررها (مصلياً)، لجعل المجلس متحداً ضرورة جواز الصلاة، ولو كرر [راكبان] في الصلاة على دابتين آيتين مختلفتين وسمع كل صاحبه، فعلى كل واحد سجدة في الصلاة، لتلاوته فيها، ويسجد خارجها مكرراً بقدر ما سمعه من صاحبه، في رواية ( النوادر » ولاختلاف مكــان صاحبه حقيقة، وإنما جعل متحداً ضرورة جواز صلاته، فلا يظهر الاتحاد في حق غيره، وفي «ظاهر الرواية»: لا يلزمه بقراءة صاحبه إلا سجدة واحدة خارج الصلاة، وعليه الاعتماد، لأنا إن نظرنا إلى مكان السامع فمكانه واحد، وإن نظرنا إلى مكان التالي فمكانه جعل كمكان واحد في حقه، فيجعل كذلك في حق السامع أيضاً؛ لأن السماع بناء على التلاوة. (و) لهذا (يتكرر الوجوب على السامع بتبديل مجلسه، و الحال أنه قد اتحد مجلس التَّالي كأن سمع تالياً بمكان، ثم ذهب السامع إلى الخارج، ثم عاد فسمعه يكررها تكرر على السامع السجود إجماعاً، أمـا عـلـى قـول البعض أن السبب هو السماع فمجلس السماع ،متعدد، وأما على قول الجمهور السبب التلاوة فلأن اتحاد المجلس أبطل التعدد في حق التالي، فلم يظهر ذلك في حق غيره، قالوا: لو مشي وراء سـيـده لا بعكسه، على الأصح.
And if it is large, and not by the movement of a ship, and not by one rak'ah, and by two rak'ahs, and a sip, and eating two morsels, and walking two steps, and not by reclining, and sitting, and standing, and riding and descending in the place of his recitation, and not by the movement of his animal while praying. And the obligation is repeated on the listener by his changing of his assembly, while the assembly of the reciter is unified. And a mosque: (and) the assembly of recitation does not change by the corners of the mosque, if it is large, therefore the spaciousness does not harm the validity of following [the imam] in it, and it was said otherwise. (And) the assembly of recitation and hearing does not change by the movement of a ship, as if it were stationary. (And) it does not change by one rak'ah in which recitation is repeated, by agreement, by analogy and by juristic preference. Similarly in al-Durar wa al-Ghurar. (And) it does not change by two rak'ahs in which it is repeated according to Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad he prostrates a second time by istihsan. and this is among the issues in which Abu Yusuf retracted from istihsan to qiyas. End. And if he repeats it in the second pair of a supererogatory prayer, or the sunnah of Zuhr, he also prostrates. And in the obligatory prayer there is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Thus in al-Qunyah. So he made the difference in the two pairs, while what is mentioned in al-Majma' and others is in two rak'ahs. Thus in Sharh al-Maqdisi. (And) it does not change by the occurrence of a sip, eating two morsels, and walking two steps in an open field, contrary to the majority. And not by reclining, sitting, and standing without walking outside a house, and riding and descending, all that being in the place of his recitation, as in al-Khaniyah. (And) the assembly does not change by the movement of his animal if he repeats it while praying, because the assembly is considered unified due to the necessity of allowing prayer. And if two riders repeat in prayer on two animals two different verses and each hears his companion, then upon each one is a prostration in the prayer due to his own recitation in it, and he prostrates outside it repeatedly according to the number he heard from his companion, in the narration of al-Nawadir, due to the difference of his companion's place in reality, and it is only considered unified due to the necessity of allowing his prayer, so unification does not appear in respect of others. And in Zahir al-Riwayah: nothing is incumbent upon him by the recitation of his companion except one prostration outside the prayer, and upon this is reliance. For if we consider the place of the listener, his place is one. And if we consider the place of the reciter, his place is considered as one place in his right, so it is made so also in the right of the listener, because hearing is built upon recitation. (And) for this reason the obligation is repeated on the listener by his changing his assembly while the assembly of the reciter is unified. For example, if he heard a reciter in a place, then the listener went outside, then returned and heard him repeating it, the prostration is repeated on the listener by consensus. Either according to the saying of some that the cause is hearing, so the hearing assembly is multiple; or according to the saying of the majority that the cause is recitation, then unification of the assembly nullifies multiplicity in the right of the reciter, so that does not appear in respect of others. They said: If he walked behind his master, not the opposite, on the correct view.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining when the 'majlis' (session) for sajdah tilawah changes for the reciter and listener. It begins by listing actions that do NOT change the session for the reciter, even if he recites multiple times: recitation in a large mosque, on a ship, during one or two rak'ahs, while drinking, eating, walking a few steps, reclining, sitting, standing, riding, etc. All these keep the session unified, so only one sajdah is required even if the verse is repeated. The text then discusses the listener: if the listener changes his place (e.g., leaves and returns), the obligation of sajdah repeats for him upon hearing the verse again, even if the reciter's session is unchanged. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding repetition in two rak'ahs: Abu Yusuf holds the session does not change, while Muhammad holds it does and requires a second sajdah by istihsan. The text also clarifies that when two riders recite different verses in prayer and hear each other, each must perform sajdah in prayer for his own recitation, but outside prayer, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, only one sajdah is needed for hearing the other. The relied-upon position is that of Zahir al-Riwayah. The passage concludes with the rule that if the listener's place changes but the reciter's place does not, the obligation repeats; if the opposite (listener stays, reciter changes), there is disagreement: the correct view is that it does not repeat, though some (like Fakhral-Islam) hold it does.

Key Terms
مجلس التلاوة (majlis al-tilāwah): The session or place where Qur'anic recitation occurs; used to determine whether multiple recitations require separate prostrations.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdah al-tilāwah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration from the Qur'an.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a Hanafi method of departing from strict analogy in favor of a more suitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Reciting the verse in two different rak'ahs of the same prayer
B) Leaving the mosque and returning later
C) Walking more than two steps in the desert
D) Riding an animal that moves a considerable distance while praying

Key Takeaway
The reciter's session remains unified unless he physically departs from the place of recitation; therefore, only one sajdah tilawah is wajib for multiple recitations within that session.

When the Listener's Session Changes for Sajdah Tilawah
Explaining when the listener's change of place necessitates a new sajdah tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the listener's change of place triggers a repetition of sajdah tilawah and explain the underlying reason according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The listener's obligation repeats when he changes his place, even if the reciter's session is unified.

This lesson addresses the listener's obligation of sajdah tilawah. While the reciter's session is unified (as seen in the previous lesson), the listener's obligation is tied to his own hearing session. If the listener changes his place (e.g., leaves the room and returns), then upon hearing the verse again, a new sajdah becomes wajib. The passage explains the rationale and cites a case of walking behind a master.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for the listener
The text states that the obligation is repeated on the listener when he changes his assembly (place). This is presented as a distinct rule from the reciter's rule.
The rule is clear: change of listener's place = new sajdah.
2
Understand the example given
The example: listener hears a reciter in a place, then leaves (goes outside), then returns and hears the same reciter repeating the verse. According to consensus, the listener must prostrate twice.
This example illustrates the application of the rule.
3
Note the difference of opinion about the cause
Some say the cause is hearing (samāʿ), so each hearing in a new assembly triggers a new obligation. The majority say the cause is recitation (tilāwah), but the unification of the reciter's session does not extend to the listener.
The majority view is consistent with the general principle that the listener's obligation is independent.
4
Apply the rule to the case of walking behind the master
The text concludes with a ruling: if the listener walks behind his master (i.e., follows him), it does not count as a change of session, but if he walks in front, it does (on the correct view).
This is a specific application showing that following does not break the session.

Source Text

(ولا) يتبدل المجلس (بسير دابته) إذا كررها (مصلياً)، لجعل المجلس متحداً ضرورة جواز الصلاة، ولو كرر [راكبان] في الصلاة على دابتين آيتين مختلفتين وسمع كل صاحبه، فعلى كل واحد سجدة في الصلاة، لتلاوته فيها، ويسجد خارجها مكرراً بقدر ما سمعه من صاحبه، في رواية ( النوادر » ولاختلاف مكــان صاحبه حقيقة، وإنما جعل متحداً ضرورة جواز صلاته، فلا يظهر الاتحاد في حق غيره، وفي «ظاهر الرواية»: لا يلزمه بقراءة صاحبه إلا سجدة واحدة خارج الصلاة، وعليه الاعتماد، لأنا إن نظرنا إلى مكان السامع فمكانه واحد، وإن نظرنا إلى مكان التالي فمكانه جعل كمكان واحد في حقه، فيجعل كذلك في حق السامع أيضاً؛ لأن السماع بناء على التلاوة. (و) لهذا (يتكرر الوجوب على السامع بتبديل مجلسه، و الحال أنه قد اتحد مجلس التَّالي كأن سمع تالياً بمكان، ثم ذهب السامع إلى الخارج، ثم عاد فسمعه يكررها تكرر على السامع السجود إجماعاً، أمـا عـلـى قـول البعض أن السبب هو السماع فمجلس السماع ،متعدد، وأما على قول الجمهور السبب التلاوة فلأن اتحاد المجلس أبطل التعدد في حق التالي، فلم يظهر ذلك في حق غيره، قالوا: لو مشي وراء سـيـده لا بعكسه، على الأصح.
And if it is large, and not by the movement of a ship, and not by one rak'ah, and by two rak'ahs, and a sip, and eating two morsels, and walking two steps, and not by reclining, and sitting, and standing, and riding and descending in the place of his recitation, and not by the movement of his animal while praying. And the obligation is repeated on the listener by his changing of his assembly, while the assembly of the reciter is unified. And a mosque: (and) the assembly of recitation does not change by the corners of the mosque, if it is large, therefore the spaciousness does not harm the validity of following [the imam] in it, and it was said otherwise. (And) the assembly of recitation and hearing does not change by the movement of a ship, as if it were stationary. (And) it does not change by one rak'ah in which recitation is repeated, by agreement, by analogy and by juristic preference. Similarly in al-Durar wa al-Ghurar. (And) it does not change by two rak'ahs in which it is repeated according to Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad he prostrates a second time by istihsan. and this is among the issues in which Abu Yusuf retracted from istihsan to qiyas. End. And if he repeats it in the second pair of a supererogatory prayer, or the sunnah of Zuhr, he also prostrates. And in the obligatory prayer there is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Thus in al-Qunyah. So he made the difference in the two pairs, while what is mentioned in al-Majma' and others is in two rak'ahs. Thus in Sharh al-Maqdisi. (And) it does not change by the occurrence of a sip, eating two morsels, and walking two steps in an open field, contrary to the majority. And not by reclining, sitting, and standing without walking outside a house, and riding and descending, all that being in the place of his recitation, as in al-Khaniyah. (And) the assembly does not change by the movement of his animal if he repeats it while praying, because the assembly is considered unified due to the necessity of allowing prayer. And if two riders repeat in prayer on two animals two different verses and each hears his companion, then upon each one is a prostration in the prayer due to his own recitation in it, and he prostrates outside it repeatedly according to the number he heard from his companion, in the narration of al-Nawadir, due to the difference of his companion's place in reality, and it is only considered unified due to the necessity of allowing his prayer, so unification does not appear in respect of others. And in Zahir al-Riwayah: nothing is incumbent upon him by the recitation of his companion except one prostration outside the prayer, and upon this is reliance. For if we consider the place of the listener, his place is one. And if we consider the place of the reciter, his place is considered as one place in his right, so it is made so also in the right of the listener, because hearing is built upon recitation. (And) for this reason the obligation is repeated on the listener by his changing his assembly while the assembly of the reciter is unified. For example, if he heard a reciter in a place, then the listener went outside, then returned and heard him repeating it, the prostration is repeated on the listener by consensus. Either according to the saying of some that the cause is hearing, so the hearing assembly is multiple; or according to the saying of the majority that the cause is recitation, then unification of the assembly nullifies multiplicity in the right of the reciter, so that does not appear in respect of others. They said: If he walked behind his master, not the opposite, on the correct view.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining when the 'majlis' (session) for sajdah tilawah changes for the reciter and listener. It begins by listing actions that do NOT change the session for the reciter, even if he recites multiple times: recitation in a large mosque, on a ship, during one or two rak'ahs, while drinking, eating, walking a few steps, reclining, sitting, standing, riding, etc. All these keep the session unified, so only one sajdah is required even if the verse is repeated. The text then discusses the listener: if the listener changes his place (e.g., leaves and returns), the obligation of sajdah repeats for him upon hearing the verse again, even if the reciter's session is unchanged. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding repetition in two rak'ahs: Abu Yusuf holds the session does not change, while Muhammad holds it does and requires a second sajdah by istihsan. The text also clarifies that when two riders recite different verses in prayer and hear each other, each must perform sajdah in prayer for his own recitation, but outside prayer, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, only one sajdah is needed for hearing the other. The relied-upon position is that of Zahir al-Riwayah. The passage concludes with the rule that if the listener's place changes but the reciter's place does not, the obligation repeats; if the opposite (listener stays, reciter changes), there is disagreement: the correct view is that it does not repeat, though some (like Fakhral-Islam) hold it does.

Key Terms
مجلس التلاوة (majlis al-tilāwah): The session or place where Qur'anic recitation occurs; used to determine whether multiple recitations require separate prostrations.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdah al-tilāwah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration from the Qur'an.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a Hanafi method of departing from strict analogy in favor of a more suitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One sajdah, because the reciter's session is unified.
B) Two sajdahs, because the assembly changed.
C) One sajdah, because the listener is still hearing the same reciter.
D) Two sajdahs, only if the listener changes his place during the recitation.

Key Takeaway
The listener's obligation of sajdah tilawah repeats when he changes his physical assembly, regardless of the reciter's session unity.

Ethical Rulings for the Verse of Prostration
Ethical rulings for the verse of prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four ethical rulings related to reciting a verse of prostration and apply them in a recitation scenario.

Core Idea
It is disliked to skip a prostration verse in a surah, but recommended to add verses and recite quietly near those unfit for prostration.

In the Hanafi school, the recitation of the Quran carries certain adab (ethical norms). One such norm relates to the verses of prostration (ayat al-sajdah). This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines four clear rulings: when skipping a prostration verse is disliked, when adding verses is recommended, and when reciting quietly is recommended. Understanding these provides practical guidance for daily recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling: dislike of skipping prostration verse
Read the phrase 'ukriha an yaqra'a surah wa yada'a ayah al-sajdah' — it is disliked to recite a surah and omit the prostration verse. Recognize that this is a karahah tanzihiyyah (slight dislike) according to the Hanafi classification.
The dislike arises from the semblance of avoiding prostration.
2
Note the exception: opposite is not disliked
The text explicitly says 'la aksuhu' — the opposite is not disliked. That is, reciting only the prostration verse (without other verses) is not disliked; it is actually virtuous.
This corrects a common misunderstanding.
3
Apply the recommendation to add verses
'wa nudi ba dammu ayah aw akthar ilayha' — it is recommended to add one or more verses before or after the prostration verse. This is sunnah/mustahabb.
The purpose is to avoid the appearance of giving preference to the prostration verse over other Quran.
4
Apply the recommendation to conceal the verse
'wa nudi ba ikhfauha an ghayr mutaahhbin laha' — it is recommended to recite quietly when around those not prepared for prostration (e.g., menstruating women, those in janabah).
This shows consideration for others' inability to perform sajdah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكُرَهَ أن يقرأ سورةً ، ويَدَعَ آية السجدة، لا عكسه. ونُدِبَ ضَمَّ آيةٍ، أو أكثر إليها. ونُدِبَ إخفاؤها عن غير متأهّب لها..
And it is disliked that he recites a Surah and leaves out the verse of prostration, not the opposite. And it is recommended to join a verse, or more, to it. And it is recommended to conceal it from those not prepared for it.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage provides ethical rulings (ahkam adabiyyah) regarding the verse of prostration (ayat al-sajdah). It states four rules: (1) It is makruh (disliked) to recite a Surah while deliberately omitting the verse of prostration from it, because this resembles disdain for the verse and implies fleeing from its obligation. (2) The opposite—reciting the prostration verse alone without other verses—is not disliked; it is actually a virtuous act. (3) It is mustahabb (recommended) to add one or two verses before or after the prostration verse, to avoid the appearance of preferring it over other Qur'anic verses. (4) It is recommended to recite the prostration verse quietly (ikhfa') in the presence of those who might not be prepared for it (e.g., menstruating women or those in a state of janabah), out of consideration for them. The 'dislike' and 'recommendation' are based on the teachings of the Salaf and are not supported by explicit dalil in this text.

Key Terms
آية السجدة (āyah al-sajdah): Any verse of the Qur'an that requires prostration upon recitation or hearing; there are fourteen such verses in the Hanafi school.
كراهة (karāhah): Dislike; a ruling that is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) or makruh tahrimi (close to haram). Here it is makruh tanzihi (not sinful but contrary to the better practice).
ندب (nadb): Recommendation; an act that is not obligatory but is praiseworthy to perform.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting only the verse of prostration (without other verses)?
A) It is makruh tanzihi.
B) It is mustahabb and not disliked.
C) It is wajib.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Skipping a prostration verse in a surah is slightly disliked, while reciting it alone or adding verses is recommended, and concealing it near those unable to prostrate is also recommended.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Repetition of Sajdat al-Tilawah for the Listener
Intra-Hanafi dispute on repetition of sajdat al-tilawah for the listener

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether sajdat al-tilawah repeats for the listener when the reciter changes his assembly, and state the position of each authority along with the tarjih.

Core Idea
The obligation for the listener may or may not repeat depending on whether the cause is hearing or recitation.

This lesson explores a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement: when a reciter repeats a sajda verse after leaving and returning, while the listener remains in the same assembly, does the listener need a second prostration? The answer depends on what is considered the cause (sabab) of the obligation for the listener—hearing or recitation. Al-Hidayah and Fakhr al-Islam offer opposing analyses, and the mufta bihi leans toward repetition, though not without hesitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Visualize the case: a reciter recites a sajda verse, leaves, returns, and recites it again. The listener stays throughout. Does the listener owe one prostration or two?
The scenario contrasts the reciter's changing assembly with the listener's fixed assembly.
2
State the two positions
According to the author of al-Hidayah, one prostration suffices (no repetition). According to Fakhr al-Islam and al-Isbijabi, a second prostration is required (repetition).
These are both within the Hanafi school; both rely on valid usul reasoning.
3
Trace the sabab and shart reasoning
Al-Hidayah identifies the cause (sabab) as hearing; the listener's hearing has not changed, so no new obligation. Fakhr al-Islam identifies the cause as recitation; hearing is only a condition (shart). Since recitation recurred, a new obligation arises.
This is a usul-level distinction: sabab vs. shart.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in the given scenario, al-Hidayah says one prostration, Fakhr al-Islam says two. A person acting on either view would perform differently.
The mufta bihi according to al-Diraya is the repetition view, but with reservation.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Al-Diraya states 'upon it is the fatwa', but Sheikh Akmal al-Din transmits it with 'it was said', showing hesitation. Thus the dispute is not definitively settled.
This nuance affects real-world fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو يكررها راكباً، تكررت عليه لا على سيده، ولا يتكرر الوجوب على السامع بعكسه وهو اتحاد مجلس السامع واختلاف مجلس التالي، بأن تلا فذهب، ثم عاد فكررها وسمعها الجالس أيضاً، تكفيه سجدة على الأصح لما قلنا أن السبب في حقه السماع، ولم يتبدل مجلسه، كما في «الهداية»، وقال في «الدراية»: قيل: يتكرر وهو اختيار «الإسبيجابي»، وعليه الفتوى، انتهى. إلا أن الشيخ أكمل الدين رحمه الله نقله بصيغة قيل وعليه الفتوى، فكأنه لا يميل إلى هذا القول، وهو قول فخر الإسلام: أن مجلس التالي إذا تكرر دون السامع يتكرر الوجوب على السامع، لأن الحكم يضاف إلى السبب وهو التلاوة لا إلى الشرط وهو السماع، وهذا هو الذي عليه الجمهور، لأن الصحيح أن السبب في حق السامع هو التلاوة كالتالي، والسماع شرط عمل التلاوة في حق السامع انتهى، وليس في الحديث بيان السبب، بل بيان الوجوب على السامع. فصاحب «الهداية» يختار عدم التكرار لجعل السبب السماع، وفخر الإسلام بخلافه يختار التكرار ويجعل التلاوة السبب.
And he repeats it while riding, it repeats upon him but not upon his master. And (it does not) repeat the obligation upon the listener in its opposite, which is the unification of the listener's assembly and the differing of the reciter's assembly: that he recited, then left, then returned and repeated it, and the sitting person also heard it, one prostration suffices him according to the most correct opinion, because we said that the cause in his right is hearing, and his assembly has not changed, as in al-Hidayah. And he said in al-Diraya: It was said it repeats, and it is the choice of al-Isbijabi, and upon it is the fatwa, end. Except that Sheikh Akmal al-Din, may Allah have mercy on him, transmitted it in the form of 'it was said, and upon it the fatwa', so it is as if he does not incline to this statement, and it is the statement of Fakhr al-Islam: that if the reciter's assembly repeats without the listener, the obligation repeats upon the listener, because the ruling is attributed to the cause which is recitation, not to the condition which is hearing. And this is what the majority are upon, because the correct view is that the cause in the right of the listener is recitation, like the reciter, and hearing is a condition for the operation of recitation in the right of the listener. End. And there is no statement in the hadith of the cause, rather a statement of the obligation upon the listener. So the author of al-Hidayah chooses non-repetition by making the cause hearing, and Fakhr al-Islam contrary to him chooses repetition and makes recitation the cause.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the repetition of sajdat al-tilawah upon the listener when the reciter repeats the verse after changing his assembly while the listener remains in the same assembly. The passage begins with the scenario of repeating the verse while riding and then focuses on the listener. The author first states the ruling according to al-Hidayah: the obligation does not repeat because the cause of obligation for the listener is hearing, and since he has not changed his assembly, the hearing does not constitute a new cause. He then cites al-Diraya, which reports another view that it does repeat, chosen by al-Isbijabi, and that the fatwa is upon that. However, Sheikh Akmal al-Din transmits this with hesitation, suggesting he may not favour it. Then Fakhr al-Islam's position is elaborated: repetition occurs because the cause is recitation, not hearing; hearing is only a condition for the activation of the cause in the listener. The passage concludes that the hadith does not specify the cause, so the difference stems from identifying the cause. The author of al-Hidayah makes hearing the cause, leading to non-repetition, while Fakhr al-Islam makes recitation the cause, leading to repetition. The practical consequence is that in the described scenario, according to al-Hidayah, one prostration suffices, whereas according to Fakhr al-Islam, a second prostration is required. The fatwa is reportedly on the side of repetition, but with some reservation.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): The effective cause or reason that necessitates the obligation of sajdat al-tilawah. In this context, it is debated whether it is recitation (tilaawah) or hearing (samaa').
الشرط (al-shart): A condition that enables the operation of the cause but is not the cause itself. In this text, hearing (samaa') is considered a condition by Fakhr al-Islam, not the cause.
المجلس (al-majlis): The sitting place or assembly. The change or unity of the assembly (majlis) of the reciter and listener is a key factor in determining repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hearing the verse
B) The recitation of the verse by the reciter
C) The intention to hear
D) The prostration of the reciter

Key Takeaway
The identification of the cause (sabab) – hearing vs. recitation – determines whether sajdat al-tilawah repeats for the listener when the reciter changes his assembly.

Skipping the Verse of Prostration
States the ruling on intentionally skipping the verse of prostration when reciting a surah, and the recommendation to add other verses and conceal the prostration verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on skipping a prostration verse and identify the recommended practice of adding verses.

Core Idea
Skipping a prostration verse is disliked, but reciting it alone is not; adding verses is recommended.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on deliberately omitting the verse of prostration when reciting a surah. It also explains the recommended additions to avoid any misunderstanding about the superiority of certain verses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that intentionally skipping a prostration verse when reciting its surah is makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful).
The dislike applies whether in or outside prayer.
2
Note the scope and difference of opinion
Understand that some early scholars limited the dislike to outside prayer, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position extends it to both settings, based on Imam Muhammad's narration.
3
Recognize the opposite ruling
Reciting the prostration verse alone is not disliked; rather, it is considered hastening to the act of prostration.
4
Understand the recommendation to add verses
To avoid the impression that prostration verses are superior, it is recommended (mandub) to join one or two verses before or after it.
Qadi Khan included adding verses after as well.
5
Recall the etiquette of concealment
It is recommended to recite the prostration verse softly if listeners are not prepared, out of compassion, unless the reciter intends to exhort them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكُرِهَ أن يقرأ سورةً ويَدَعَ آية السجدة منها، لأنه يشبه الاستنكاف عنها، ويوهم الفرار من لزومها، وهجران بعض القرآن وكله مكروه، سواء كان في الصلاة أو خارجها. قال الشيخ الإمام فخر الإسلام علي البزدوي في شرح الجامع الصغير: ومن الناس من كره ذلك خارج الصلاة ولم يكرهه في الصلاة ولكن هذا خلاف الرواية. قال محمد رحمه الله في الجامع الصغير: وأكره أن يقرأ السورة في الصلاة أو غيرها ويدع آية السجدة. كذا في التاتارخانية. ولا يكره عكسه وهو أن يفرد آية السجدة بالقراءة؛ لأنه مبادرة إليها. ولكن ندب ضم آية أو ضم أكثر من آية إليها، قال محمد: أحب إلي أن يقرأ قبلها آية أو آيتين لدفع وهم التفضيل، أي تفضيل آي السجدة على غيرها، إذ الكل من حيث أنه كلام الله تعالى في رتبة واحدة، وإن كان اشتماله على ذكر صفات الحق جل جلاله زيادة فضيلة باعتبار المذكور، لا باعتباره من حيث هو قرآن. كذا في الفتح. وقال قاضي خان: إن قرأ معها آية أو آيتين فهو أحب، وهذا أعم من الأول لأنه يشمل قراءتهما بعدها. ونُدِبَ إخفاؤها عن غير متأهب لها، شفقة على السامعين، وقيل: إن وقع في قلبه عدم الإشفاق عليهم جهر حثاً لهم على الطاعة.
And it is disliked that one recites a surah and leaves out the verse of prostration from it, because it resembles disdain for it, and it gives the impression of fleeing from its obligation, and abandoning part of the Quran and all of it is disliked, whether in prayer or outside it. Sheikh Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: Among the people are those who disliked that outside prayer and did not dislike it in prayer, but this is against the narration. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: I dislike that one recites the surah in prayer or other than it and leaves the verse of prostration. Likewise in al-Tatarakhaniyyah. And its opposite is not disliked: that one recites only the verse of prostration, because it is a hastening to it. But it is recommended to join a verse or more than a verse to it. Muhammad said: I prefer that he recites before it a verse or two to remove the impression of preference, i.e., preferring the verses of prostration over others, since all, from the perspective that it is the speech of Allah Almighty, are in one rank, even if their inclusion of mentioning the attributes of the Truth, may His glory be exalted, is an extra virtue by virtue of the mentioned thing, not by virtue of the fact that it is Quran. Likewise in al-Fath. And Qadi Khan said: If he recites with it a verse or two, it is more beloved, and this is more general than the first because it includes reciting them after it. And it is recommended to conceal it from those who are not prepared for it, out of compassion for the listeners, and it is said: if he feels in his heart no compassion for them, he may recite it aloud to urge them to obedience.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings related to the recitation of the verse of prostration (ayat al-sajdah). The main ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) to recite a surah while deliberately skipping the verse of prostration that is part of it, because this resembles disdain or avoidance of the obligation. This applies both inside and outside prayer. The author cites Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, who notes a difference of opinion: some only dislike it outside prayer, but the correct narration (from Imam Muhammad) includes dislike in both situations. The opposite—reciting only the prostration verse alone—is not disliked; rather, it is a commendable act. However, it is recommended (mandub) to add one or two verses before or after the prostration verse to avoid the impression that the prostration verses are superior to other Quranic verses, since all of the Quran is the speech of Allah. Scholars like Qadi Khan extend the recommendation to include reciting additional verses after the prostration verse. Finally, it is recommended to recite the prostration verse quietly or subtly if there are listeners who may not be prepared for it, out of compassion, unless the reciter intends to exhort them audibly. This reflects the Hanafi concern for the listener's state.

Key Terms
آية السجدة (ayat al-sajdah): A verse of the Quran that requires prostration (sajdat al-tilawah) upon recitation or hearing.
مندوب (mandub): A recommended act; doing it is rewarded, not doing it is not sinful. Here, adding verses before or after the prostration verse is mandub.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on reciting only the verse of prostration (without adding other verses)?
A) Disliked (makruh)
B) Forbidden (haram)
C) Not disliked, and it is recommended to add verses
D) Obligatory (wajib)

Key Takeaway
Skipping a prostration verse is disliked, and it is recommended to add other verses around it to avoid the impression of superiority.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Sajdat al-Tilawah: Conditions, Etiquettes, and the Timing Dispute
Describes the recommended actions and conditions for performing sajdat al-tilawah, including standing, following the reciter, and prerequisites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for sajdat al-tilawah, explain the Hanafi position on delaying prostration, and identify the dispute with Zufar.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah is wajib, not fard — conditions mirror prayer but the opening takbir is sunnah.

This lesson unpacks the conditions and recommended etiquettes of sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) as taught in the Hanafi school. You will learn what makes the prostration valid, when it can be delayed, and how the listener should follow the reciter. We will also examine an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding timing, particularly when a rider dismounts and then delays the prostration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sajdat al-tilawah is a wajib act triggered by reciting or hearing a prostration verse.
Wajib, not fard, due to zanni dalil.
2
List the conditions for validity
The conditions mirror those of prayer: taharah, covering awrah, facing qibla, intention. Notably, the opening takbir (tahrimah) is not required.
Tahrimah is sunnah here.
3
Examine the recommended etiquettes
Standing before prostrating is recommended; the listener should not raise the head before the reciter, though it is not real iqtida'.
4
Analyze the dispute with Zufar
The issue: if a rider dismounts, delays prostration, then mounts and gestures. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say valid (considering time of recitation); Zufar says obligatory immediately upon dismount.
The Hanafi response distinguishes from 'Asr prayer of the previous day.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), though a fatwa from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl follows Abu Yusuf's other narration.
Authority: zahir al-riwayah with later variance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونُدِبَ القيام، ثم السجود لها. روي ذلك، ولأن الخرور الذي مدح به أولئك فيه أكمل. وكذا لو كان راكباً فتلاها، الأولى له النزول يسجدها على الأرض، فلو نزل فلم يسجد ثم ركب فأومأ بها جاز، اعتباراً لوقت تلاوتها، خلافاً لزفر: هو يقول: لما نزل وجب أداؤها على الأرض، فصار كما لو تلاها على الأرض. وكذا لو تلاها عند الشروق فلم يسجد أجزأنا سجودها في وقت الزوال والغروب خلافاً لزفر لأنه أداها كما وجبت ناقصة، وعنده كما لو أدرك وقتاً كاملاً وجبت فيه بصفة الكمال كعصر أمس، ونحن نقول: عصر أمس يضاف إلى كل وقت فافترقا. كذا في البرهان. وحكاه في التاتارخانية عن أبي يوسف ومحمد، ثم قال: وذكر في مواضع أخرى عن أبي يوسف أنه لا يجوز، وبه كان يفتي الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل. وندب أن لا يرفع السامع رأسه منها قبل رفع رأس تاليها؛ لأنه الأصل في إيجابها، فيتبع في أدائها، وليس هو حقيقة اقتداء، ولذا لا يؤمر التالي بالتقدم، ولا يؤمر السامعون بالاصطفاف، فيسجدون معه حيث كانوا وكيف كانوا. قال شيخ الإسلام: وفي النوازل يتقدم ويصطف الناس خلفه، كذا في الدراية. وقال الكمال: وليس هذا اقتداء حقيقة بل صورة، ولذا يستحب أن لا يسبقوه بالوضع والرفع، فلو كان حقيقة لوجب، ولفسدت سجدتهم بفساد سجدة التالي بسبب من الأسباب وهما منتفيان. انتهى. وذكر أبو بكر: أن المرأة تصلح إماماً للرجل فيها، كذا في الدراية. وشُرِطَ لصحتِها شرائط الصلاة في الساجد، وهي: الطهارة من الحدث والخبث، وستر العورة، واستقبال القبلة، وتحريها عند الاشتباه، والنية، إلا التحريمة، فلا تشترط لأن التكبير سنة، كما سنذكره. وفي التاتارخانية عن الحجة: ويستحب للتالي أو السامع إذا لم يمكنه السجود أن يقول: سمعنا وأطعنا غفرانك ربنا وإليك المصير. تنبيه: قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني: قال مشايخنا رحمهم الله السبيل في زماننا إذا قرأها الإمام في صلاة الجمعة أن لا يسجد لها لامتداد الصفوف وكثرة القوم، فإن المكبر إذا كبر لها يظن القوم أنه كبر للركوع فيركعون، وفيه من الفتنة ما لا يخفى، وهكذا في صلاة العيد. قال شمس الأئمة: هكذا سألت القاضي رحمه الله: هل يكره للإمام أن يقرأ سورة فيها سجدة يوم الجمعة كما يكره في ...
And standing is recommended, then prostrating for it. That was narrated, and because the falling (prostration) that those were praised for is more complete in it. Likewise, if he was riding and recited it, it is better for him to dismount and prostrate on the ground. If he dismounted and did not prostrate, then mounted and gestured towards it, it is valid, considering the time of its recitation, contrary to Zufar: he says: when he dismounted, its performance on the ground became obligatory, so it is as if he recited it on the ground. Likewise, if he recited it at sunrise and did not prostrate, its prostration is valid for us at the time of noon and sunset, contrary to Zufar, because he performed it as it was obligated deficiently, and according to him, just as if he reached a complete time in which it was obligated with the description of completeness, like yesterday's Asr. And we say: yesterday's Asr is added to each time, so they differ. Likewise in al-Burhan. And al-Tatarakhaniyyah narrated it from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, then said: And it was mentioned in other places from Abu Yusuf that it is not valid, and with that the Sheikh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl used to give fatwa. And it is recommended that the listener not raise his head from it before the raising of the head of the reciter, because he is the originator of its obligation, so he is followed in its performance, and it is not real following. Hence, the reciter is not commanded to step forward, nor are the listeners commanded to line up, so they prostrate with him wherever and however they are. Sheikh al-Islam said: In al-Nawazil, he steps forward and the people line up behind him, similarly in al-Dirayah. And al-Kamal said: This is not real following but in form, hence it is recommended that they not precede him in place and raise, for if it were real, it would be obligatory, and their prostration would be invalidated by the invalidity of the reciter's prostration due to some cause, and both are negated. End. And Abu Bakr mentioned that the woman is valid as an imam for the man in it, similarly in al-Dirayah. And for its validity, the conditions of prayer are required in the one prostrating, which are: purification from major and minor impurity and from filth, covering the 'awrah, facing the qibla, striving to determine it when unclear, and intention, except for the opening takbir, for it is not required because the takbir is sunnah, as we will mention. And in al-Tatarakhaniyyah from al-Hujjah: It is recommended for the reciter or listener, if he cannot prostrate, to say: 'We hear and we obey, Your forgiveness our Lord, and to You is the return.' Note: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: Our teachers (may Allah have mercy on them) said: The way in our time, if the Imam recites it in Friday prayer, is not to prostrate for it due to the extended rows and the multitude of people, for if the one who says 'Allahu Akbar' says it for it, the people will think that he said the takbir for bowing and they will bow, and in that there is no small fitna. Similarly, in the Eid prayer. Shams al-A'imma said: I asked the judge (may Allah have mercy on him): Is it disliked for the Imam to recite a surah that has a prostration verse on Friday, just as it is disliked in...
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage covers the etiquettes (adab) and conditions (shurut) of sajdat al-tilawah. It begins with the recommendation to stand before prostrating, following a narration from Aisha (radhiyallahu 'anha) and because the falling in prostration is more complete. For a rider, it is recommended to dismount and prostrate on the ground; if he dismounts but does not prostrate immediately, then mounts and gestures, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but a difference with Zufar is noted. Similarly, if one recites at sunrise and delays the prostration to noon or sunset, it is valid according to the Hanafis, but Zufar disagrees. The Hanafi response compares it to the 'Asr prayer of the previous day. Then the text discusses the listener's behavior: it is recommended not to raise the head before the reciter, but this is not real following (iqtida'), so the reciter does not need to step forward, nor do the listeners line up. However, in Nawazil (a later work), it is recommended to line up. The text also mentions that a woman can lead a man in this prostration. Then the conditions for validity are stated: all conditions of prayer (taharah from hadath and najasah, covering 'awrah, facing qibla, intention) except the opening takbir (tahrimah), because the takbir is sunnah. Finally, a practical note from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani advises that in Friday and Eid prayers, due to large crowds, the Imam should avoid reciting a prostration verse or should not prostrate to avoid confusion and fitna. This reflects the Hanafi pragmatism in avoiding public disorder.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates prayer. In sajdat al-tilawah, it is not required for validity.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in prayer. In sajdat al-tilawah, the listener follows the reciter but it is not real iqtida', so the rulings of prayer following do not fully apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the validity of sajdat al-tilawah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Purification from hadath and najasah
B) Facing the qibla
C) The opening takbir (tahrimah)
D) Covering the 'awrah

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawah is wajib; its conditions mirror prayer except the opening takbir, and delaying it is permissible within the Hanafi school.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Ruling and Conditions of Sajdat al-Tilawah
Opening segment establishing ruling and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdat al-tilawah, identify its conditions, and apply the exception of takbirat al-ihram.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah is a stressed sunnah, not wajib; its conditions mirror prayer except the opening takbir.

This lesson extracts the foundational ruling from the commentary: the prostration of recitation is recommended (sunnah muakkadah) for both reciter and listener. The author establishes the proof from the action of Aisha (radiyallahu anha) and lists the conditions for validity, highlighting the unique Hanafi position that takbirat al-ihram is not among them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm of sajdat al-tilawah
Read the beginning of the passage and note that the author uses 'undiba' (it is recommended) for both standing and prostration, indicating a sunnah level. Confirm that the school classifies it as sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
The hadith of Aisha is cited as proof; it is a mursal hadith, hence zanni.
2
List the conditions for validity
The text states 'Shurita li-sihhatiha sharait al-salat illa al-tahrimah'. Extract the conditions: purity from hadath and khabath, covering awrah, facing qibla, effort when in doubt, and intention. Note the exception.
Tahrimah (opening takbir) is excluded because the takbir for prostration is sunnah, not a pillar.
3
Distinguish between fard and sunnah in conditions
Understand that the conditions are the same as for prayer (fard/wajib), but the takbir is not a condition for validity; it is a sunnah. This is a key Hanafi distinction.
Other schools may require takbirat al-ihram; Hanafis relax this requirement.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a person who recites a prostration verse without wudu. The prostration would be invalid because purity is a condition, even though the act itself is sunnah.
The ruling anatomy below formalizes this.

في بيان ما يبطل هذه السجدة وما لا يبطلها: إذا تكلم فيها، أو قهقه، أو أحدث متعمداً، أو خطأ، فعليه إعادتها اعتباراً بالصلوية، ولا وضوء عليه في القهقهة فيها اتفاقاً، لما قدمناه في الطهارة، وإن سبقه الحدث توضأ وأعادها، قال شيخ الإسلام هذا الجواب مستقيم على قول محمد رحمه الله، فإن عنده تمام السجدة بوضع الجبهة ورفعها، فإذا أحدث فيها أو ضحك أو تكلم أعادها، أما على قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله : تمام السجدة بوضع الجبهة لا غير، فإذا وضعت الجبهة فقد تمت السجدة، وإن قل، فكيف يتصور القهقهة أو الكلام ونحوه فيها، وإذا ضحـك بـعـد ذلك فقد ضحك بعد تمام السجدة، فلا يلزمه الإعادة، كذا في ( التاتارخانية»، قال الكمال: وهـو حسن، انتهى. وقد يقال: الرفع وإن لم يكن من تمامها فما دام في الوضع فهو فيها، كمن أطال القراءة والقيام وهو في الفرض، فإذا قهقه أو عمل المنافي حصل في حقيقة السجود، مبطل الجزء الملاقي له، فيبطل الكل ببطلانه، فليتأمل. ( وكيفيتها ) أي : سجدة التلاوة أن يسجد سجدة واحدة) كائنة (بين تكبيرتين) تكبيرة للوضع وتكبيرة للرفع، قال في ( البحر » : وفي « السراج الوهاج» : إذا أراد السجود ينويها بقلبه ويقول بلسانه أسجد لله سجدة الله أكبر، كما يقول: أصلي الله تعالى صلاة كذا، وقدمنا أن النطق بالنية طريقة استحبها المشايخ، وليست منقولة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا عــن خلفائه انتهى. وفي ( الهداية » : ومن أراد السجود كبر ولم يرفع يديه وسجد، ثم كبر ورفع رأسه، اعتباراً بسجدة الصلاة، وهو المروي عن ابن مسعود .انتهى. ورواه ابن أبي شيبة، عن إبراهيم، والحسن، وأبي قلابة، وابن سيرين كذا بخط شيخ مشايخنا انتهى. وفي ( الذخيرة» : هو المختار، وقيل: يكبر في الابتداء بلا خلاف، وفي الانتهاء خلاف، يكبر عند أبي يوسف لا عند محمد، وفي المحيط » : روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه لا يكبر مع الانحطاط ، وفي ( الحجة » : قال بعض المشايخ: لو سجد ولم يكبر يخرج عن العهدة، وهذا يعلم ولا يعمل به لما فيه من مخالفة السنة، انتهى. وقال شيخ انتهى.
(1) فعن أم سلمة الأزدية قالت: «رأيت عائشة تقرأ في المصحف فإذا مرت بسجدة قامت فسجدت» أخرجه البيهقي في السنن الكبرى (326/2).
Standing is recommended, then prostration for it. The listener should not raise his head from it before the reciter. The reciter is not commanded to go forward, nor are the listeners commanded to line up; they prostrate as they are. Conditions for its validity are the conditions of prayer, except the takbirat al-ihram. Aisha (1). Out of compassion for them, recite loudly to urge them to obedience. Standing is recommended for one who recited while sitting, then prostration for it; that is narrated and because the falling down praised for those [people] is more complete in it. Likewise, if one was riding and recited it, it is better for him to dismount to prostrate on the ground. If he dismounted and did not prostrate, then rode and gestured, it is permissible, considering the time of recitation, contrary to Zufar, who says: When he dismounted, performing it on the ground became obligatory, so it becomes as if he recited it on the ground. Likewise, if he recited it at sunrise and did not prostrate, then we allowed its prostration at the time of zenith or sunset, contrary to Zufar—because he performed it as it was required, incomplete. According to him, it is as if he caught a complete time in which it was required in a perfect state, like yesterday's Asr. We say: Yesterday's Asr is added to each time, so they differ. Thus in al-Burhan. He narrated it in al-Tatarkhaniyya from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, then said: It is mentioned in other places from Abu Yusuf that it is not permissible, and that was the fatwa of Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl. It is recommended that the listener not raise his head from it, i.e., the prostration, before the reciter raises his head, because he is the basis of its obligation, so he is followed in performing it, and it is not real following. Hence the reciter is not commanded to go forward, nor are the listeners commanded to line up; they prostrate with him wherever and however they are. Shaykh al-Islam said: In nawazil, he goes forward and people line up behind him, as in al-Diraya. Al-Kamal said: This is not real following but form, so it is recommended that they not precede him in placing and raising. If it were real, it would be obligatory, and their prostration would be invalidated by the invalidity of the reciter's prostration due to some cause, and both are negated. End. Abu Bakr mentioned that a woman is suitable as an imam for a man in it, as in al-Diraya. Conditions for its validity are that the conditions of prayer be present in the one prostrating: purity from hadath and khabath, covering the awrah, facing the qibla, striving for it when in doubt, and intention, except takbirat al-ihram; it is not required because the takbir is a sunnah, as we will mention. In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Hujja: It is recommended for the reciter or listener, if he cannot prostrate, to say: 'We hear and obey, Your forgiveness, our Lord, and to You is the return.' Notice: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: Our shaykhs, may Allah have mercy on them, said: The way in our time if the imam recites it in Friday prayer is not to prostrate for it because of the length of the rows and the large number of people; when the muballigh says takbir for it, the people think it is the takbir for bowing, so they bow, and there is obvious fitna in that. Likewise in Eid prayer. Shams al-A'imma said: I asked the qadi, may Allah have mercy on him: Is it disliked for the imam to recite a sura containing a prostration on Friday just as it is disliked in Zuhr prayer? He said: There is no narration about it, but it should be disliked. In Sharh al-Tahawi: The imam should not recite a verse of prostration in Friday and Eid prayers when the people are not all hearing the recitation. End. If the khatib recites on the minbar, he may prostrate on the minbar or descend and prostrate. In Sharh al-Tahawi: Those who hear him prostrate with him, and it is not obligatory on those who do not hear, unlike in prayer. End. As for reciting 'Alif Lam Meem Sajdah' and 'Hal ata' and prostrating in Fajr of Friday, it is sometimes recommended to do it, and one should not persist in abandoning it, just as one should not persist in doing it. Another notice about what invalidates this prostration and what does not: If one speaks, laughs loudly, or breaks wudu intentionally or mistakenly, he must repeat it, considering it like prayer. No wudu is required for loud laughter in it by consensus, as we presented in tahara. If something that breaks wudu overtakes him, he performs wudu and repeats it. Shaykh al-Islam said: This answer is correct according to Muhammad's saying, for according to him, the completion of the prostration is by placing the forehead and raising it. So if he breaks wudu, laughs, or speaks during it, he repeats it. According to Abu Yusuf, the completion of the prostration is by placing the forehead only. Once the forehead is placed, the prostration is complete, even if brief. So how can one conceive of loud laughter, speech, or the like during it? If he laughs after that, he has laughed after completion, so no repetition is required. Thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. Al-Kamal said: This is good. End. It may be said: Raising, even if not part of its completion, as long as he is in the state of placing, he is in it, like one who lengthens recitation and standing in obligatory prayer. If he laughs loudly or does something contrary, it occurs in the essence of prostration, invalidating the part that meets it, so the whole is invalidated by its invalidation. So reflect. (Its description) i.e., prostration of recitation: that one prostrates a single prostration between two takbirs: a takbir for placing and a takbir for raising. He said in al-Bahr: In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: When he wants to prostrate, he intends it in his heart and says with his tongue: 'I prostrate to Allah, prostration of Allah, Allahu Akbar,' just as he says: 'I pray to Allah Almighty such a prayer.' We already mentioned that verbalizing the intention is a method recommended by the shaykhs, not transmitted from the Prophet, peace be upon him, nor from his successors. End. In al-Hidaya: Whoever wants to prostrate says takbir without raising his hands, prostrates, then says takbir and raises his head, considering the prostration of prayer. This is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud. End. Ibn Abi Shayba narrated it from Ibrahim, al-Hasan, Abu Qilaba, and Ibn Sirin, as in the handwriting of the shaykh of our shaykhs. End. In al-Dhakhira: It is the chosen view. It is said: The initial takbir is without dispute, and there is dispute about the final takbir: Abu Yusuf says to say it, Muhammad does not. In al-Muhit: Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he does not say takbir while descending. In al-Hujja: Some shaykhs said: If he prostrated without saying takbir, he fulfills the obligation. This is known but not acted upon because it contradicts the Sunnah. End. Shaykh said: End.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rulings of sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) from a Hanafi perspective. The author begins by stating the recommended (mandub) acts: the reciter should stand if he was sitting, then prostrate (the prostration itself is also recommended). There is a proof from the action of Aisha (radiyallahu anha) as narrated by Umm Salama al-Azdiyya. The commentator expands on the ruling for a rider: it is better to dismount, but if he dismounts and does not prostrate then rides and gestures, it is permissible (contrary to Zufar who held it becomes obligatory upon dismounting). Similarly, delaying the prostration from sunrise to a later time is permissible according to the Hanafis but Zufar disagrees. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree on the permissibility, but in some places Abu Yusuf is reported to say it is not permissible; the fatwa was on the latter by Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl. Next, the listener should not raise his head before the reciter, as the reciter is the basis. This is not real following (iqtida'), so the reciter does not step forward and listeners do not line up; they prostrate wherever they are. However, in nawazil (calamities), the reciter may step forward and people line up behind him, but it is only formal, not real iqtida'. A woman can act as imam for a man in this prostration. The conditions for validity are the same as for prayer: purity from hadath and khabath, covering the awrah, facing qibla, effort in direction when unsure, and intention—except takbirat al-ihram, which is not required because the takbir for prostration is sunnah. If one cannot prostrate, he may say a supplication. Special rulings for Friday and Eid: due to large crowds, the imam should avoid reciting a verse of prostration to prevent confusion (people think the takbir is for bowing). The khatib on the minbar may prostrate on the minbar or descend. Regarding what invalidates sajdat al-tilawah: speaking, laughing loudly, or hadath require repetition. There is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: for Abu Yusuf, the prostration is complete once the forehead is placed (so subsequent actions do not invalidate), while for Muhammad, it is complete only with both placing and raising. The text notes that the former view is considered good by al-Kamal. Finally, the method: one prostration between two takbirs (one for descent, one for raising). There are variations regarding the second takbir: Abu Yusuf affirms it, Muhammad does not; Abu Hanifa is reported not to say takbir while descending. The chosen view is to say both takbirs, as it follows the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and is more consistent with the sunnah.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Quran. In Hanafi fiqh, it is a stressed sunnah.
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) that initiates the prayer; not required for sajdat al-tilawah according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the validity of sajdat al-tilawah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Purity from hadath
B) Facing the qibla
C) Takbirat al-ihram
D) Intention

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawah is a recommended act of worship with the same conditions as prayer but without the opening takbir.
