Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Timing and Delay of Sajdat al-Tilawah: The Zufar Dispute
Segment on delaying prostration and the Zufar dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on delaying sajdat al-tilawah and evaluate Zufar's counter-argument using the analogy with 'Asr prayer.

Core Idea
Delaying sajdat al-tilawah is permissible in the Hanafi school, contrary to Zufar who requires immediate performance upon recitation.

This passage addresses scenarios where a rider dismounts or recites at sunrise but delays the prostration. The majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit delay, while Zufar argues it becomes obligatory immediately upon dismounting or upon the recitation time passing. The author counters Zufar's analogy to 'Asr prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the part about the rider: he dismounts, does not prostrate, then mounts and gestures. The author says it is permissible (jaza). Note that this is based on considering the time of recitation.
Gesturing refers to a slight movement indicating prostration if on a mount.
2
Locate Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that once the rider dismounts, performing the prostration on the ground becomes obligatory (wajib), just as if he had recited on the ground.
3
Analyze the analogy with 'Asr prayer
Zufar compares delaying prostration to performing 'Asr prayer after its time; that would be incomplete (naqisa). The Hanafi response is that 'Asr belongs to a complete time (allotted time for prayer), whereas sajdat al-tilawah does not have a designated time.
The key difference: 'Asr is attached to a specific time window; sajdat al-tilawah is linked to the act of recitation but not to a time limit.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi variation
The text mentions that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree on permissibility, but there is a conflicting report from Abu Yusuf that it is not permissible, and that was the fatwa of Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl.
This shows that even within the Hanafi school, there is a range of opinions.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
Zufar's view would require immediate prostration upon recitation (or after dismounting). The Hanafi majority view allows flexibility: one can prostrate later, even at a different time of day.
This facilitates performance for those who are traveling or unable to prostrate immediately.

ببطلانه، فليتأمل. ( وكيفيتها ) أي : سجدة التلاوة أن يسجد سجدة واحدة) كائنة (بين تكبيرتين) تكبيرة للوضع وتكبيرة للرفع، قال في ( البحر » : وفي « السراج الوهاج» : إذا أراد السجود ينويها بقلبه ويقول بلسانه أسجد لله سجدة الله أكبر، كما يقول: أصلي الله تعالى صلاة كذا، وقدمنا أن النطق بالنية طريقة استحبها المشايخ، وليست منقولة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا عــن خلفائه انتهى. وفي ( الهداية » : ومن أراد السجود كبر ولم يرفع يديه وسجد، ثم كبر ورفع رأسه، اعتباراً بسجدة الصلاة، وهو المروي عن ابن مسعود .انتهى. ورواه ابن أبي شيبة، عن إبراهيم، والحسن، وأبي قلابة، وابن سيرين كذا بخط شيخ مشايخنا انتهى. وفي ( الذخيرة» : هو المختار، وقيل: يكبر في الابتداء بلا خلاف، وفي الانتهاء خلاف، يكبر عند أبي يوسف لا عند محمد، وفي المحيط » : روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه لا يكبر مع الانحطاط ، وفي ( الحجة » : قال بعض المشايخ: لو سجد ولم يكبر يخرج عن العهدة، وهذا يعلم ولا يعمل به لما فيه من مخالفة السنة، انتهى. وقال شيخ انتهى.
(1) فعن أم سلمة الأزدية قالت: «رأيت عائشة تقرأ في المصحف فإذا مرت بسجدة قامت فسجدت» أخرجه البيهقي في السنن الكبرى (326/2).
Standing is recommended, then prostration for it. The listener should not raise his head from it before the reciter. The reciter is not commanded to go forward, nor are the listeners commanded to line up; they prostrate as they are. Conditions for its validity are the conditions of prayer, except the takbirat al-ihram. Aisha (1). Out of compassion for them, recite loudly to urge them to obedience. Standing is recommended for one who recited while sitting, then prostration for it; that is narrated and because the falling down praised for those [people] is more complete in it. Likewise, if one was riding and recited it, it is better for him to dismount to prostrate on the ground. If he dismounted and did not prostrate, then rode and gestured, it is permissible, considering the time of recitation, contrary to Zufar, who says: When he dismounted, performing it on the ground became obligatory, so it becomes as if he recited it on the ground. Likewise, if he recited it at sunrise and did not prostrate, then we allowed its prostration at the time of zenith or sunset, contrary to Zufar—because he performed it as it was required, incomplete. According to him, it is as if he caught a complete time in which it was required in a perfect state, like yesterday's Asr. We say: Yesterday's Asr is added to each time, so they differ. Thus in al-Burhan. He narrated it in al-Tatarkhaniyya from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, then said: It is mentioned in other places from Abu Yusuf that it is not permissible, and that was the fatwa of Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl. It is recommended that the listener not raise his head from it, i.e., the prostration, before the reciter raises his head, because he is the basis of its obligation, so he is followed in performing it, and it is not real following. Hence the reciter is not commanded to go forward, nor are the listeners commanded to line up; they prostrate with him wherever and however they are. Shaykh al-Islam said: In nawazil, he goes forward and people line up behind him, as in al-Diraya. Al-Kamal said: This is not real following but form, so it is recommended that they not precede him in placing and raising. If it were real, it would be obligatory, and their prostration would be invalidated by the invalidity of the reciter's prostration due to some cause, and both are negated. End. Abu Bakr mentioned that a woman is suitable as an imam for a man in it, as in al-Diraya. Conditions for its validity are that the conditions of prayer be present in the one prostrating: purity from hadath and khabath, covering the awrah, facing the qibla, striving for it when in doubt, and intention, except takbirat al-ihram; it is not required because the takbir is a sunnah, as we will mention. In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Hujja: It is recommended for the reciter or listener, if he cannot prostrate, to say: 'We hear and obey, Your forgiveness, our Lord, and to You is the return.' Notice: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: Our shaykhs, may Allah have mercy on them, said: The way in our time if the imam recites it in Friday prayer is not to prostrate for it because of the length of the rows and the large number of people; when the muballigh says takbir for it, the people think it is the takbir for bowing, so they bow, and there is obvious fitna in that. Likewise in Eid prayer. Shams al-A'imma said: I asked the qadi, may Allah have mercy on him: Is it disliked for the imam to recite a sura containing a prostration on Friday just as it is disliked in Zuhr prayer? He said: There is no narration about it, but it should be disliked. In Sharh al-Tahawi: The imam should not recite a verse of prostration in Friday and Eid prayers when the people are not all hearing the recitation. End. If the khatib recites on the minbar, he may prostrate on the minbar or descend and prostrate. In Sharh al-Tahawi: Those who hear him prostrate with him, and it is not obligatory on those who do not hear, unlike in prayer. End. As for reciting 'Alif Lam Meem Sajdah' and 'Hal ata' and prostrating in Fajr of Friday, it is sometimes recommended to do it, and one should not persist in abandoning it, just as one should not persist in doing it. Another notice about what invalidates this prostration and what does not: If one speaks, laughs loudly, or breaks wudu intentionally or mistakenly, he must repeat it, considering it like prayer. No wudu is required for loud laughter in it by consensus, as we presented in tahara. If something that breaks wudu overtakes him, he performs wudu and repeats it. Shaykh al-Islam said: This answer is correct according to Muhammad's saying, for according to him, the completion of the prostration is by placing the forehead and raising it. So if he breaks wudu, laughs, or speaks during it, he repeats it. According to Abu Yusuf, the completion of the prostration is by placing the forehead only. Once the forehead is placed, the prostration is complete, even if brief. So how can one conceive of loud laughter, speech, or the like during it? If he laughs after that, he has laughed after completion, so no repetition is required. Thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. Al-Kamal said: This is good. End. It may be said: Raising, even if not part of its completion, as long as he is in the state of placing, he is in it, like one who lengthens recitation and standing in obligatory prayer. If he laughs loudly or does something contrary, it occurs in the essence of prostration, invalidating the part that meets it, so the whole is invalidated by its invalidation. So reflect. (Its description) i.e., prostration of recitation: that one prostrates a single prostration between two takbirs: a takbir for placing and a takbir for raising. He said in al-Bahr: In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: When he wants to prostrate, he intends it in his heart and says with his tongue: 'I prostrate to Allah, prostration of Allah, Allahu Akbar,' just as he says: 'I pray to Allah Almighty such a prayer.' We already mentioned that verbalizing the intention is a method recommended by the shaykhs, not transmitted from the Prophet, peace be upon him, nor from his successors. End. In al-Hidaya: Whoever wants to prostrate says takbir without raising his hands, prostrates, then says takbir and raises his head, considering the prostration of prayer. This is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud. End. Ibn Abi Shayba narrated it from Ibrahim, al-Hasan, Abu Qilaba, and Ibn Sirin, as in the handwriting of the shaykh of our shaykhs. End. In al-Dhakhira: It is the chosen view. It is said: The initial takbir is without dispute, and there is dispute about the final takbir: Abu Yusuf says to say it, Muhammad does not. In al-Muhit: Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he does not say takbir while descending. In al-Hujja: Some shaykhs said: If he prostrated without saying takbir, he fulfills the obligation. This is known but not acted upon because it contradicts the Sunnah. End. Shaykh said: End.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rulings of sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) from a Hanafi perspective. The author begins by stating the recommended (mandub) acts: the reciter should stand if he was sitting, then prostrate (the prostration itself is also recommended). There is a proof from the action of Aisha (radiyallahu anha) as narrated by Umm Salama al-Azdiyya. The commentator expands on the ruling for a rider: it is better to dismount, but if he dismounts and does not prostrate then rides and gestures, it is permissible (contrary to Zufar who held it becomes obligatory upon dismounting). Similarly, delaying the prostration from sunrise to a later time is permissible according to the Hanafis but Zufar disagrees. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree on the permissibility, but in some places Abu Yusuf is reported to say it is not permissible; the fatwa was on the latter by Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl. Next, the listener should not raise his head before the reciter, as the reciter is the basis. This is not real following (iqtida'), so the reciter does not step forward and listeners do not line up; they prostrate wherever they are. However, in nawazil (calamities), the reciter may step forward and people line up behind him, but it is only formal, not real iqtida'. A woman can act as imam for a man in this prostration. The conditions for validity are the same as for prayer: purity from hadath and khabath, covering the awrah, facing qibla, effort in direction when unsure, and intention—except takbirat al-ihram, which is not required because the takbir for prostration is sunnah. If one cannot prostrate, he may say a supplication. Special rulings for Friday and Eid: due to large crowds, the imam should avoid reciting a verse of prostration to prevent confusion (people think the takbir is for bowing). The khatib on the minbar may prostrate on the minbar or descend. Regarding what invalidates sajdat al-tilawah: speaking, laughing loudly, or hadath require repetition. There is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: for Abu Yusuf, the prostration is complete once the forehead is placed (so subsequent actions do not invalidate), while for Muhammad, it is complete only with both placing and raising. The text notes that the former view is considered good by al-Kamal. Finally, the method: one prostration between two takbirs (one for descent, one for raising). There are variations regarding the second takbir: Abu Yusuf affirms it, Muhammad does not; Abu Hanifa is reported not to say takbir while descending. The chosen view is to say both takbirs, as it follows the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and is more consistent with the sunnah.

Key Terms
زفر (Zufar): Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a prominent Hanafi jurist known for divergent opinions on various fiqh issues.
الوقت الكامل (al-waqt al-kāmil): Complete time: a designated period during which an act of worship must be performed in its optimal manner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (majority view), what is the ruling on delaying sajdat al-tilawah from sunrise to noon?
A) Permissible
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Impermissible (haram)
D) Obligatory to repeat

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits delaying sajdat al-tilawah, distinguishing it from obligatory prayers which have fixed times.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Method, Invalidators, and Intra-Hanafi Differences in Sajdat al-Tilawah
Segment on method, invalidators, and completion dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the recommended method of sajdat al-tilawah, identify what invalidates it, and differentiate between the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on its completion.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah consists of one prostration between two takbirs; its completion is disputed (placing vs. placing+raising), affecting when invalidators take effect.

This final segment details the physical method (kayfiyya) and discusses what breaks the prostration. It contains a notable intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf holds that the prostration is complete upon placing the forehead on the ground, while Muhammad requires both placing and raising. This difference affects whether later actions (like laughing) invalidate the act.

Guided Path
1
Learn the standard method
The text describes the method as one prostration between two takbirs: one for descending, one for raising. This is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and considered the chosen view.
Some scholars say the initial takbir is agreed upon, but the final takbir is disputed (Abu Yusuf says yes, Muhammad says no).
2
Identify what invalidates the prostration
The text lists: speaking, loud laughter (qahqaha), and hadath (breaking wudu) intentionally or mistakenly. If these occur, the prostration must be repeated.
Consensus: no wudu required for laughter, as per tahara rulings.
3
Understand the completion dispute
Muhammad: completion requires placing the forehead and raising it. So if any invalidator occurs before raising, the prostration is incomplete and must be repeated. Abu Yusuf: completion is achieved by placing the forehead only; raising is not part of the prostration's essence. Thus, after placing, any subsequent action does not affect the already completed prostration.
Al-Kamal preferred Abu Yusuf's view, calling it 'good' (hasan).
4
Analyze a counter-argument
Some later scholars argue that even if raising is not part of completion, as long as the person is still in the state of prostration (i.e., forehead on ground before raising), any invalidator would affect the ongoing act, similar to lengthening recitation in prayer.
The text says 'reflect upon this' (falyata'ammal), indicating it is a point of deliberation.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, one should avoid all invalidators during the entire act (from takbir to raising). If an invalidator occurs before raising, one should repeat the prostration out of caution, especially according to Muhammad's view which is more cautious.
The mufta bihi may be the cautious approach.

( وكيفيتها ) أي : سجدة التلاوة أن يسجد سجدة واحدة) كائنة (بين تكبيرتين) تكبيرة للوضع وتكبيرة للرفع، قال في ( البحر » : وفي « السراج الوهاج» : إذا أراد السجود ينويها بقلبه ويقول بلسانه أسجد لله سجدة الله أكبر، كما يقول: أصلي الله تعالى صلاة كذا، وقدمنا أن النطق بالنية طريقة استحبها المشايخ، وليست منقولة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا عــن خلفائه انتهى. وفي ( الهداية » : ومن أراد السجود كبر ولم يرفع يديه وسجد، ثم كبر ورفع رأسه، اعتباراً بسجدة الصلاة، وهو المروي عن ابن مسعود .انتهى. ورواه ابن أبي شيبة، عن إبراهيم، والحسن، وأبي قلابة، وابن سيرين كذا بخط شيخ مشايخنا انتهى. وفي ( الذخيرة» : هو المختار، وقيل: يكبر في الابتداء بلا خلاف، وفي الانتهاء خلاف، يكبر عند أبي يوسف لا عند محمد، وفي المحيط » : روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه لا يكبر مع الانحطاط ، وفي ( الحجة » : قال بعض المشايخ: لو سجد ولم يكبر يخرج عن العهدة، وهذا يعلم ولا يعمل به لما فيه من مخالفة السنة، انتهى. وقال شيخ انتهى.
(1) فعن أم سلمة الأزدية قالت: «رأيت عائشة تقرأ في المصحف فإذا مرت بسجدة قامت فسجدت» أخرجه البيهقي في السنن الكبرى (326/2).
Standing is recommended, then prostration for it. The listener should not raise his head from it before the reciter. The reciter is not commanded to go forward, nor are the listeners commanded to line up; they prostrate as they are. Conditions for its validity are the conditions of prayer, except the takbirat al-ihram. Aisha (1). Out of compassion for them, recite loudly to urge them to obedience. Standing is recommended for one who recited while sitting, then prostration for it; that is narrated and because the falling down praised for those [people] is more complete in it. Likewise, if one was riding and recited it, it is better for him to dismount to prostrate on the ground. If he dismounted and did not prostrate, then rode and gestured, it is permissible, considering the time of recitation, contrary to Zufar, who says: When he dismounted, performing it on the ground became obligatory, so it becomes as if he recited it on the ground. Likewise, if he recited it at sunrise and did not prostrate, then we allowed its prostration at the time of zenith or sunset, contrary to Zufar—because he performed it as it was required, incomplete. According to him, it is as if he caught a complete time in which it was required in a perfect state, like yesterday's Asr. We say: Yesterday's Asr is added to each time, so they differ. Thus in al-Burhan. He narrated it in al-Tatarkhaniyya from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, then said: It is mentioned in other places from Abu Yusuf that it is not permissible, and that was the fatwa of Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl. It is recommended that the listener not raise his head from it, i.e., the prostration, before the reciter raises his head, because he is the basis of its obligation, so he is followed in performing it, and it is not real following. Hence the reciter is not commanded to go forward, nor are the listeners commanded to line up; they prostrate with him wherever and however they are. Shaykh al-Islam said: In nawazil, he goes forward and people line up behind him, as in al-Diraya. Al-Kamal said: This is not real following but form, so it is recommended that they not precede him in placing and raising. If it were real, it would be obligatory, and their prostration would be invalidated by the invalidity of the reciter's prostration due to some cause, and both are negated. End. Abu Bakr mentioned that a woman is suitable as an imam for a man in it, as in al-Diraya. Conditions for its validity are that the conditions of prayer be present in the one prostrating: purity from hadath and khabath, covering the awrah, facing the qibla, striving for it when in doubt, and intention, except takbirat al-ihram; it is not required because the takbir is a sunnah, as we will mention. In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Hujja: It is recommended for the reciter or listener, if he cannot prostrate, to say: 'We hear and obey, Your forgiveness, our Lord, and to You is the return.' Notice: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: Our shaykhs, may Allah have mercy on them, said: The way in our time if the imam recites it in Friday prayer is not to prostrate for it because of the length of the rows and the large number of people; when the muballigh says takbir for it, the people think it is the takbir for bowing, so they bow, and there is obvious fitna in that. Likewise in Eid prayer. Shams al-A'imma said: I asked the qadi, may Allah have mercy on him: Is it disliked for the imam to recite a sura containing a prostration on Friday just as it is disliked in Zuhr prayer? He said: There is no narration about it, but it should be disliked. In Sharh al-Tahawi: The imam should not recite a verse of prostration in Friday and Eid prayers when the people are not all hearing the recitation. End. If the khatib recites on the minbar, he may prostrate on the minbar or descend and prostrate. In Sharh al-Tahawi: Those who hear him prostrate with him, and it is not obligatory on those who do not hear, unlike in prayer. End. As for reciting 'Alif Lam Meem Sajdah' and 'Hal ata' and prostrating in Fajr of Friday, it is sometimes recommended to do it, and one should not persist in abandoning it, just as one should not persist in doing it. Another notice about what invalidates this prostration and what does not: If one speaks, laughs loudly, or breaks wudu intentionally or mistakenly, he must repeat it, considering it like prayer. No wudu is required for loud laughter in it by consensus, as we presented in tahara. If something that breaks wudu overtakes him, he performs wudu and repeats it. Shaykh al-Islam said: This answer is correct according to Muhammad's saying, for according to him, the completion of the prostration is by placing the forehead and raising it. So if he breaks wudu, laughs, or speaks during it, he repeats it. According to Abu Yusuf, the completion of the prostration is by placing the forehead only. Once the forehead is placed, the prostration is complete, even if brief. So how can one conceive of loud laughter, speech, or the like during it? If he laughs after that, he has laughed after completion, so no repetition is required. Thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. Al-Kamal said: This is good. End. It may be said: Raising, even if not part of its completion, as long as he is in the state of placing, he is in it, like one who lengthens recitation and standing in obligatory prayer. If he laughs loudly or does something contrary, it occurs in the essence of prostration, invalidating the part that meets it, so the whole is invalidated by its invalidation. So reflect. (Its description) i.e., prostration of recitation: that one prostrates a single prostration between two takbirs: a takbir for placing and a takbir for raising. He said in al-Bahr: In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: When he wants to prostrate, he intends it in his heart and says with his tongue: 'I prostrate to Allah, prostration of Allah, Allahu Akbar,' just as he says: 'I pray to Allah Almighty such a prayer.' We already mentioned that verbalizing the intention is a method recommended by the shaykhs, not transmitted from the Prophet, peace be upon him, nor from his successors. End. In al-Hidaya: Whoever wants to prostrate says takbir without raising his hands, prostrates, then says takbir and raises his head, considering the prostration of prayer. This is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud. End. Ibn Abi Shayba narrated it from Ibrahim, al-Hasan, Abu Qilaba, and Ibn Sirin, as in the handwriting of the shaykh of our shaykhs. End. In al-Dhakhira: It is the chosen view. It is said: The initial takbir is without dispute, and there is dispute about the final takbir: Abu Yusuf says to say it, Muhammad does not. In al-Muhit: Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he does not say takbir while descending. In al-Hujja: Some shaykhs said: If he prostrated without saying takbir, he fulfills the obligation. This is known but not acted upon because it contradicts the Sunnah. End. Shaykh said: End.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rulings of sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) from a Hanafi perspective. The author begins by stating the recommended (mandub) acts: the reciter should stand if he was sitting, then prostrate (the prostration itself is also recommended). There is a proof from the action of Aisha (radiyallahu anha) as narrated by Umm Salama al-Azdiyya. The commentator expands on the ruling for a rider: it is better to dismount, but if he dismounts and does not prostrate then rides and gestures, it is permissible (contrary to Zufar who held it becomes obligatory upon dismounting). Similarly, delaying the prostration from sunrise to a later time is permissible according to the Hanafis but Zufar disagrees. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree on the permissibility, but in some places Abu Yusuf is reported to say it is not permissible; the fatwa was on the latter by Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl. Next, the listener should not raise his head before the reciter, as the reciter is the basis. This is not real following (iqtida'), so the reciter does not step forward and listeners do not line up; they prostrate wherever they are. However, in nawazil (calamities), the reciter may step forward and people line up behind him, but it is only formal, not real iqtida'. A woman can act as imam for a man in this prostration. The conditions for validity are the same as for prayer: purity from hadath and khabath, covering the awrah, facing qibla, effort in direction when unsure, and intention—except takbirat al-ihram, which is not required because the takbir for prostration is sunnah. If one cannot prostrate, he may say a supplication. Special rulings for Friday and Eid: due to large crowds, the imam should avoid reciting a verse of prostration to prevent confusion (people think the takbir is for bowing). The khatib on the minbar may prostrate on the minbar or descend. Regarding what invalidates sajdat al-tilawah: speaking, laughing loudly, or hadath require repetition. There is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: for Abu Yusuf, the prostration is complete once the forehead is placed (so subsequent actions do not invalidate), while for Muhammad, it is complete only with both placing and raising. The text notes that the former view is considered good by al-Kamal. Finally, the method: one prostration between two takbirs (one for descent, one for raising). There are variations regarding the second takbir: Abu Yusuf affirms it, Muhammad does not; Abu Hanifa is reported not to say takbir while descending. The chosen view is to say both takbirs, as it follows the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and is more consistent with the sunnah.

Key Terms
تمام السجدة (tamām al-sajdah): The completion of the prostration; whether it requires only placing the forehead (Abu Yusuf) or both placing and raising (Muhammad).
مبطلات سجدة التلاوة (mubtilāt sajdat al-tilāwah): Actions that invalidate the prostration of recitation: speaking, loud laughter, and breaking wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad (Sahib), what is required for the completion (tamam) of sajdat al-tilawah?
A) Only placing the forehead
B) Placing the forehead and raising the head
C) Saying both takbirs
D) Having intention and facing qibla

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of sajdat al-tilawah is one prostration between two takbirs, but its completion is debated, affecting when invalidators nullify it.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Manner of Sajdah al-Tilawah
Ruling with proof on the manner and legal status of the prostration of recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the manner of sajdah al-tilawah and state the status of its takbirs according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilawah is a single prostration between two sunnah takbirs, without raising hands or taslim.

The prostration of recitation (sajdah al-tilawah) is an important act when reciting or hearing specific Quranic verses. This lesson details its prescribed manner according to the Hanafi school, focusing on the number of takbirs, hand placement, and the absence of tashahhud and taslim. Understanding these details ensures the prostration is performed correctly, avoiding common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic form of sajdah al-tilawah
The passage states it is a single prostration between two takbirs: one for going down (takbirat al-wad') and one for rising (takbirat al-raf').
Note the contrast with the prostration in prayer, which has multiple prostrations.
2
Analyze the sources cited
The author quotes from al-Hidayah, al-Bahr, al-Dhakhirah, and others to establish the practice. Recognize that these are authoritative Hanafi references.
The chain of narration strengthens the reliability of the ruling.
3
Determine the ruling on the takbirs
The passage concludes that both takbirs are sunnah (not wajib), citing the hadith of Abu Dawood and the Hanafi principle that the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates recommendation.
This is the mufta bihi position, though there is intra-Hanafi disagreement.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that the second takbir is performed, while Muhammad does not. Abu Hanifa reportedly did not say takbir when descending. The chosen position (al-mukhtar) is that both are sunnah.
The disagreement does not affect the basic validity of the prostration.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
When performing sajdah al-tilawah, one should say 'Allahu Akbar' while going down and again while rising, but without raising the hands. The prostration is valid even if the takbirs are omitted, though it is better to include them.
This distinguishes it from prayer, where missing a sunnah may require prostration of forgetfulness.

وكيفيتها أن يسجد سجدة واحدة بين تكبيرتين) كائنة (بين تكبيرتين) تكبيرة للوضع وتكبيرة للرفع، قال في ( البحر ) : وفي ( السراج الوهاج ) : إذا أراد السجود ينويها بقلبه ويقول بلسانه أسجد لله سجدة الله أكبر، كما يقول: أصلي الله تعالى صلاة كذا، وقدمنا أن النطق بالنية طريقة استحبها المشايخ، وليست منقولة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا عن خلفائه انتهى. وفي ( الهداية ) : ومن أراد السجود كبر ولم يرفع يديه وسجد، ثم كبر ورفع رأسه، اعتباراً بسجدة الصلاة، وهو المروي عن ابن مسعود .انتهى. ورواه ابن أبي شيبة، عن إبراهيم، والحسن، وأبي قلابة، وابن سيرين كذا بخط شيخ مشايخنا انتهى. وفي ( الذخيرة ) : هو المختار، وقيل: يكبر في الابتداء بلا خلاف، وفي الانتهاء خلاف، يكبر عند أبي يوسف لا عند محمد، وفي المحيط : روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه لا يكبر مع الانحطاط ، وفي ( الحجة ) : قال بعض المشايخ: لو سجد ولم يكبر يخرج عن العهدة، وهذا يعلم ولا يعمل به لما فيه من مخالفة السنة، انتهى. وقال شيخ الإسلام: روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة: الركن في السجدة وضع الجبهة والتكبير عند الرفع، حتى لو تركه يعيد انتهى. وقلت: وهذا يعكر على ما قيل: إن السجدة تتم بمجرد الوضع فتبطل بالمنافي بعده انتهى. وفي ( مبسوط) فخر الإسلام التكبير ليس بواجب، كما في الصلاة، فلذا بين صفة التكبيرين، بقوله (هما سنتان) أي: كل منهما سنة كما صححه في ( البدائع )؛ لحديث أبي داود في السنن من فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام، كذلك ( بلا رفع يد ) لأن الرفع للتحريمة ولا تحريم هنا، والتكبير للانحطاط، كما في سجود الصلاة، ولا تشهد لعدم وروده (ولا تسليم لأنه يستدعي سبق التحريمة وهي منعدمة.
Its manner is that he prostrates a single prostration between two takbirs: a takbir for placing and a takbir for raising. In (al-Bahr) and (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj): When he intends to prostrate, he intends in his heart and says with his tongue, 'I prostrate to Allah as a prostration, Allahu Akbar,' just as he says, 'I pray to Allah the Exalted such a prayer.' We have mentioned that verbalizing the intention is a method recommended by the scholars, but it is not transmitted from the Prophet peace be upon him nor from his caliphs. In (al-Hidayah): Whoever intends to prostrate says Allahu Akbar and does not raise his hands, prostrates, then says Allahu Akbar and raises his head, analogizing to the prostration of prayer, and this is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud. Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated it from Ibrahim, al-Hasan, Abu Qilabah, and Ibn Sirin . In (al-Dhakhirah): It is the chosen view. It is said: The takbir at the beginning is without disagreement, and at the end there is disagreement: Abu Yusuf says takbir, Muhammad does not. In (al-Muhit): al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he does not say takbir with descending. In (al-Hujjah): Some scholars said: If he prostrates without takbir, he fulfills the duty, but this is known and not acted upon because it contradicts the sunnah. Shaykh al-Islam said: al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: The pillar in prostration is placing the forehead and the takbir at rising, so if he leaves it, he repeats. I say: This contradicts what was said: The prostration is completed merely by placing, so it is invalidated by a nullifier thereafter. In (Mabsut) Fakhr al-Islam: The takbir is not obligatory, as in prayer, so he described the nature of the two takbirs, saying (they are both sunnah) meaning each is sunnah as confirmed in (al-Bada'i') due to the hadith of Abu Dawood in al-Sunan from his action (peace be upon him). Likewise, (without raising hands) because raising is for the opening takbir and there is no opening takbir here, and the takbir is for descending as in the prostration of prayer. No tashahhud because it is not reported, and no taslim because it requires a preceding opening takbir which is absent.
Source pages p. 514

Commentary
This passage explains the manner (kayfiyyah) of performing the prostration of recitation (sajdah al-tilawah). The author states that it consists of a single prostration between two takbirs: one for going down and one for rising. Various Hanafi sources are cited to elaborate: some recommend verbalizing the intention (though it is not from the Prophet), the takbirs are performed without raising hands, and the prostration is analogous to that in prayer. The text then discusses the status of the takbirs: although some early authorities considered them obligatory, the relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) is that they are sunnah, not wajib, as confirmed by the hadith in Abu Dawood. The passage also clarifies that hands are not raised because the raising of hands is associated with the opening takbir (tahrimah), which is absent here. There is no tashahhud because it is not reported, and no taslim because taslim requires a preceding tahrimah. The commentary thus establishes the Hanafi ruling on the form of sajdah al-tilawah.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration (ayat sajdah) in the Quran.
تكبيرة (takbirah): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' at specific points during the prostration.
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during the takbir; not done here because there is no tahrimah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the two takbirs in sajdah al-tilawah according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Both are wajib.
B) Both are sunnah.
C) The first is wajib, the second is sunnah.
D) Neither is required.

Key Takeaway
The two takbirs in sajdah al-tilawah are sunnah, not wajib, and hands are not raised.
